**Phase B — §12.3.D run-spine is now a real grid zone (structural over the absolute hack).** The spine was `position:absolute; left: max(0.5rem, calc(50% - 32rem))`, so at very wide viewports it hugged the centred column and left a dead far-left gutter (the §12.15 imbalance). Replaced with the tempdoc's actual three-zone composition (commit `5b8e81f2f`): a four-column grid `[minmax(0,1fr) | 40rem conversation | 15–20rem rail | minmax(0,1fr)]` whose two outer `1fr` tracks are symmetric, so the conversation+rail group is centred BY CONSTRUCTION and the spine is a real `grid-column:1` zone scaling with the viewport (`justify-self:center`, decorative + aria-hidden, non-scrolling). The plan's 3-column sketch would have pushed the group right (a lone `1fr` eats all slack) — the symmetric 4-column form is the correct realization. Verified: FE `tsc` + **2404** unit + the presentation gates (layout-purity, a11y-closure, color-tokens, controls-a11y, theme-token-closure, presentation-purity, observed-state-collapse, adaptive-closure, message-single-model, run-renderers, strip-token-fallbacks) green. (`gen-token-names --check` fails on a **pre-existing main-inherited** drift — `--surface-content-max-width`, added to `tokens.css` by 559 commit `77d32f5f2`, never regenerated into the vocabulary — logged to `observations.md`, not 565's.) **Pixel-level margin tuning at 1440/1920/2560 is the live-iteration step (Phase C).**

**Phase C — the live batch (real-LLM grounded run) — DONE, the §12.16 model-pin fix VALIDATED + the differentiator live-proven with REAL data.** A lease-free stack was stood up from this worktree (head 61703 + Vite 5181 proxying `/api`→61703; Llama pinned via `POST /api/settings/v2 {modelPath}` + `/api/inference/reload` + `/api/ai/runtime/activate {variantId:cuda12}`). **The §12.16 diagnosis is confirmed: with Llama pinned, the agent loop runs end-to-end with NO `LLM_TRANSIENT`** — it called `core_search_index` (6×), multi-iterated, and emitted a grounded `AgentDone` carrying **10 sources + 5 citations**, each a full local passage (`parentDocId`, `chunkIndex`, `path`, `startLine`/`endLine`, `excerpt`). The §12.13/§12.14 blocker is gone. **Honest journey (recorded so the next runner skips it):** the data dir's pre-existing index was schema-stale (hits had empty `fields`/`excerptRegions` → 0 grounding), and an in-place reindex attempt corrupted the keyword searcher; the fix was a **clean-data-dir restart + a fresh ingest** (`tmp/.dev-data-565-clean` via `tmp/launch-head-565-clean.bat`), which built a proper chunk-identity index — confirming §12.14's "use a properly-built index, not a degraded hand-assembled one." **Live-validated in the real browser (screenshots saved), every (d) item:**
- **Grounded agent answer renders inline citations + the persistent sources rail** — a real markdown answer (Head/Worker/Brain) with inline `[n]` superscripts + a "Sources · 10" rail of clickable local-passage cards (`Agent System Architecture · Line 1`, …).
- **The differentiator** — clicking a source card fired `citation-select` → opened `22-agent-system-architecture.md` in the Preview pane with the **cited passage highlighted** at its line. Click → exact local passage, working, with real data.
- **Fix-B per-answer grounding** — a 2nd turn (VRAM/inference) produced an entirely different, topic-appropriate rail (`AI Architecture`, `AI Bridge Deep Dive`, `Module Architecture (ORT)`, `NVIDIA GPU Booster · Line 376`) vs turn-1's architecture sources. Each answer carries its own grounding.
- **§12.3.D three-zone layout (Phase B) — measured + populated.** Computed `grid-template-columns` at 1920px = **`402px 640px 320px 402px`** (symmetric outer tracks → group centred by construction; the §12.15 imbalance gone); live it rendered as left status-spine · conversation · sources rail.
- **Every mode through the same authorities** — switching to Documents/RAG, the answer rendered via `jf-streaming-text-block` with inline `[n]` superscripts + a scored citations list + the **§12.3.E source-chip row** (numbered chips) + a "Sources" disclosure (DOM census: 2 `jf-markdown-block` agent answers + 1 `jf-streaming-text-block` RAG answer + 8 `.cite-ref` + 2 source panes — one shared render path).
- **§3.D risk-graded approval — live.** The agent proposed a medium-risk `core_ingest_files` write → the type-to-confirm approval modal rendered (and I Denied it; the run summarised "2 steps · 1 denied" with a red spine node). The §12.3.F status-coloured spine + the run-collapse summary both render live.
- **Narrow-viewport fallback** — `resize_window` could not drop `innerWidth` below the 64rem breakpoint (the §12.12 limitation persists), so this stays deterministic-CSS-verified in source (base = 1-col, rail+spine `display:none`), not exercised live.

**Phase D — measured + independent review.** (1) **Measured a11y:** a fresh live axe injection was blocked (Vite doesn't serve the dev-only `axe-core`); the §12.15 measured axe audit (25 passes, 1 PRE-EXISTING accent-contrast violation) remains valid because Phase B is CSS-grid-only (no DOM/semantic change, axe-neutral), cross-checked by the passing `check-a11y-closure` / `check-controls-a11y` / `check-color-tokens` gates on the change. (2) **Independence:** an independent reviewer (≠ committer) gave **both Phase A and Phase B a SOUND verdict, no blocking defects** — confirming the ArchUnit invariant's three exemptions are correct + complete and non-vacuous, and the 4-track symmetric grid centres by construction with the `::before` anchor + narrow fallback intact. Its one actionable finding (the `List`-substring discriminator's future-overload fragility) is folded back as an honest caveat in the test javadoc. **Still owed (honest, per §12.12):** the formal `auditor ≠ committer` *measured whole-screen* UX audit by a second human/session remains the closure item — the in-session subagent review is a code-level proxy, not a measured visual audit.

**Status:** every Phase A–D item is implemented, verified, and (for Phase C) live-validated in the real browser with the local model on a Llama-pinned stack, screenshots saved. No merge to `main`. The remaining open item is the independent *human* measured UX audit (honor-system since 563 retired the gate).

---

## §13 The SPATIAL-COMPOSITION tier — the run renders as one ordered, prominence-graded, GENERATED-zone composition (design theory 2026-06-05)

> **Altitude pointer.** §13 is the correct long-term design for the layer §12 left hand-authored — the **spatial** composition. Same correct-design register as §3 / §12.1–§12.7: feasibility disregarded, major re-seats in scope, end-state grade, every current-behaviour claim cited against source. This is theory the next implementer de-risks (a §10/§12.10 analog is owed) — NOT a build plan, NOT yet implemented. The verdict from a live visual read of the shipped §12 window: the *structure* is right (answer leads, grounding ambient, the differentiator works), but the **left run-spine reads as a lone dot in an empty left margin** and the wide margins are *geometrically* balanced but *visually* lopsided — because the spatial composition is hand-authored Lit/CSS with no authority, and it will drift again.

### §13.0 Diagnosis (corrected) — composition's SPATIAL sub-tier is the unowned remainder, and 559 §8 left it so on purpose

§12 projected the run's **prominence facet** (`primary`/`secondary`/`ambient` on `UnifiedTurnItem`, `unifiedThreadProjection.ts`) and the **one-ordered-run projection** (`mergedTimeline()`), and composed the run *answer-first*. But the **spatial** layer — the multi-zone frame, the *run-as-visual-timeline* spine, the margin balance, the density→space mapping — stayed **hand-authored Lit/CSS** in `UnifiedChatView.ts`. Two visible failures + one structural:

- **The spine degenerates to a dot.** It IS a faithful projection of `mergedTimeline()`, but `renderRunSpine` (`UnifiedChatView.ts:~1404`) **slices to the LATEST run only** (resets `start` on every `user` item), so once an answer lands it shows one terminal node — and it is spatially **decoupled** from the reading position (scroll to an earlier answer and the spine still shows the last run). A minimap that shows only the latest run is a category error: a minimap's job is whole-history overview-and-locate.
- **The margins are geometric, not visual.** The zones are a hand-tuned 4-column grid (`UnifiedChatView.ts:~771`) whose outer `1fr` tracks are **decorative dead space** — symmetric by construction (the §12.17 Phase B fix) but visually a rich evidence rail on the right vs a lone dot on the left.
- **No authority owns the spatial composition → it will drift again.** This is the recurrence the design must prevent long-term.

**Correction of §12.1.** §12.1 said this gap "559 itself already named." It did not — **559 §8 deliberately EXCLUDED layout composition** ("the engine owns the cross-cutting element classes where the authorities apply; it does NOT own layout composition"), leaving it to hand-authored templates *on purpose*. So §13 is **not** finishing a named-but-deferred 559 item; it is the **principled REFINEMENT of 559 §8's boundary** (below).

**The boundary refinement (the key idea).** 559 §8 lumped *all* composition as bespoke. But the run / chat / evidence are **not bespoke** — their content is a **projection of one declared timeline** (`UnifiedTurnItem`), re-composed identically every turn. The correct cut:

- **Governable (the engine owns the zone FRAME):** composition whose *content is a projection* and whose *arrangement recurs* — which zones exist, their placement, the margin balance, the empty-collapse. The run-timeline spine, the evidence rail, the chat transcript's zone frame.
- **Not governable (the template owns the zone CONTENTS):** composition *within* a bespoke leaf — how the conversation column arranges its messages, how a single tool-card lays out its args/output, how a one-off form arranges fields. This stays hand-authored, exactly as 559 §8 intends.

Hold the cut at **frame vs contents**: push it past the frame (try to govern how a leaf arranges its innards) and you re-manufacture the over-DRY 559 §15 walked back.

### §13.1 Pillar A — the run made visual: a whole-conversation, prominence-graded spine, dual-bound to the reading position

The spine is an `aria-hidden` decorative minimap; its job is whole-history **overview-and-locate**. So:

- **Whole-conversation scope, prominence-graded.** Project the WHOLE ordered `mergedTimeline()`, not the latest run. Grade by the already-typed `prominence` facet: **`primary` turns (user/assistant) are landmark nodes**; **`secondary`/`ambient` steps are inter-segment texture** *between* the landmarks (the "trace segment between primary items" already implied by §12.3.F). Turns are the scannable structure; steps are density. A long history stays legible because the landmarks dominate.
- **Two bindings, because two change-reasons** (do NOT collapse them into one store — that would be the AHA violation this very tempdoc warns against): an **IntersectionObserver scroll-spy** for the *continuous* "which timeline item is in view" (reading → active spine node, unidirectional, **no FE-invented clock** — the reading column owns "what's in view", the spine derives from it); and a **`selectedSource`-style focus store** for the *discrete* click-jump (click a spine node → scroll the reading column to it; bidirectional, event-driven, mirroring the existing cross-highlight store).

Result: the spine reads as *one ordered, status-scannable run*, always aligned to what you are reading — fixing both the dot and the spatial decoupling, with **no new authority** (it reuses the prominence facet + the `selectedSource` pattern + `statusAccent`).

### §13.2 Pillar B — the composition is GENERATED from a declared zone-set, not hand-authored

A **new Composition primitive** — **beside `SurfaceLayout`, NOT an extension of it** (the §12.10 Probe R already concluded the three-zone layout is "net-new layout, NOT `SurfaceLayout` (single-column only)"; and 559 §8 puts `SurfaceLayout` on the element-class side of the line, multi-zone composition on the layout-composition side). It takes a surface's declared **`zones[] × viewport × density`** and **emits** the grid (`grid-template-columns` + zone placement) as a *total function*.

- **It owns the gutter / margin balance and zone placement — NOT the reading measure** (the measure is already correct per Probe R; do not constrain it further). The zones declare their content = a projection (the spine zone ← the timeline; the evidence zone ← the answer's grounding); the reading zone holds the bespoke transcript template (the frame/contents cut).
- **Empty-collapse is a property of the generator, not a new "adaptivity" engine.** A zone whose content projects `nothing` contributes a **zero track by construction**, so the layout rebalances and the dead gutter cannot exist. (Explicitly **DROP** any "zone-adaptivity authority": empty-collapse is NOT a generalization of the horizontal-bar `OverflowController` — §12.10 §12.3.C already refuted that, and the two share only the word "adaptive": a 1-D priority-cut-to-ellipsis vs a 2-D grid-track rebalance have different reasons to change. AHA: only unify what shares a reason to change.)

### §13.3 Anti-drift — generation is the floor, the register is the catalog (564, not the grep gate)

A grep/import-scan register has the run-renderers ceiling (§12.10 §12.6): an **import-invisible** second hand-authored grid in another component imports no canonical symbol, so the register never sees it. Per 564 ("**Gate is the floor, not the mechanism**"; a hand-authored second copy should be made *unrepresentable*, not merely caught):

- **The teeth are in GENERATION.** Because the only way to compose the governed content (run / chat / evidence) is to **declare zones and let the primitive emit the grid**, a second hand-authored composition is **unrepresentable for that content** — there is no authored grid to drift. The grep ceiling stops mattering because the authored artifact no longer exists.
- **A `composition-surfaces.v1.json` register degrades to its honest role: a CATALOG** of which surfaces declare zones — the *discovery step* for a new surface (exactly the `adaptive-regions.v1.json` framing, "adding the row is the discovery step"), plus an early-warning that a surface hand-rolls a grid for governed content. The register is necessary (discovery) but **not** the anti-drift mechanism; generation is.

### §13.4 What must NOT change

- The **content authorities** (§0–§11) and the **surface** (561) — reuse, never re-model. The new tier is strictly the *spatial frame* of already-projected content.
- The **reading measure** — already correct (Probe R); the Composition primitive owns gutters/placement, not the measure.
- The **zone CONTENTS** — the transcript's message arrangement, a tool-card's internals — stay hand-authored templates (the 559 §8 frame/contents boundary held precisely).
- The kernel + existing primitives — **extend** (a new Composition primitive *beside* `SurfaceLayout`; reuse the `prominence` facet, the `selectedSource` store, `statusAccent`, the `adaptive-regions` catalog precedent), never fork a parallel framework.

### §13.5 Honest residual, lineage & the de-risk owed

- **The hard, design-uncertain part is the GENERATOR.** Probe R validated three-zone as *net-new layout* at MEDIUM confidence; it never validated *generating* the grid from a declaration. Generating it is the only thing in this tier that actually answers "no authority owns composition" — everything else (Pillar A) is symptom repair. If generation proves heavier than authoring one good grid, the only fallback is the register-as-early-warning the codebase already lives with — but **that re-accepts drift, which the goal of this tier forbids**, so generation is not optional polish. A **pre-implementation de-risk pass (the §10 / §12.10 analog) is owed before building**: prove the zone-declaration grammar is expressive enough to model the actual composition (placement, margin balance, empty-collapse, prominence→space) — per 564, *if the declaration is too weak, the hand-authored CSS persists as a second authority*.
- **Lineage:** 559 (presentation *values* + element facets; layout composition **deferred** by §8) → 561 (the *surface*, gated by `interaction-surface`) → §0–§11 (the *content* authorities) → §12 (the *composition*: the prominence facet + the one-ordered-run projection) → **§13 (the *spatial* composition: the whole-conversation prominence-graded spine + the generated-zone frame)**. Same kernel — single authority → governed projection → register-backed *(here: generation-backed)* anti-drift — one altitude further down, refining 559 §8's deliberate boundary rather than overturning it.
- **Phasing (general, order not slices; each independently shippable + bar-raising):** (1) Pillar A — un-slice the spine to whole-conversation + prominence-grade it + the dual binding (highest-leverage *visible* win, no new authority, fixes the dot). (2) Pillar B — the Composition primitive that *generates* the zone grid from a declaration (fixes the dead margin + prevents recurrence; the de-risk-gated piece). (3) The `composition-surfaces` catalog + the discovery early-warning. The measured whole-screen UX audit (auditor ≠ committer) validates each, per §9.

### §13.6 De-risk pass (2026-06-05) — discharges §13's unknowns against source + two probes, and CORRECTS §13.2/§13.3

A read-only investigation (gate-compat + binding + grid-facets, source-cited) plus two throwaway probes (one pure-function prototype + one live spine experiment on the Llama-pinned stack, both reverted) — run before any implementation, the §10 / §12.10 analog. It resolved every §13 uncertainty and **CORRECTS §13.2/§13.3; those corrections are authoritative over §13.0–§13.5.**

- **Gate compatibility — RESOLVED: PERMIT (the biggest surprise, gone).** `check-layout-purity` scans only files that `customElements.define('jf-*-surface', …)`; a Composition *primitive* nesting inside a view/surface body is not scanned, and grids are not banned (only `position:fixed`). `presentation-purity` has no CSS-generation rule; the token gates permit `minmax(…rem)` literals (the current grid passes). **Correction of §13.2:** `UnifiedChatView` is a *view*, not a `jf-*-surface` — the primitive nests *inside* the body region; it does not sit "beside `SurfaceLayout`." No gate forbids the design.
- **Binding — RESOLVED: feasible, anchors are the only cost.** `.conversation` is the scroll root (`overflow-y:auto`); messages are direct descendants in the component's single shadow root, so an IntersectionObserver rooted at `.conversation` can observe them. Stable `data-item-id` anchors are ABSENT today and must be added — Probe S1 added them and confirmed they render (`hasDataId:true`). The scroll-spy/click-jump wiring on top is mechanical.
- **Empty-collapse — CORRECTED (the scope-reshaping finding).** Empty-collapse **already works**: a zone that renders `nothing` is unmounted and its `minmax(0,…)` track collapses. So the dead left margin was **never** a Pillar-B failure — it was a **Pillar-A content problem** (the `1fr` track held the anemic *latest-run-only* spine, not nothing). ⇒ **Pillar A alone fixes BOTH visible defects; Pillar B is purely anti-drift.**
- **Probe S1 (live) — Pillar A CONFIRMED.** A throwaway edit un-sliced `renderRunSpine` to the whole `mergedTimeline()` and prominence-graded it (landmark turns `0.62rem`, secondary/ambient texture `0.32rem`) + added the `data-item-id` anchors. Live on the multi-turn grounded conversation: the spine rendered **10 graded nodes** as a connected, scannable vertical timeline filling the left margin (NOT a dot), with the margins now roughly balanced (left zone 494 px holding the spine vs right margin 442 px). It reads as "one ordered run." Honest nuance: the probe stacked the nodes compactly at the top — the *scroll-aligned* minimap (active-node-tracks-reading) needs the scroll-spy binding, whose prerequisite (anchors + a same-shadow-root scroll container) is now confirmed; the wiring itself is unbuilt. **Pillar A is the visual fix, HIGH confidence.**
- **Probe S2 (pure function) — generator EXPRESSIBLE but does NOT earn its place yet → DOWN-SCOPE Pillar B.** A throwaway `composeGrid(zones, viewport)` fed the enumerated current-grid facet set **faithfully reproduced** the grid (narrow `minmax(0,1fr)` + wide 4-track + placements both MATCH) — so the zone-declaration grammar is **strong enough** (no 564 "declaration-too-weak" surprise); the 74ch measure correctly stays a zone-*content* concern outside the frame. BUT the generator is ~18 LOC vs the ~20 LOC hand-authored grid (indirection, not simplification), empty-collapse already works without it, and there is **exactly one** multi-zone composition surface today. So generation is a *speculative* abstraction now (YAGNI; "only unify what shares a reason to change"). **Correction of §13.2/§13.3:** ship Pillar A now (no new primitive); register the agent-chat as the canonical (and only) multi-zone composition in a `composition-surfaces` catalog + the import-scan early-warning; **extract the generator when a SECOND multi-zone surface triggers it** (the catalog "discovery step," kernel-consistent with `adaptive-regions`). The generator is the *declared, ready* structure — not a preemptive build.

**Corrected confidence (post-de-risk):**

| Part | Pre | Post | Residual |
|---|---|---|---|
| §13.1 Pillar A (whole-conversation prominence spine) | MEDIUM | **HIGH** | the scroll-spy/click-jump wiring is mechanical (anchors + scroll-root confirmed); the rest is a localized `renderRunSpine` + render-anchor edit |
| §13.1 reads-well visually | MEDIUM | **HIGH** | Probe S1 measured it scannable + margin-balanced |
| §13.2 gate-permits-the-primitive | UNKNOWN | **HIGH (PERMIT)** | nest inside the body, not a `jf-*-surface`; define any new token in `:root` |
| §13.2/§13.3 generator (Pillar B) | LOW-MEDIUM | **EXPRESSIBLE, but DEFERRED** | faithful + grammar-strong, but YAGNI for one surface → register now, generate on the 2nd multi-zone surface |

**Net:** no part is blocked, and the design simplified. The **visible defect (the dot + the unbalanced margin) is fully addressed by Pillar A alone** — a localized, gate-permitted, no-new-authority change with HIGH confidence. The generator (Pillar B) is sound and grammar-validated but is **correctly deferred** to the second multi-zone surface (registered + early-warned in the interim), avoiding a speculative build over a single artifact. §13.0–§13.5 stand except where this pass supersedes them: §13.2/§13.3's "generate now" becomes "Pillar A now; register now; generate on the second instance."

## §13.7 Implementation outcome (2026-06-05) — Pillar A + Pillar B + the register SHIPPED + live-validated

Implemented on `worktree-565-agent-window` (one phase per commit, `189c05a79..38fea1c5f`), each user-visible phase live-validated in the real browser with the local model on the Llama-pinned stack (screenshots saved). **NB — the §13.6 deferral of Pillar B was OVERRIDDEN at the user's direction (the always-structural / never-defer standing rule beats the YAGNI judgement): the generator was BUILT now, not deferred.** The de-risk had proven it feasible (Probe S2's faithful reproduction), so this was a low-surprise build, not a gamble. No merge to `main`.

- **Pillar A (P1 + P2) — the whole-conversation, prominence-graded spine + the dual binding.** `renderRunSpine` projects the WHOLE `mergedTimeline()` (not the latest-run slice), prominence-graded via the existing facet (primary turns = landmark nodes, secondary/ambient = texture); each node + each user/assistant message carries a `data-item-id` anchor. The spine is an operable `<nav>` of keyboard-operable `<button>` nodes with accessible names (controls-a11y-clean); an `IntersectionObserver` rooted at `.conversation` marks the in-view node `.active` (scroll-spy, no FE clock, `disconnectedCallback`-cleaned), and click/Enter `scrollIntoView`s the matching message (click-jump). **Live:** 10 graded nodes (6 primary + 4 texture) render as a connected, scannable vertical timeline filling the left margin (the §13.0 "lone dot" gone); the scroll-spy `.active` ring tracks the reading position; clicking a node set it active + scrolled. The narrow fallback works live (at 991 px the grid collapses to one `907px` column and the spine/rail are unmounted).
- **Pillar B (P3) — the composition is GENERATED.** New `primitives/compositionLayout.ts` — `composeGridStyles(zones, opts)` emits the grid frame (responsive `grid-template-columns` + per-zone placement) as a total function of a declared `ZoneDecl[]` (Lit `css`/`unsafeCSS`; placements as one trusted string since `css` rejects arrays). `UnifiedChatView` declares `CONVERSATION_ZONES` + appends `composeGridStyles(...)` to its static styles; the hand-authored `grid-template-columns` + the four per-zone `grid-column` placements were REMOVED (the zones keep only their content CSS — the 559 §8 frame/contents cut). Empty-collapse needs no branch (a wide-only zone that renders nothing leaves a collapsible `minmax(0,…)` track). **Live:** the generated grid renders `184px 640px 320px 184px` at 1484 px — symmetric outer tracks (centred by construction), byte-structure-identical to the prior hand-authored grid. A unit assertion pins the faithful reproduction (Probe S2 as a regression guard).
- **The anti-drift (P4) — `composition-surfaces.v1.json` + `check-composition-surfaces.mjs`.** Because a governed adopter routes its frame through the generator, the hand-authored grid for that content does not exist to drift (564 "Gate is the floor"). The gate enforces POSITIVE coverage — every `adopters` entry composes the primitive (**proven to bite:** registering a non-composing file fails it). It deliberately does NOT scan for arbitrary multi-track grids (a governed frame is syntactically indistinguishable from a bespoke leaf grid — label+value, card grids, toolbars — the §3.B/§12.10 ceiling); a new governed composition is a review-gated discovery step. Wired into `ci.yml` + the CLAUDE.md pre-merge list.

**Final verification (2026-06-05).** FE `tsc` clean · FE unit **2409 passed** (243 files; +6: the whole-conversation spine, the 2-turn span, click-jump, the generator's faithful-reproduction + frame-emission + empty-collapse) · the presentation gates green (`layout-purity`, `a11y-closure`, `controls-a11y`, `color-tokens`, `theme-token-closure`, `presentation-purity`, `observed-state-collapse`, `adaptive-closure`, `message-single-model`, `run-renderers`, `composition-surfaces`, `strip-token-fallbacks`) · `./gradlew.bat build -x test` BUILD SUCCESSFUL. Six commits `189c05a79..38fea1c5f`; clean tree. **Lineage complete: 559 → 561 → §0–11 → §12 → §13 — the kernel one altitude further down, refining 559 §8's deferral by GENERATING the governed multi-zone composition.** The honor-system residual (the independent, measured whole-screen UX audit by an auditor ≠ committer, §12.12) remains the merge-gating item.

## §13.8 Follow-up (2026-06-05) — re-zone the spine to FLANK the column, and unify the source presentation (the UI is the single source authority)

A live, measured visual critique of the shipped §13 window (real browser, Llama-pinned stack) found two residual defects — not in the structure, in **placement** and **redundancy**:

1. **The spine floated in a vast empty zone.** §12.3.D's premise was that "the spine fills the left margin to balance the rail." But a thin spine (~13 px) **cannot fill** a wide `1fr` margin — forcing it into a `1fr` zone (`justify-self: center`) floated it: ~13 px element in a ~495 px zone, 263 px dead-left, 219 px from the conversation. The premise was wrong: a spine is a **gutter that flanks the column**, not a thing that fills a margin.
2. **The sources were shown 3–4×.** Inline `[n]` marks + the `.source-chips` row + the persistent rail + (worst) **a verbose scored "Citations: [n] … (score)" list the MODEL wrote into its own prose** (confirmed in the markdown content — model prose, not a UI renderer). §3.A says the UI is the single source authority; the model's prose list violates it.

Both fixes are mostly declaration/projection over what §13 shipped. Three phases, one commit each (`dcc36e216`, `b4cc2859c`, `92cef8218`, `3a1b799f6`), then ONE live-validation batch. No merge to `main`.

- **P1 — re-zone the spine as a flanking gutter (Pillar B owns it).** `CONVERSATION_ZONES` goes from the 4-zone `[1fr-with-spine | conv | rail | 1fr]` to the **5-zone centred-group** form: `[1fr margin | .run-spine minmax(0, 2.5rem) col 2 | .conversation 40rem col 3 | .evidence-rail 15–20rem col 4 | 1fr margin]` — the reading column FLANKED by the spine gutter (left) + the rail (right), symmetric `1fr` outer margins. Pure generator-declaration change (no grammar extension); the narrow fallback is unchanged (only the non-`wideOnly` conversation participates narrow → one column). `compositionLayout.test.ts`'s `trackTemplate(…,'wide')` + `cssText` assertions updated to the 5-track string.
- **P2 — strip the model's prose citation list (the UI is the durable authority).** New exported pure `stripTrailingCitationBlock(text)` in `MarkdownBlock.ts` — removes a TRAILING block that BOTH begins (after a blank line) with a `Citations/Sources/References` heading (optionally bold/ATX) AND carries a bracketed `[n]` ref; inline `[n]` marks and mid-prose "Sources:" sentences are untouched (they lack the leading-heading + trailing-to-EOF shape). Wired into `render()` before `md.parse` (strip-before-mend so a half-written trailing list never flashes mid-stream); 7 unit tests pin strip + non-strip cases. Belt-and-suspenders prompt nudges on `AgentLoopService.DEFAULT_SYSTEM_PROMPT` + `RAGQAStyle.FRAGMENT` ("cite inline `[n]`; do NOT append a Citations/Sources/References list"). The FE strip is the authority; the prompts reduce the model producing it. (`AgentLoopService` 1038→1042 LOC: `declared-growth` changeset + pin realign — prompt text, not logic.)
- **P3 — collapse the under-answer chips behind a "Sources · N" disclosure; the rail owns detail.** `renderSourceChips(sources, key)` becomes a collapsible disclosure mirroring `CitationsPanel`'s "N sources" toggle (a `.source-disclosure-summary` `<button>` with chevron + `aria-expanded`/`aria-controls`): **collapsed by default when the wide rail is showing the same sources**, expanded by default at narrow (no rail), the per-answer choice pinned in a `sourceChipsToggles` `Map` (keyed by answer item id, or `__live__` for the streaming block). controls-a11y-clean (a native keyboard-operable button). A new unit test pins collapse-default → expand → collapse; the existing chip cross-highlight test expands first.

**Live validation (2026-06-05, real browser, measured).** A crucial discovery first: the dev-runner's frontend (`:5173`) roots its Vite server at the **canonical** repo, NOT the worktree — so the served `UnifiedChatView.ts` (203 KB) had **none** of §13/§13.8 (no `conversation-zone`/`run-spine`/`source-disclosure`/`composeGridStyles`). Validation only became real after starting Vite from the worktree's `modules/ui-web` (`:5190`, the 299 KB module WITH the markers). Against that, with the live agent having performed a real `core_search_index` (the local Qwen-9B reliably searched but would not synthesize a grounded final answer — it looped on `core_ingest_files`; orthogonal to the presentation change), the three surfaces were driven with real indexed-doc source data and measured on the real component:
  - **Spine re-zone — exact symmetry.** The LIVE computed grid at 1440 px is `370px 40px 640px 320px 370px`: the 640 px conversation flanked by the 40 px spine gutter (col 2) + the 320 px rail (col 4), with **exactly equal 370 px outer margins** (symmetric by construction — the generated grid from `CONVERSATION_ZONES`). The spine sits **38 px** from the conversation (the §12.3.D 219 px float is gone), and renders **3 prominence-graded nodes** (primary / ambient / primary+terminal) with the scroll-spy `.active` ring on the in-view node. `@media (min-width: 64rem)` confirmed live; the narrow one-column template stays unit-pinned.
  - **Citation strip — measured + visible.** The injected model-style trailing "Citations: [1] … (score)" block is **absent** from the rendered `.md-content` (stripped); the inline `[1] [2] [3]` marks are **preserved**; the answer ends cleanly at its last real sentence. (Screenshot: the answer card shows the three process sentences with inline marks and NO appended list.)
  - **Collapsible disclosure — measured both states.** Default: `aria-expanded="false"`, the chip body not rendered, the summary reads "▸ Sources · 3". On expand: `aria-expanded="true"`, chevron rotated, 3 numbered chips rendered, `aria-controls` wiring the body. The docked rail simultaneously shows the full "Sources · 3" detail (title / line / excerpt per card) — the rail owns detail, the chips are the on-demand echo.

**Final verification (§13.8).** FE `tsc` clean · FE unit **2417 passed** (243 files; +8: the 7 `stripTrailingCitationBlock` cases + the "Sources · N" disclosure collapse/expand) · the 12 presentation gates green · `class-size` green (changeset + pin realign) · `:modules:app-agent:test` + `:modules:app-services` (`RAGQAStyle`) green. Four commits `dcc36e216..3a1b799f6`; clean tree. **The §12.3.D "fill both margins" premise is corrected to "flank the column"; the source presentation is unified onto the single UI authority (strip the model's prose list, the rail owns detail, the chips a collapsible echo).** Pre-existing branch gate failures (`ui-bundle` hard-cap, `consumer-drift`, `stage-completeness`, `execution-surface`, `clone`) are unrelated to §13.8 and logged in `docs/observations.md`. The honor-system residual (the independent, measured whole-screen UX audit by an auditor ≠ committer, §12.12) remains the merge-gating item.

## §14 External-benchmark pass (2026-06-05) — the convergent industry standard validates the kernel, and names the ONE place the render trails the substrate

A web-research pass benchmarked the one window's content tier against the best-designed 2026 frontends for exactly this feature set (streaming agent runs, grounded citations, background/memory surfaces, multi-step workflow, human-in-the-loop approval). The purpose was not feature-envy but **calibration**: does the §1–§3 structure match where the category has converged, and — where it doesn't — is the gap in the *substrate* (expensive) or the *render* (cheap, projection-tier)? The finding is sharp: **the substrate is at or above the convergent bar in every authority; the one measurable shortfall is purely in the render of §3.A, and §3.A's own end-state already specifies the fix.** Sources are listed at the end of this section.

**§14.1 The convergent standard independently re-derives the run-is-a-run thesis.** The industry has standardized on **AG-UI** (the Agent-User Interaction Protocol), which models a run as five event categories — lifecycle (`RUN_STARTED`/`STEP_*`/`RUN_FINISHED`/`RUN_ERROR`), text streaming (`TEXT_MESSAGE_*`), tool execution (`TOOL_CALL_START`/`ARGS`/`END`/`RESULT`), human-in-the-loop (`INTERRUPT`), and state sync (`STATE_SNAPSHOT`/`STATE_DELTA`). This is, concept-for-concept, our one-`SseEvent`-sink + shape-descriptor model (§3.C's "one ordered run timeline"; the conversation-shape substrate's single `Consumer<SseEvent>`). The unification theory recorded in the session prose ("a run is a run — improvised / declared / background — rendered through one authority") is therefore not a local aesthetic preference but the **standard the category settled on**; the corollary is unchanged and now externally corroborated: the **workflow** run rendering through the 565 `run-renderers.v1.json` authority (rather than its bespoke `NodeProgress`/`ToolResult` fork) is the highest-value next unification step, and the **background/Presence** run is the same entity (already true in `AgentRunStore`). Confidence the run model needs no restructuring: **HIGH** (it matches the published protocol).

**§14.2 Authority-by-authority calibration against the bar.**
- **§3.A grounded answer — substrate at Perplexity bar, render one tier below.** The category bar (ShapeofAI's citation-pattern catalog; Perplexity's "evidence physically close to the claim" synthesis rule; Granola's hover-to-peek-the-quote) is **inline, claim-proximate citations with a hover card that shows the exact cited excerpt and a deep-link to the passage** — explicitly *not* a footer/end-of-text source list. Our substrate already carries precisely this: `AgentSentenceCite { sentenceText, sourceIndex, similarity }` (the claim↔source correlation) and `AgentSource { path, title, excerpt, startLine, endLine, headingText }` (the hover-excerpt + deep-link payload), both now on the `done` wire descriptor (§14-era hardening). **But §13.8 P3 shipped the *collapsed end-list* form ("Sources · N" disclosure + chips), which is the footer pattern the bar names as the *weaker* option.** This is not a contradiction of §3.A — §3.A's stated end-state is verbatim *"inline citations woven into the answer, a source-chip row beneath it, a sources pane, and click-to-the-exact-local-passage"* — it is an observation that **§13.8 realized the chips/pane/deep-link thirds of §3.A but not the *inline claim-proximate* third.** The unrealized piece is the category's *differentiator* (§4), and the research confirms it is **projection-tier**: the per-sentence correlation data is already on the wire, so weaving inline `[n]` marks keyed by `AgentSentenceCite.sentenceText` + a hover card reading `AgentSource.excerpt`/line-range is FE-only, no new substrate. → **This is the one place the render measurably trails the category, and it is cheap to close.**
- **§3.B/§3.C run-status + ordered timeline — at bar.** AG-UI's lifecycle events + progressive collapse of terminal steps is exactly §3.C's auto-collapse (`ToolCallCard` §3.C) over the one ordered timeline; the 2026 framing ("co-presence over autonomy" — show the thought process in a shared workspace, *not* Devin-style invisible background work) validates rendering the background run *in* the window rather than as a silent separate surface.
- **§3.D approval — at bar.** The universal published rule is **propose-then-commit: approval must precede side effects** ("gate after the side effect and it is not approval, it is incident documentation"), gated at the **tool level** when the call itself is the risk. Our single `<jf-authorization-host>` ceremony (550 C3) is the recommended pattern, byte-for-byte.
- **Grounding honesty — the productized form of §3.A's WARN.** The bar says *make broken/missing citations explicit* rather than hiding them. The grounding-hardening backlog items ④ (a `groundingReady` readiness signal) and ⑤ (an "N of M sentences grounded" coverage indicator) are exactly this — the user-facing productization of the silent-degradation WARN added to `collectGroundingSources()`. The research reframes them from "nice telemetry" to **the category-expected honesty surface**; they remain named content-tier work, not optional polish.
- **Memory split — confirmed correct.** Every 2026 memory product (Cloudflare Agent Memory, Mem0, Anthropic's async "Dreaming" consolidation) separates durable *facts/knowledge* from the *activity stream* of runs, with memory writes async/out-of-band. This independently confirms the session's unification conclusion: fold Presence-inbox + run-launcher into the window's run history, but keep the durable *facts* half as a distinct linked peer surface — do **not** collapse "what it knows" into "what it did."
- **Workflow — graph-for-design, stream-for-run.** LangGraph Studio is the reference: a node/edge **graph** is the *authoring/debug* view; **execution renders as a step stream** you can pause, inspect state, and resume. This sharpens the §14.1 unification step — the workflow *run* renders through the run authority (same step cards), while any DAG/authoring view stays a separate concern; do not conflate the graph editor with the run renderer.

**§14.3 What this changes in the plan (no descope, one promotion).** The benchmark adds no new authority and retires nothing. It **promotes** the inline-claim-proximate-citation render (the unrealized third of §3.A) from "implied by §3.A" to an explicitly-named, externally-justified next content-tier item, and reframes ④/⑤ as the category-expected grounding-honesty surface. Both are projection-tier over data already on the wire (`AgentSentenceCite`/`AgentSource`), validatable in the real browser per §9 — so they fit the kernel (single authority → governed projection) without forking it. Sequence, highest-value first: **(1)** weave inline claim-proximate `[n]` marks + hover-excerpt card over `AgentSentenceCite`/`AgentSource` (closes the one render gap vs. the bar); **(2)** ship ④/⑤ as the visible grounding-honesty signal; **(3)** the cross-surface unification step — render the **workflow** run through `run-renderers.v1.json` (the run-is-a-run thesis AG-UI corroborates). None of these is descoped; all are user-visible and therefore declared done only on a freshly-built dist in the real browser (§9, the stale-dist lesson).

**Sources (2026-06-05).** AG-UI protocol (event model, HITL `INTERRUPT`, generative-UI render layer): *codecademy.com/article/ag-ui-agent-user-interaction-protocol*, *docs.ag-ui.com/concepts/tools*. Citation UX patterns (inline/claim-proximate, hover-excerpt, deep-link, make-gaps-explicit): *shapeof.ai/patterns/citations*; Perplexity synthesis/citation pipeline: *ziptie.dev/blog/how-perplexity-ai-answers-work*. Generative-UI run rendering (static/declarative/open-ended; tool-lifecycle→component): *copilotkit.ai/blog/the-developer-s-guide-to-generative-ui-in-2026*. Approval placement (propose-then-commit, gate-at-risk): *mastra.ai/blog/hitl-where-to-put-approval-in-agents-and-workflows*. Memory facts-vs-activity split + async writes: *blog.cloudflare.com/introducing-agent-memory*, *mem0.ai/blog/state-of-ai-agent-memory-2026*. Workflow graph-vs-stream views: LangGraph Studio (*github.com/langchain-ai/langgraph*). Co-presence-over-autonomy framing: *blink.new/blog/best-ai-coding-agents-2026*.

## §15 The LEAF tier (design theory, 2026-06-05) — complete the single-authority kernel from the run TRUNK down to the grounded-claim LEAF

> **Status: SHIPPED (2026-06-06).** This section is the original design theory, preserved as written. §15.A–D shipped (§15.H); the **§15.J enforcement closure** then gate+seam-locked the grounding-semantics leaf and unified the approval path to one backend endpoint — so all four forked leaves are now unforkable, satisfying §15.E. Per the dated-history discipline, **§15.G/§15.H/§15.I/§15.J (later, dated) supersede the theory below where they differ** — most notably §15.I.2/§15.J correct §15.D.1's framing (the typed seam was *declined* in §15.H, then found non-breaking and *shipped* in §15.J, with the register-gate as the actual teeth). Residual (named, deferred): the ④/⑤ grounding-honesty signals + the §15.A numeric calibration. NOT merged to `main`.

The CONTENT tier (§0–§3) unified the run *record*; the COMPOSITION tier (§12) unified the *tool-card* and the *ordered run projection*; the SPATIAL-COMPOSITION tier (§13) unified the run's *spatial frame*. Each unified a **trunk**. This tier names the remainder the prior tiers never reached: the **leaves** of the one concept *"a grounded claim rendered in a run"* — the grounding **scorer**, the inline-citation **weave**, the answer **text-renderer**, and the **workflow run** — each of which is **still forked** on `main`, *because trunk-unification does not propagate to a leaf unless a typed authority-seam reaches the leaf or a register positively covers it, and neither did.* This is the same 548 two-authorities class §1 diagnosed, found one tier deeper than any of §1's three concepts — and, unlike §14, it is **not a feature gap** (the features ship); it is a **structure gap** that will silently drift. Design theory; feasibility disregarded; major re-seats in scope; reuses/extends 559's Evidence authority and 561's surface authority, invents no new kernel.

### §15.0 Correction of §14 + the corrected diagnosis (the leaf-fork class)

§14 claimed the inline, claim-proximate citation render was *"the unrealized third of §3.A"* and *"the one place the render trails the substrate."* A two-front code investigation (2026-06-05, against the worktree source) **refutes that**: the agent answer already renders inline claim-proximate `[n]` marks — `MarkdownBlock.decorateCitations()` DOM-walks the settled `.md-content`, matches each `AgentSentenceCite.sentenceText` (whitespace-tolerant, markdown-marker-stripped), splices a `cite-ref` marker keyed by `sourceKey(parentDocId,startLine)`, with a **hover-excerpt** card (`CitationHoverCard`), a **passage deep-link** (`citation-select` → `highlightCitation`/`openExternal`), and **cross-surface selection** (`selectedSource.ts`, shared by the marks, the chips, and the rail). `UnifiedChatView.resolveAnswerCitations()` resolves `AgentSentenceCite[]`+`AgentSource[]` into the `MarkdownCitation[]` the block consumes. **The Perplexity-bar feature ships.** §14's render-trails-substrate framing is therefore **superseded** (per the dated-history discipline — §15.0 wins over §14).

The corrected diagnosis: the defect is **one tier below the feature**. *"A grounded claim rendered in a run"* is ONE concept, forked at four leaves because the unification stopped at each trunk:

- **Scorer leaf — forked 3–4 ways.** `evidenceProjection.evidenceTier` (0.7/0.3 · high/medium/low · "Relevance"); `StreamingTextBlock.groundingStatus` (0.5/0.2 · grounded/weak/ungrounded); `MarkdownBlock.groundingStatus` (0.5/0.2 · same words); `CitationHoverCard` (0.5/0.2 · strong/moderate/weak, **hardcoded**). One question — *"how strongly does this source support this claim?"* — answered by four sites, **two threshold sets, three label vocabularies**. 559 named `evidenceProjection` as the Evidence typed-seam; the score-tiering **escaped it**.
- **Weave leaf — forked two ways.** RAG `StreamingTextBlock.renderAnnotated()` (plain-text segment-split, `Claim[]`, `cite-ref-click`/`cite-ref-hover` events) vs agent `MarkdownBlock.decorateCitations()` (post-render DOM-walk, `MarkdownCitation[]`, `citation-select` event). Two engines, two models, two event vocabularies for **one weave** ("mark each grounded sentence, key it to a source, hover/click to the passage").
- **Answer-text leaf — forked two ways.** plain `jf-streaming-text-block` (RAG/chat) vs markdown `jf-markdown-block` (agent). §3.C declared "one answer-presentation authority" but completed it only at the *run-ordering* level (§12/§13), never at the *text* level.
- **Run-render leaf — workflow is a bespoke fork.** `WorkflowView` ships its own `NodeProgress`/`ToolResult`, does **not** mount `jf-tool-call-card`, does **not** call `projectUnifiedThread`/`projectLiveAgentActivity`, and runs its **own** authorization flow — in 561's terms, a *second interaction surface*. (The backend is already unified: `WorkflowShapeRunner` emits to the **same** `Consumer<SseEvent>` sink as `ToolIteratingShapeRunner`; the fork is **purely the FE render path**.)

**Why the forks persisted despite §3.A naming them:** the anti-drift teeth never reached the leaf. `run-renderers.v1.json` covers the tool-card + the run-projection but **not** the scorer / weave / answer-renderer; and 561's `interaction-surface` register+gate — which would make `WorkflowView`-as-second-surface a *build failure* — was **designed but never built** (561 §2–§3, "the correct structure — unbuilt"). Prose named the unification; nothing enforced it at the leaf; it drifted.

### §15.A The one grounding-semantics authority (collapse the 3–4 scorers)

**End-state.** A single projector — the natural extension of 559's `evidenceProjection` — is the **sole** producer of a grounding verdict `{ tier, label, pct }` from a similarity. Every inline mark (`MarkdownBlock`, `StreamingTextBlock`), every hover card (`CitationHoverCard`), every chip and rail card reads it; **no renderer may hold a threshold literal.** The four scorers collapse to one; the tier words and the cut-points exist in exactly one place.

**The one genuinely-open decision (named, not defaulted — AHA / tempdoc 272: unify the mechanism, not necessarily the constants).** There are two *legitimately distinct score domains* in play: **relevance** (RAG `ContextCitation.similarity` — a cross-encoder over the *query*) and **grounding** (`AgentSentenceCite.similarity` — a cross-encoder of an *answer sentence* against a source). The threshold divergence on `main` (0.7/0.3 vs 0.5/0.2) is today an **accident** scattered across four files; the question is whether it is also a *truth*. The correct structure does not assume one answer:
- if the two domains are the *same* semantic → **one metric, one threshold set**;
- if they genuinely differ → **one projector exposing two *declared, calibrated* metrics** (`RELEVANCE`, `GROUNDING`), each with its own cut-points — so the divergence becomes a **single reviewed declaration**, not four silent copies.

Either way the *authority* is one. This is the precise completion of 559's Evidence **tier-2 typed-seam** for the one facet that escaped it — and it dissolves the §14 ④/⑤ "grounding-honesty" items into the same authority: *"is this answer grounded? how many of its sentences?"* becomes a **read** of the one verdict over `AgentSentenceCite[]`, not a new signal bolted on.

### §15.B The one answer-presentation authority + one inline-citation weave (collapse StreamingTextBlock + MarkdownBlock)

**End-state.** One answer renderer parameterized by `(text, format: plain | markdown, citations)`, with **one** format-aware citation-weave and **one** cite-interaction event vocabulary. The post-render DOM-walk generalizes to both formats (markdown is the superset; plain text is markdown with no syntax), so the agent path's `decorateCitations` mechanism — already the more capable of the two — subsumes the RAG path's `renderAnnotated` segment-split. The two citation models collapse to **one** `Citation` shape: `StreamingTextBlock.Claim` (sentenceIndex, sentenceText, score, sourceRefs) and `MarkdownBlock.MarkdownCitation` (sentenceText, similarity, label, deep-link detail, hover) already carry the same facts; one shape with one resolver (`resolveAnswerCitations`, generalized off the answer-event grounding rather than the RAG-only `Claim` path) feeds both. This is §3.C's "one answer-presentation authority" finished at the **text leaf** — the rung §12 (run ordering) and §13 (spatial frame) deliberately left, because they unified the run's *composition*, not the *answer glyphs inside one turn*.

**What this is NOT.** Not a re-theming and not a merge of *content semantics* — plain-vs-markdown stays a `format` parameter (a plain transcript must not gain markdown styling); the unification is of the **renderer + weave + event channel**, not the visual grammar. (AHA: unify what shares a reason to change — the weave and the scorer do; the format flag does not.)

### §15.C The one run-render authority that workflow ADOPTS (retire the WorkflowView fork)

**End-state.** The workflow run projects through `projectUnifiedThread`/`projectLiveAgentActivity` into `UnifiedTurnItem[]` and renders through `jf-tool-call-card` + the unified conversation render: a workflow **node** → a turn/step item; a **ToolStep** → `jf-tool-call-card` (the one primitive, with its `composeToolLabel` authority and its `searchEvidence`/`mcpContent` rich content); a **GateStep** → the **shared** `<jf-authorization-host>` ceremony (550 C3), not `WorkflowView`'s private `requestAuthorization`. **Workflow becomes a MODE of the one window (561), not a surface.** Because `WorkflowShapeRunner` already shares the SSE sink, the work is a **render-path adoption + an event-kind mapping** (`workflow_started`/`node_started`/`node_completed`/`tool_exec_completed` → the unified `user`/`assistant`/`tool-activity`/`progress` kinds the projection already speaks), **not** a backend rebuild. The graph/DAG *authoring* view, if one is ever wanted, stays a separate concern (§14.2: graph-for-design, stream-for-run) — the **run** renders through the one authority. `AgentRunStore` already proves the persistence half of this unification (it holds agent **and** background runs as one entity behind a `background` flag; the memory Presence surface is a projection of it) — workflow runs are the remaining EPHEMERAL hold-out, persisted-or-not being an orthogonal axis to *how they render*.

### §15.D The anti-drift teeth — prefer the typed seam, extend the registers, build 561's owed gate

The forks persisted because nothing enforced the unification at the leaf. The correct structure makes re-forking **unrepresentable**, strongest mechanism first:

1. **Typed seam over grep gate (559 tier-2 > tier-4; the §12.10 honest limit made load-bearing).** A grep/register gate only catches *import-visible* forks — a renderer that hand-rolls a threshold while importing nothing **slips** (this is exactly how the four scorers drifted under an existing register regime). The *strongest* prevention is to make the leaf value **unreproducible except through the authority**: the grounding-verdict `tier` is a branded/opaque type **only constructible by `evidenceProjection`**, so a renderer literally *cannot* compute its own tier — it must hold the authority's value. Prefer this wherever the type system can carry the constraint (the scorer, §15.A — the highest-value place to apply it).
2. **Extend the run-render register to the weave + answer-renderer (where the type can't reach).** `run-renderers.v1.json` grows (or gains a sibling `evidence-render` register) declaring the ONE answer-renderer + ONE citation-weave + ONE cite-event vocabulary, with **positive coverage** (the §13.3 pattern: declare the authority → the gate auto-covers it; a second inline-`[n]` weave or a second answer-text renderer fails). This is the tier-4 fallback for the seams the type system cannot brand.
3. **Build 561's deferred `interaction-surface` register+gate (the teeth for §15.C).** It is *already designed* in 561 §2–§3 (catalog audience×consumes scan + positive coverage + forbidden-reintroduction) and merely unbuilt; standing it up makes `WorkflowView`-as-second-surface a build failure and forces workflow to contribute a *mode/panel*. **This is owed to 561, not new to 565** — 565's §15.C is the concrete adopter that motivates finally building it. (Per 561 §, plugin-owned *novel* interaction shapes stay un-fenced; the gate fences only the **core** interaction-shape from re-forking.)

### §15.E The meta-principle (the general prevention, stated once)

**Unification at the trunk does not propagate to the leaves unless the authority's typed seam reaches the leaf, or a register positively covers it.** 565 unified the run record / tool-card / projection; 559 unified the evidence record and *named* the seam; 561 unified the window record — yet *"a grounded claim in a run"* **lives at the leaf** (the scorer, the weave, the answer glyphs, the workflow step), and every one of those leaves was reached by **neither** a typed seam **nor** a register. The cure is **not** "audit harder" — 559 §15 already established that the audit-keeps-finding-drift loop is evidence the *projection is missing*, not that auditing is insufficient. The cure is to **push the authority's seam (preferred) or register (fallback) down to the leaf**, so that every leaf of a unified concept either *reads a value it cannot reproduce* or is *positively covered by a gate that fails on a fork*. Stated as a rule for the next concept that unifies a trunk: **a unification is only complete when its leaves are unforkable — name the leaves, and reach each one with a seam or a gate before declaring the trunk done.**

### §15.F Lineage, reuse boundary & residuals (honest accounting)

- **Reuses (unchanged):** `evidenceProjection` (the Evidence seam), `projectUnifiedThread`/`projectLiveAgentActivity` (the run projection), `jf-tool-call-card` + `composeToolLabel` (the tool primitive + label authority), `selectedSource` (cross-surface selection), `<jf-authorization-host>` (the shared ceremony), `AgentRunStore` (the one run entity).
- **Extends:** the Evidence seam down to the score-**tier** (§15.A); the answer renderer + weave into one format-parameterized authority (§15.B); the run-render register to the weave/answer-renderer (§15.D.2).
- **Adds nothing 559/561 didn't already name:** the `interaction-surface` gate (§15.D.3) is **561's**, owed; the typed-seam discipline (§15.D.1) is **559's** tier-2, applied. 565's contribution at this tier is the *diagnosis that the leaves were missed* and the *meta-principle* (§15.E), not a new mechanism.
- **The one open decision:** the two-score-domain question (§15.A — one metric or one projector / two declared metrics) is a genuine design choice to be made against the calibration data, **named as a decision, not defaulted**.
- **Validation discipline unchanged (§9):** every user-visible piece of any eventual implementation is declared done only on a **freshly-built dist in the real browser** (the §10/§13.8 stale-dist lesson), never on green unit tests alone.

## §15.G De-risk pass (2026-06-05) — discharges §15's unknowns against source + a live probe, and CORRECTS §15.A/§15.B/§15.C/§15.D

Before any implementation, §15's load-bearing assumptions were verified against code (two `Explore` traces + direct reads) and a live dev-stack probe. The pass **corrected four of the six claims**. As with §10/§12.10/§13.6, the later section wins where it differs.

- **§15.A — CORRECTED: the "two-score-domain" open decision (§15.F) is FALSIFIED → it is ONE metric, one scorer, one scale.** A backward trace proves `ContextCitation.similarity` (RAG) and `AgentSentenceCite.similarity` (agent) are produced by the **same** worker scorer: `AgentCitationResolver` converts `AgentSource`→`ContextCitation` and calls the *same* `documents.matchCitations(answer, citations, threshold)` path RAG's `StreamingCitationMatcher` uses → `CitationMatchOps.execute()` (cross-encoder `CitationScorer`; embedding-cosine fallback), both on `[0,1]` (`AgentCitationResolver.java:45-65`, `CitationMatchOps.java:128-281`, `StreamingCitationMatcher.java:127-140`). Both are *answer↔source grounding* — NOT "relevance vs grounding." So the displayed-tier split (RAG `evidenceProjection.evidenceTier` **0.7/0.3** vs the inline blocks' `groundingStatus` **0.5/0.2**) is **drift, not calibration**; §15.A is **one metric, one threshold set** (the §15.F "genuine design choice" was an artifact of not having traced the producer). **A second single-authority item surfaced:** the *matcher CUTOFFs* also diverge — `AgentCitationResolver` drops citations below **0.45**, `StreamingCitationMatcher` below **0.5** — so the very *set* of cited sentences can differ between paths for one answer; §15.A must own the cutoff, not only the display tier. **The cut-point *values* could not be calibrated live** (see the live-probe note below); but the *unification* stands entirely on the code trace and does **not** depend on the distribution — choosing the single tier/cutoff numbers is an implementation-time calibration, not a design unknown.
- **§15.B — REFINED: the grammars genuinely differ (union, confirmed), but the event blast-radius is SMALL.** `StreamingTextBlock.renderAnnotated` (RAG) colors **every** sentence by grounding status (whole-answer heat-map) and numbers `[n]` **sequentially**; `MarkdownBlock.decorateCitations` (agent) marks **only cited** sentences, numbers `[n]` by **source index**, and carries the deep-link + `selectedSource` cross-highlight — so the unified weave is the **union** (agent's source-stable deep-linked marks + RAG's per-sentence coloring), and the unified `Citation` carries `sourceRefs: number[]` (RAG `Claim` is multi-source; agent `MarkdownCitation` one-source). **But the consumer change is contained:** `citation-select` is *already* the shared deep-link event (4 emitters — `CitationsPanel`/`MarkdownBlock`/`SourcesPane`/`UnifiedChatView` — into the one `Shell.onCitationSelect` consumer), and `cite-ref-hover`/`cite-ref-leave` are *already* shared (both blocks → `UnifiedChatView` → `CitationHoverCard`). The **only** divergence is the click: `StreamingTextBlock` emits `cite-ref-click` (sentenceIndex-only, no deep-link) where `MarkdownBlock` emits `citation-select` (full deep-link). So §15.B converges clicks onto the already-canonical `citation-select` — a small, well-bounded change, not a rewrite of the event layer.
- **§15.C — CORRECTED on cost: tool-events are ALREADY compatible; the real blocker is ephemerality + missing order key (a BACKEND decision, not FE-only).** `WorkflowShapeRunner` *intentionally* emits `tool_call_pending`/`tool_exec_started`/`tool_exec_completed`/`tool_call_approved`/`tool_call_rejected` with `callId`, reusing the agent broker (`WorkflowRunShape.java:39-59`) → the shared `<jf-authorization-host>` and the callId-lifecycle collapse work as-is. **But** `WorkflowRunShape` is `PersistenceMode.EPHEMERAL`, writes nothing to `AgentRunStore`, and emits **no per-event `occurredAt`**; the record-side `projectUnifiedThread` reads only `/api/thread/{id}` (`unifiedThreadClient.ts:84-103`) → it **cannot see a workflow run**, and even the live `projectLiveAgentActivity` needs a per-event order key. So §15.C is **not** "FE render-path adoption only" as the §15.C prose implied: it requires a backend decision — **persist workflow runs + stamp events** (record-side parity, reload-durable) *or* **add per-event timestamps + wire the live controller** (live-only, no reload durability). Name it as a decision; the tool-vocabulary half is free.
- **§15.D — CORRECTED (factual error): the 561 `interaction-surface` gate IS BUILT and LIVE — it is NOT "owed/unbuilt."** `scripts/governance/gates/interaction-surface/enforcer.mjs` + `governance/interaction-surfaces.v1.json` exist and enforce "one visible USER×{RAIL,STAGE} surface consuming a **core** shape = the canonical `core.unified-chat-surface`." My §15.D.3/§15.F claim that it was "designed but never built" and "owed to 561" is **wrong**. **However, the gate does NOT catch the workflow fork:** `WorkflowView` mounts via `registerViewFactory('core.workflow-run','jf-workflow-surface')` and `core.workflow-surface` *is* a registered RAIL surface (`CoreSurfaceCatalog.java:367-380`) — but it consumes `core.workflow-run`, which is **excluded from `CORE_USER_INTERACTION_SHAPES`** (only rag-ask/free-chat/extract/agent-run), so the gate is scope-filtered past it. → The correct §15.D teeth is a **one-line scope change — bring `core.workflow-run` into the gate's core-shape set** — after which the gate fails on `core.workflow-surface` as a second visible surface, forcing workflow to fold into the canonical window. The gate machinery itself needs no new build.
- **Live-probe note (operational, 2026-06-05).** A dev-stack probe (taken over with user approval, then released) found this data dir has **no chat model** (`MODEL_PATH_REQUIRED`) and the **citation cross-encoder ONNX `not_found`** (`onnxFeatures[citation_scorer].status="inactive"/"not_found"`, `citationOrtCuda.configured=false`) — so any live grounding similarity would come from the **embedding-cosine fallback**, not the production cross-encoder, and `chunkCoverage` was `ready:false`. Per *interrogate-results*, calibrating the §15.A cut-points off the fallback path would measure the **wrong scorer**; the live calibration is therefore deferred to an environment with the citation scorer loaded + chunk coverage ready (the readiness ④/⑤ signals would themselves fire here — a tidy corroboration that the "grounding-honesty" surface is the right product). The probe did **not** weaken any code-proven verdict above.

**Net confidence after the pass.** §15.A unification: **HIGH** (code-proven one scorer/one scale; only the numeric cut-points await calibration — an impl detail). §15.B: **HIGH** (union grammar confirmed; consumer change small and bounded). §15.C: **MEDIUM-HIGH** (FE adoption clear; the persist-vs-live backend decision is named, not open-ended). §15.D: **HIGH** (gate exists; the fix is a one-line scope addition + the deliberate inclusion of workflow-run). The §15.E meta-principle is unaffected. No production code, canonical-doc, or merge changes in this pass.

## §15.H Implementation outcome (2026-06-06) — §15.A + §15.B shipped, §15.C backend shipped; §15.C FE + live verification residual

The LEAF tier was implemented in the `worktree-565-grounding-hardening` worktree (never on `main`; no merge — the user lands it). As-built, with the verification surfaced in the implementing transcript:

- **§15.A — one grounding-semantics authority — SHIPPED + verified.** `evidenceProjection.ts` is now the sole producer of the grounding tier: `groundingClass` (inline-mark CSS stem) and `groundingLabel` (hover word) both derive from the single `evidenceTier` threshold (extracted to private `TIER_HIGH`/`TIER_MEDIUM`). The three forked FE scorers (`MarkdownBlock.groundingStatus`, `StreamingTextBlock.groundingStatus`, `CitationHoverCard.scoreLabel`) were deleted and routed through it. The backend matcher cutoff was unified onto one `DocumentService.DEFAULT_CITATION_SIMILARITY_THRESHOLD` (both `AgentCitationResolver` and `StreamingCitationMatcher` read it). Tests: +3 `evidenceProjection` cases pinning the one-similarity→one-tier collapse. **The chosen tier/cutoff values (0.7/0.3 display; 0.5 cutoff) are the §15.G-deferred calibration — they live in one place now and await the live distribution to finalize.**
- **§15.B — one answer renderer + one inline-citation weave — SHIPPED + verified.** `MarkdownBlock` is the one answer renderer (`format: 'plain' | 'markdown'`; cited-sentence tier coloring via a robust single-text-node wrap; the one `Citation` shape). `StreamingTextBlock` was **retired** (its `Claim` model relocated to the leaf `citationTypes`; its plain rendering + cursor subsumed). RAG + agent both render through the one weave; the RAG `Claim`→`Citation` mapping lives once in `citationResolve.claimsToCitations` (shared by `UnifiedChatView` + `SummarizeView`), so RAG gained the source-stable, deep-linked, cross-surface marks it lacked. The cite click converged onto the already-canonical `citation-select` (the `cite-ref-click` + `resolveMessageData` plumbing retired). The `run-renderers.v1.json` register + gate were extended with the `answerRenderer` (one block, 6 mount sites) + `weave` (one resolver) coverage. Tests: +3 `claimsToCitations` cases; FE `tsc` clean + **2450 unit tests pass**.
- **§15.C — workflow adopts the run-render authority — SHIPPED + verified (backend + FE).** *Backend:* the shape-agnostic **`RunEventStore`** was extracted from `AgentRunStore`'s event-log half (the generic `{timestamp,eventType,payload}` ndjson + listener fan-out + the legacy upcaster + a minimal run-meta index); `AgentRunStore` now composes it (behavior-preserving — app-agent tests green). `WorkflowShapeRunner` **persists + indexes** every run through the *shared* store (a conversation-linked `meta.json` + each streamed event, via a persisting sink wrapper), wired through a new `HeadAssembly.agentRunStore()` accessor + the `LocalApiServer` injection. `AgentInteractionMapper` was generalized (the `tool_exec_started` identity case) so the workflow's tool calls — which already share the agent `tool_call_*`/`chunk`/`done` vocabulary — project; a persisted workflow run projects into the unified thread record-side (`listRunIdsByConversation` finds it; `fromRunEvent` renders it as tool cards + a final assistant message). *FE:* the live path turned out to be far smaller than feared — `AgentSessionController.dispatchEvent` already handles the shared vocabulary and no-ops the workflow-only wrappers, so ONE controller drives both ("a run is a run"): a new `AgentSessionController.runWorkflow(workflowId)` streams `shapeId='core.workflow-run'` into the SAME conversation/toolCalls model `projectLiveAgentActivity` renders (with the side-channel approve/reject routed to the workflow gate). `WorkflowView`/`WorkflowSurface` were **retired**; `core.workflow-run` now mounts `jf-unified-chat-view` (preset to the agent-rendered mode; mounting the shape auto-runs the workflow) — workflow is a MODE of the one window, not a surface.
- **§15.D — anti-drift teeth — SHIPPED.** §15.D.2 (the `run-renderers` register/gate extension for the answer-renderer + weave) shipped with §15.B. §15.D.1 (the typed grounding-tier seam) was assessed and, per the plan's own rule ("prefer the typed seam *where the type system can carry it*"), the string-union tier's ergonomics (the `CitationsPanel` `=== 'high'` comparisons) favored the private-threshold + register-gate form — a plan-sanctioned fallback, recorded here, not a silent omission. §15.D.3 (bringing `core.workflow-run` into the live `interaction-surface` gate scope) **shipped with the §15.C FE retirement**: `core.workflow-run` was added to `CoreConversationShapeCatalog.CORE_USER_INTERACTION_SHAPES` + the FE mirror `coreInteractionShapes.ts` + the unified-chat-surface's consumed shapes, and `core.workflow-surface` was removed from `CoreSurfaceCatalog` + `CorePlugin`. The live **`interaction-surface` gate passes** — a re-introduced second visible workflow surface is now a build failure.

**Verification (build/test, surfaced green in the implementing transcript):** `./gradlew.bat build -x test` **BUILD SUCCESSFUL**; app-agent tests **BUILD SUCCESSFUL** (the `RunEventStore` extraction + mapper generalization behavior-preserving); `class-size` governance gate **pass** (the `LocalApiServer` +7 LOC growth declared via a `565` changeset); FE `tsc` clean + **2450 unit tests**; the **`run-renderers`** gate green; the **`interaction-surface`** gate **pass** (workflow folded into the one window). The only red is the pre-existing, unrelated `AppServicesWorkerGuardrailsTest`/ExamplePlugin `getenv` (logged).

**Residual (the §9 discipline's final gate):** (a) the §15.A tier/cutoff numeric calibration against a live distribution (the values live in one place, awaiting the data); (b) the single batched **live-browser verification** on a model-configured stack (one tier/colour per score across surfaces; RAG per-sentence coloring + deep-linked marks; the workflow run rendering as unified turns + tool cards + shared ceremony) — requires the chat model + citation-scorer ONNX loaded (present canonically; unconfigured in the current dev data dir per §15.G). **All §15.A–D CODE is implemented + statically green; the live verification is the remaining gate.**

**Live-browser verification (2026-06-06, real browser, worktree Vite :5199 → fresh-installDist backend :56604, Meta-Llama-3.1-8B online).** The §15.G model-config blocker was overcome by setting `llm.modelPath` via `POST /api/settings/v2` (the canonical GGUF), then `ai_activate` (GPU); 3 docs ingested → chunkCoverage 100% ready. Verified, with screenshots:
- **§15.A + §15.B — a grounded agent answer in the one window:** the markdown answer rendered through the ONE `MarkdownBlock` with inline `¹` citation marks woven in, the cited sentences **underlined by grounding tier** (the StreamingTextBlock per-sentence coloring ported into the markdown weave), and the **"Sources · 1"** collapsible disclosure + the **"1 System Overview"** chip — the inline mark, the sentence coloring, and the chip all reference the one source consistently (the §15.A one-authority collapse + the §15.B one-renderer/one-weave, live).
- **Shared approval ceremony (which §15.C reuses):** the agent proposed a medium-risk `core_ingest_files` write → the unified `<jf-authorization-host>` "Authorize action" dialog rendered (Deny/Approve); the Deny registered on the run-spine as "2 steps · 1 denied".
- **§15.C — a workflow run in the one window:** `agentCtrl.runWorkflow('core.demo-compose')` (the §15.C controller path, reached through the shadow tree) streamed into the SAME unified window — rendered as a "Run workflow: core.demo-compose" turn + the run-spine + the validation result, NOT a bespoke surface (title stayed "Unified Chat"). The demo workflow failed *validation* (`core.demo-compose` delegates to `vendor.mcphost.*` operations not loaded in this dev stack — an environment/demo-content gap, not a §15.C defect), so its tool steps did not run; the tool-cards + ceremony primitives the workflow reuses were shown live by the agent run in this same window.

**Environment boundary (honest):** the reranker + citation-scorer ONNX were `not_found` in the dev data dir (the "semantic search degraded" banner) so grounding used the embedding-cosine fallback — sufficient to verify the FE render, but the §15.A tier/cutoff numeric calibration still wants the production cross-encoder distribution; and the demo workflow's mcphost delegations are unavailable without that plugin pack. The stack + worktree Vite were stopped after capture. **Net: every §15.A–D user-visible behavior was confirmed rendering correctly in the real browser, to the boundary the dev environment's models allow.**

## §15.I Post-implementation design reflection (2026-06-06) — what the build corrected, validated, and left honestly open

Implementing §15 end-to-end produced findings the design theory should absorb — corrections to the de-risk's fears, a validation of the §15.E meta-principle, and an honest critical-analysis pass over the residual forks.

**1. §15.C's FE coupling was OVER-feared — the controller was already shape-agnostic ("a run is a run" was MORE true than assumed).** Across §15.G and three in-session checkpoints I framed the workflow live-integration as a hard coupling — "the unified window's *live* path is built around `AgentSessionController`/`projectLiveAgentActivity` (agent-specific), so workflow must join that controller path before `WorkflowView` can be retired." The reality, found on reading the controller: `dispatchEvent` routes by a generic `map[event]?.(payload)` that handles the shared `tool_call_*`/`chunk`/`done` vocabulary and **silently no-ops the workflow-only wrappers** (`workflow_started`/`node_*`). So ONE `runWorkflow(workflowId)` method — dispatch a different `shapeId`/`body` into the *same* dispatch — was the whole live integration; the controller was already vocabulary-agnostic at the event seam. The de-risk was right to *flag* the coupling as the risk locus but wrong about its *magnitude*. The lesson: **a shared event vocabulary + a graceful-ignore dispatch is itself a form of trunk-unification that makes leaf-adoption nearly free** — and the failure mode of a de-risk is over-estimating a gap the trunk's seam already spans.

**2. §15.D.1's typed seam was assessed and DECLINED — the register-gate fallback is the honest teeth.** The plan committed to a branded `GroundingTier` seam as the strongest prevention. But the tier is a string union (`'high'|'medium'|'low'`) compared with `=== 'high'` in `CitationsPanel`'s grouping; an intersection-brand breaks those literal comparisons, and converting every consumer to authority-predicates was more churn than the marginal safety bought. Per the plan's own rule ("prefer the typed seam *where the type system can carry it*"), the correct fallback was taken: **private thresholds + one mapper + the deletion of the three forked scorers** (no renderer can hold a threshold), backed by the register-gate. The sharpened theory: a string-union *enum/tier* is a recurring shape the type system "cannot cleanly carry" as a brand — for those facets, the teeth are *deletion of the fork + a positive-coverage gate*, not nominal typing.

**3. Critical-analysis pass — residual leaf-forks the build surfaced (named, not hidden):**
   - **Two backend approval endpoints.** The shared `<jf-authorization-host>` ceremony is ONE FE authority, but `runWorkflow`'s approve/reject route to `/api/chat/workflow/{approve,reject}` while the agent routes to `/api/chat/agent/{approve,reject}`; the controller bridges them by `runShapeId`. The *ceremony* is unified; the *gate endpoints* are still two. A deeper unification — one approval endpoint keyed by `callId` regardless of shape — is a follow-on leaf.
   - **The workflow trigger is auto-run-on-mount.** Mounting `core.workflow-run` auto-runs the demo workflow — adequate for the structural unification (workflow renders through the one window), but the proper UX is a workflow *mode with a picker* (the user chooses the workflow), replacing the retired "Run demo workflow" button. A follow-on, not a descope.
   - **§15.A numeric calibration.** The tier/cutoff values (0.7/0.3 display; 0.5 cutoff) now live in one place but await the production cross-encoder distribution (the dev stack verified the render on the cosine fallback).

**4. §15.E meta-principle — validated + a COST corollary.** The build confirmed "a unification is complete only when its leaves are unforkable," and added: **the cost of reaching a leaf is inversely proportional to how far the trunk's seam already extends toward it.** Where the seam reached the leaf (the controller's vocabulary-agnostic dispatch; the shared `Consumer<SseEvent>` sink; the shape-agnostic `events.ndjson` log) leaf-adoption was nearly free (a method, a delegation); where it did not (the scorer fork, the two answer-renderers) active collapse was required (deletions, a shared resolver). Practical guidance for the next leaf-unification: **measure how far the trunk's seam already reaches *first* — that measurement is the de-risk's real value, and over-estimating the gap is its characteristic error (this slice's §15.G being the example).**

**5. Operational discovery (a reusable dev-stack live-verify recipe).** §15.G concluded the chat model was "unconfigurable through the available dev tooling." That was wrong: `POST /api/settings/v2` with `{"llm":{"modelPath":"<gguf>","gpuLayers":99}}` configures the chat model at runtime, then `ai_activate` loads it — no installer pack-import, no `-D justsearch.llm.model_path` restart. This is the recipe that unblocked the live verification; it belongs in the `/dev-stack` discipline (logged to `docs/observations.md`).

## §15.J Enforcement closure (2026-06-06) — the kernel's third leg (register-backed gate) landed for the grounding leaf + the approval path unified

A purely-theoretical re-read of the tempdoc against the *shipped* §15 found the LEAF tier achieved the **unification** (one scorer, one weave, one renderer, workflow renders in the one window) but only **half the enforcement** — the kernel's third leg ("single authority → governed projection → **register-backed gate**"). Two of four leaves were gate-locked (the answer-renderer/weave gate §15.D.2; the interaction-surface gate §15.D.3); two were convention-only (the grounding-semantics authority had no gate/seam; the approval path was still forked at the backend). By §15.E's own test — *a unification is complete only when its leaves are unforkable* — the grounding leaf was incomplete. This pass closes both.
