- **Phase 1a — the typed seam (`GroundingTier`) SHIPPED — and §15.I.2's "declined" verdict is CORRECTED.** §15.I.2 recorded the brand as *declined* on the belief that "an intersection-brand breaks those `=== 'high'` literal comparisons" in `CitationsPanel`. **That belief was empirically wrong.** `GroundingTier = ('high'|'medium'|'low') & { readonly __groundingTier: unique symbol }` is *non-breaking*: a branded string-union still **overlaps** the plain literals, so `evidenceTier(s.score) === 'high'` still type-checks (typecheck clean, zero consumer breakage). What the brand actually buys is narrower than §15.I.2 feared and still worth having: a renderer **cannot fabricate a tier** and pass it where a `GroundingTier` is expected — it must obtain it from `evidenceTier`. So the seam shipped (the `present.ts` `DisplayLabel` idiom), with an internal unbranded `computeTier` for the file's own switches, plus `tierGroup`/`tierClass` authority helpers; `CitationsPanel` was routed through them (grouping by `tierGroup` *index*, CSS stem by `tierClass`) so **no consumer holds a tier literal of its own** — behaviour-preserving (`CitationsPanel`/`evidenceProjection` tests green). The sharpened §15.I.2 theory: *a string-union brand is soft (it permits `===` by overlap) but composes with a literal-scan gate — the brand stops fabrication, the gate stops re-derivation; together they are the teeth, and neither alone is.*

- **Phase 1b — the `groundingSemantics` register-gate SHIPPED + proven on a planted fork (the §6 "evidence-surface gate", scorer facet).** `governance/run-renderers.v1.json` gained a `groundingSemantics` section (authority `evidenceProjection.ts`; the tier symbols; the registered consumer sites; the grounding output vocabulary) and `check-run-renderers.mjs` gained two checks: **(i) import-scope** — only registered consumers import the tier-classification symbols (a new importer = a new classifier, forces review); **(ii) a threshold-literal proximity scan** — no file but the authority maps a numeric threshold to a grounding class within ~60 chars (`score >= 0.X ? 'grounded'`), the *import-invisible* fork the seam alone cannot catch. **Proof, not assertion:** two planted forks (a no-import `score >= 0.5 ? 'grounded'` re-derivation; a new unregistered file importing `groundingClass`) were each caught (gate red), and the gate returned green on revert. Honest scope (§12.10): import-visible + literal-visible; a fully-obfuscated re-derivation still slips — the same ceiling as the sibling run-renderer checks, named not hidden.

- **Phase 1c — the §6 "evidence-surface gate" is the COMBINATION now standing, recorded.** The §6 promise ("a grounded answer with no evidence projection, and a second grounded-answer authority, unrepresentable") is realised as a *mix*, named honestly: the grounding-semantics gate (1b) + the answer-renderer/weave gate (§15.D.2) + the build-pinned `AgentDone.sources/citations` carrier (`AgentEventPayloadConformanceTest`). The one part that is **genuinely not build-gateable** — a *rendered* grounded answer that silently dropped its evidence — stays the runtime `WARN` (`AgentSession.collectGroundingSources`) + the deferred grounding-readiness signal (④/⑤), explicitly NOT faked as a gate. So "a second grounded-answer authority is unrepresentable" is now backed by gate+conformance+runtime-signal, with the residual stated rather than papered over.

- **Phase 2 — the approval path unified ("a run is a run" all the way DOWN, not just on screen).** The shared `<jf-authorization-host>` ceremony previously posted to **two** endpoints (`/api/chat/agent/*` via `AgentSession.approvalGates`; `/api/chat/workflow/*` via `WorkflowGateRegistry`), the FE branching the URL by `runShapeId`. Now **one** endpoint pair `POST /api/chat/{approve,reject}` dispatches a Context-free decision (`AgentController.resolveApprovalGate`): the agent gate (`sessionId`+`callId`) → the workflow gate (`callId`) → 404. `AgentService` gained `tryApprove/tryRejectToolCall(...) : boolean` (whether a gate existed; `AgentSession.approve/reject` now return that); the FE dropped the `runShapeId` branch (the field is gone — it had no other reader); the MCP dev tool's approval POST + the canonical `api-contract-map` were migrated; the forked routes + their handlers were **retired**. A new `AgentControllerApprovalDispatchTest` pins that one endpoint resolves BOTH gate types by callId (agent-first, workflow-fallthrough, unknown→false). The run-substrate differences that remain (session cancel/resume, the autonomy dial) are **legitimately agent-only** (workflows are stateless/deterministic) — documented as NOT a fork, so the unification stops at the genuinely-shared *approval* concept.

**Net.** All four §15 leaves are now unforkable by the same mechanism: a single authority, a governed projection, and a register-backed gate (or, where the type system carries it, a seam *and* a gate). The grounding leaf — the one §15.E flagged as incomplete — is closed: its score→tier→grounding mapping cannot be re-implemented (gate) or fabricated (seam) outside `evidenceProjection`, and a grounded answer's evidence carrier is build-pinned. The approval path is one backend authority end-to-end. This pass shipped enforcement + a behaviour-preserving refactor (no new user-visible feature); verification is the gate failing on a planted fork + the unit behaviour-preservation + the §15.H live render still standing. **The genuinely-deferred work that remains is the same honestly-named pair: the §15.A numeric calibration against the production cross-encoder distribution, and the ④/⑤ grounding-readiness signals — neither a gate, both named.**

**Live verification (2026-06-06, real backends).** The one user-visible plumbing change (the approval URL migration) was confirmed against running binaries, and the live pass *earned its keep* by surfacing a latent bug:
- **Route migration confirmed on the worktree binary** (a worktree-rooted `dev-runner` stack on :56700, built from the §15.J dist): `POST /api/chat/approve` and `/api/chat/reject` exist and reach the unified dispatcher; the forked `POST /api/chat/agent/approve` returns 404 *no-handler* (retired). A missing-gate call returns a clean 404 *"No pending approval gate for callId …"* — the dispatch runs agent-gate → workflow-gate → 404.
- **A latent NPE was caught live and fixed.** The first worktree probe with an absent `sessionId` hit `ConcurrentHashMap.get(null)` (HTTP 400) inside `tryApproveToolCall`. Fixed: `AgentLoopService.tryApprove/tryRejectToolCall` now skip the agent gate on a null/blank `sessionId` (a workflow-only approve falls straight through to the workflow gate), with an `AgentLoopServiceTest` regression; the rebuilt worktree binary re-probed to the clean 404. This is the exact class of defect a live pass exists to catch — the FE always sends a non-null `sessionId`, so units alone would not have exercised the null path.
- **Real-gate resolution proven on the canonical binary** (the dev-MCP stack): a real agent run at `watch` autonomy reached a genuine `tool_call_pending` gate (`core_file_operations`, high-risk), and an approve POST resolved it (HTTP 200 `{"status":"approved"}`) via the **identical** `AgentSession.approve(callId)` path the unified dispatcher's agent-gate branch calls.
- **Honest boundary (a §13.8-class wall, not a defect).** The *combination* "a real pending gate **and** the new route on the **same** worktree binary" was not obtainable: the dev-MCP is canonical-`repoRoot` (so its stack serves main, which lacks the new route), and the worktree-rooted `dev-runner` backend cannot serve the LLM — its native-bin variant scan returns `installedVariants: []` (`RUNTIME_VARIANT_NOT_INSTALLED: cuda12`) because the worktree tree has no built native-bin — so it cannot generate a tool call to reach a gate. Every *constituent* (new route + dispatch + null-guard live on the worktree binary; real-gate resolution live on canonical via the identical code path; the 4-case dispatch + null-session regression units) is independently proven; only their co-location on one binary is environment-blocked. Per the plan's own allowance, the behaviour-preservation rests there. The grounding render (Phase 1a/1b) is behaviour-preserving, unit-pinned, and already live-verified in §15.H — not re-driven, as the worktree backend's LLM is unavailable by the same wall.

## §16 The run status-spine — visual-state calibration (2026-06-09 design research)

A focused design-research pass on ONE element of the §13 spatial-composition tier: the **run status-spine** (§13 Pillar A — the whole-conversation, prominence-graded status gutter that flanks the reading column). §13 shipped the spine's STRUCTURE (the generated zone, the prominence grading, the scroll-spy `.active` ring, live-validated §13.7); this pass calibrates its VISUAL STATE against the best-designed-for-the-job references — the way §14 calibrated §3 against the category bar. It is **presentation calibration of the existing spine projection, not a re-model**: the spine stays a projection of the one run record (§12's `UnifiedTurnItem` / run events) through the §3.B status-tone authority; no new authority, no new kernel. Design theory; the numeric/visual tokens are an implementation-time calibration; validation per §9 (real browser + measured UX audit). Motivated by a 2026-06-09 live-browser look at the shipped spine (the agent run rendered through the unified window): structurally correct, visually under-developed.

### §16.1 Genre placement — the spine is NOT a debug waterfall and NOT a fixed wizard

The research found two adjacent genres the spine must NOT drift into:
- **The developer trace-timeline** (LangSmith / Honeycomb "Agent Timeline" / AgentLens / Maxim) — dense nested **waterfall** spans, latency bars, force-graphs, built to expose EVERYTHING for debugging. Our spine is user-facing **co-presence** ("show the work, hide the plumbing" — the §3.A inversion); it must SUMMARISE, not expose. A spine that grows latency bars and nested spans has drifted into the wrong genre.
- **The fixed-length form wizard** (the classic 3–6-step Material/PatternFly stepper) — assumes a KNOWN, bounded, linear set of steps with backward navigation. Our run is **append-only and open-ended** (unknown step count, no "go back"); the wizard's "limit to 3–6 steps" rule does **not** apply — density is managed by COLLAPSE, not by capping the count.

The correct genre is a **hybrid of four established patterns**, each contributing exactly one property:
1. **Progress/timeline stepper** → the *node-state semantics* (PatternFly's 7 states, below).
2. **Git commit graph** → the *dot-and-line spine aesthetic* — a continuous vertical connector threading state-coded nodes, branch/parallel-capable (for sub-agent fan-out).
3. **Scroll-spy reading-position rail** → the *sticky active-on-view* behaviour + click-to-scroll navigation.
4. **2026 co-presence agent UI** (AG-UI's auto-collapse of terminal steps; §14) → *emphasise the live moment, collapse the routine*.

### §16.2 The canonical anatomy + the state model

A well-formed vertical spine has four parts — **indicator (node) · connector (line) · label · optional description** — with **state-coded nodes**. PatternFly's progress-stepper 7-state model maps onto the run lifecycle, and the node's TONE is a read of the ONE §3.B status-tone authority (not a per-node colour choice):

| Spine node state | Run lifecycle | Glyph + tone (read from §3.B) |
|---|---|---|
| Pending | queued | hollow ring · dim/neutral |
| In-progress / current | running tool / streaming | **alive** (pulse/spinner) · brightest · info tone · full label |
| Completed | tool done | filled + check · success/settled tone |
| Failure | error | ✕ · danger tone |
| Warning | degraded / partial | warning glyph · warning tone |
| Denied (ours) | rejected approval | ⊘ · muted-danger tone |

**Microcopy is a projection too — and it is where the spine is weakest.** PatternFly's rule: **present-participle while running** ("Searching your files…", "Reading 3 sources…"), **specific past tense when done** ("Searched 5 files", "Denied file write"), **specific past for errors** ("Couldn't reach the model"). The shipped spine shows ALL-CAPS technical labels ("STARTING AGENT SESSION", "CALLING LLM") — machine state, not human co-presence. The correct label is a **microcopy projection of the event kind** (one mapper, the sibling of `composeToolLabel` the spine lacks), not raw event names.

### §16.3 The correct visual state — dimension by dimension

1. **Status-encoded nodes, not bare dots.** Each node's glyph + tone reads the ONE §3.B status-tone authority: queued ◦ / running ◌-pulse / done ✓ / denied ⊘ / error ✕ — **icon AND colour**, never colour-alone (a11y + the §3.B "no status without its tone token" gate).
2. **A connector that reads as a spine.** A continuous vertical line threads the nodes; traversed segment solid, the live edge lighter/animated. The shipped connector is faint — the "spine" barely reads as one; the calibration is a legible continuous thread (the git-graph rail).
3. **Prominence grading made legible.** The active node + the run's terminal node are emphasised (larger, brighter, full label); routine done steps recede to **ambient** ticks under a count ("2 steps · 1 denied"). This is the §3.C auto-collapse / co-presence principle — important moments stand out, the routine recedes. §13 grades by primary/ambient/terminal; this pass sharpens the CONTRAST between the tiers so the grading is readable, not subtle.
4. **Scroll-spy = navigation, not decoration.** The in-view run carries the active ring (shipped); the calibration adds **click-the-node → scroll-to-that-turn**, so the spine is a *minimap* of the conversation (the reading-position-indicator pattern fully realised).
5. **Whole-conversation scope, git-graph shape.** One spine spanning all turns, each run a node-cluster (shipped as §13); the visual BINDING to the column is tightened so the spine reads as attached to the reading column, not floating (§13.7 fixed the symmetric margin; this fixes the perceived attachment).
6. **Motion with restraint.** The running node is subtly alive (pulse/spin), settling to a check on completion; honour `prefers-reduced-motion` (static fallback — the 559 reduced-motion guard already in the codebase).
7. **Responsive / compact.** At rest a thin gutter; narrow widths fold to a single status dot or off-canvas (the §13 `OverflowController`/adaptive primitive) — matching the "compact stepper for space-constrained areas" guidance.
8. **Accessibility.** The spine is a labelled list/nav; each node's accessible name = status + label ("Completed: searched 5 files"); focus-visible; not colour-only (the §3.B tone-token gate + the 559 a11y-closure landmark gate already cover these).

### §16.4 The shipped spine — observed visual state + critical gap analysis (live, 2026-06-09)

**What it actually renders today.** A thin far-left gutter of small, low-contrast grey text: a per-run HEADER as a terse count (`• 2 steps · 1 denied`, `• 1 step · 1 denied · 2 errors`); sub-step lines in ALL-CAPS machine event-names (`STARTING AGENT SESSION`, `CALLING LLM`); nodes that are a `•` bullet / tiny tick, with a single STATIC amber dot on the active step; a barely-visible hairline connector; near-monochrome grey throughout; collapsing to a count at rest. The STRUCTURE is right (per-run, collapsible, scroll-spy-linked — §13); the SURFACE is where it falls short. The deficits, ranked worst-encoding first:

1. **Status is shown as a text COUNT (`1 denied · 2 errors`), not as node state — the weakest possible encoding.** A spine's entire value is *glanceability*; a count forces READING, not scanning, and you cannot tell WHICH step failed or ran from the nodes themselves. This is the §1 "status text is colourless / `AgentProgress.severity` dangling" defect recurring at the very leaf the §3.B status-tone authority exists to fix.
2. **Bare dots — no per-status glyph.** Running / done / denied / error all look identical (a dot). The PatternFly 7-state model is entirely absent; the node — the primary visual unit of a spine — carries almost no information.
3. **Near-monochrome grey — the §3.B tone authority is not read.** A denied/error step renders the same grey as a routine done step; the only colour is the active amber dot, which is itself COLOUR-ONLY (no glyph — an a11y regression). The tone tokens exist; the spine ignores them.
4. **ALL-CAPS machine labels (`CALLING LLM`) instead of human present-participle microcopy.** Internal telemetry surfaced to a user — the OPPOSITE of co-presence, and it drifts the spine toward the developer-debug-log genre §16.1 says to avoid. "CALLING LLM" tells the user nothing about what is happening *for them*.
5. **Faint hairline connector — it does not read as a spine.** Without a legible connector the discrete events read as a STACK OF GREY LABELS, not one continuous run (the "what is this graph called?" tell — it does not read as a graph/timeline at all).
6. **Static active dot — the live moment is not alive.** A motionless dot under-sells the single most important thing a run-spine communicates (the agent is working *now*); the PatternFly in-progress state + 2026 co-presence both want a living indicator (pulse/spinner).
7. **Prominence grading invisible.** The §13 primary/ambient/terminal grading exists in code but not in perception — uniform small grey means nothing pops; the active and terminal moments do not stand out.
8. **Detached gutter.** The spine floats far-left, visually disconnected from the answer it annotates — the node↔turn relationship is ambiguous (the git-graph rail should hug its content; §13.7 fixed the symmetric margin, not the perceived attachment).

**The meta-defect (why it is theoretically worse, not merely unpolished).** The spine is the ONE place in the unified window where two things the project ALREADY BUILT are both left visually unused: the **§3.B status-tone authority** (tone tokens present; the spine renders grey) AND the **co-presence principle** (labels are machine telemetry, not human narration). It is therefore not *under-built for lack of data* — `UnifiedTurnItem` / run events carry the step kind and status, and §3.B carries the tone — it is **under-PROJECTED**: it reads the existing record into the WEAKEST visual form (grey text + a count) instead of the strongest (glyph + tone + human label + living connector). That places the shipped spine on the WRONG SIDE of the §16.1 genre line — a terse debug-log when the substrate for a co-presence rail is already in hand.

### §16.5 The authority framing — the fix is calibration, not a re-model (no new kernel)

> **Superseded in part by §17 (2026-06-09).** This subsection framed the fix as "presentation calibration + one tiny microcopy projection, no new authority." A subsequent codebase investigation (3 Explore passes + tempdoc 559) found that framing **too small**: the spine is one of ≥5 run-step render sites that each hand-author the step's glyph/label/prominence/bundle ad-hoc (only the *tone* facet is projected, via `statusTone`), so the correct structure is a genuine new authority — the **run-step presentation projection** (§17), of which the spine's visual fix is a consequence. Per the dated-history discipline, **§17 wins where it differs from the "no new authority" claim below.** The token-calibration framing (node sizes, connector weight, motion timings as implementation-time tuning) remains correct.

Every deficit in §16.4 is a **presentation calibration of the existing projection**, kernel-consistent:
- the node TONE is a read of the ONE §3.B status-tone authority (no new scorer);
- the node LABEL is a microcopy projection of the event kind — the **one genuinely-new (but tiny) addition**: the spine's missing label-authority, the analog of the tool-card's `composeToolLabel` (§12.3.B);
- the connector / prominence / motion / responsive behaviours are pure CSS-token calibration of the §13 generated zone.

**No new authority and no new gate are earned.** The spine already rides the §3.B tone gate (no status without its token) and the 559 a11y-closure gate (landmarks + not-colour-only). The single structural add is the **microcopy projection** (event-kind → human present-participle/past label); everything else is token/CSS calibration. **Residual (named, not a design unknown):** the exact visual tokens — node sizes, connector weight, prominence contrast ratios, motion timings — are an implementation-time calibration validated in the real browser + a measured UX audit (§9). This is the §13-tier analog of §14's "render trails the substrate" finding: the spine's *structure* is at bar; its *visual state* is the one place it trails, and the fix is projection/token-tier, not a re-model.

### §16.6 Sources (2026-06-09)
- Node-state model + microcopy (present-participle / specific-past) + vertical-orientation (split-view) + compact density: **PatternFly Progress stepper design guidelines** (`patternfly.org/components/progress-stepper/design-guidelines`).
- Stepper anatomy (indicator/connector/label/description) + vertical-vs-horizontal + connector semantics (solid vs dashed): **Lollypop "Beyond the Progress Bar"** (`lollypop.design`); **Eleken "32 Stepper UI Examples"** (`eleken.co`); **Setproduct "Stepper UI design: States, behavior, best practices"** (`setproduct.com`); **Material steppers** (`m1.material.io/components/steppers`).
- The developer-trace genre to NOT become: **LangSmith/LangGraph trace timeline** (`docs.langchain.com`); **Honeycomb "Agent Timeline"** (`honeycomb.io/blog/agent-timeline-flight-recorder-for-your-ai-agents`); **AgentLens** (`medium.com/@satyaraj.479`).
- Git-graph dot-and-line aesthetic: **commit-graph drawing algorithms** (`pvigier.github.io/2019/05/06/commit-graph-drawing-algorithms`); **Git Graph for VS Code** (`marketplace.visualstudio.com`).
- Scroll-spy reading-position rail: **CSS-Tricks "Reading Position Indicator"** (`css-tricks.com`).
- Co-presence-over-autonomy framing: the §14 sources (AG-UI; CopilotKit generative-UI).

## §17 The correct design — the run-step presentation authority (the spine is one leaf of it)

Design theory (2026-06-09): the correct long-term structure for the issue §16 researched, with feasibility disregarded and major re-seats in scope. The goal is **not** the spine's visual fix as such — it is the **structure that makes the whole defect-class unrepresentable**, of which the spine fix falls out. A codebase investigation (3 Explore passes + tempdoc 559) **supersedes §16.5's "calibration, no new authority" conclusion**: the correct design is a genuine new authority — *one run-step presentation projection* — that **extends** the existing engine (559) and authorities (§3.B, Display, `composeToolLabel`, `prominenceFor`, §12's `UnifiedTurnItem`); it invents no new kernel.

### §17.1 The corrected diagnosis — the spine is a SYMPTOM; the disease is the forked run-step *presentation* leaf

The investigation corrected §16's read of the shipped code:
- The spine is **already** a projection of the one run projection (`UnifiedChatView.renderRunSpine` reads `mergedTimeline()` → `UnifiedTurnItem[]`, the *same* source the conversation body reads) and **already** reads the §3.B tone authority (`statusTone.ts` `statusAccent`). It is *not* a model fork and *not* "monochrome / ignores §3.B" — its node is a tiny status-tinted dot.
- The ALL-CAPS "STARTING AGENT SESSION / CALLING LLM" §16.4 attributed to the spine is **not** the spine — it is the *in-body run-trace rows* (`renderTraceNode`, progress items), a *different* render site.

The real defect is one tier deeper and **broader than the spine**: there is **no run-step presentation authority.** `statusTone.ts` (§3.B) unified exactly ONE facet — the *tone*. But a run step's **glyph, its human label/microcopy, its prominence→visual mapping, and its "alive" indicator are re-assembled ad-hoc at every render site** that presents a step: `renderRunSpine` (the spine node), `renderTraceNode` (the in-body trace row), `ToolCallCard` (the card header), `RetrospectivePanel` (the drawer row), and the presence inbox. Concretely: there is **no status→glyph authority at all** (only `NavigationReceipt` has an ad-hoc outcome→glyph for URLs), and the label authority `composeToolLabel` is **tool-card-only** (the spine has its own a11y-label switch; progress/error labels are raw content).

This is, verbatim, **tempdoc 559's named disease**: *"the single-authority projection kernel is half-applied to presentation — element membership and typed-value facets are projected, but the rendered presentation itself is hand-authored in templates and therefore drifts and can only be grep-checked."* 559's §4 authority table already declares the relevant facets of the ONE engine — **Display = accessible name + ICON ← `present()`**, **Messaging = tone × severity**, **Theme = color** — each projected from one declaration. The run-step is simply the **element where that engine was never run** for its glyph / label / bundle facets. And it is another instance of the §15.E meta-principle: §3.B unified the *tone-trunk*, but the run-step *presentation* leaf was reached by **neither a typed seam nor a register**, so — exactly as §15 found for the grounding leaf — it forked across sites.

### §17.2 The correct structure — one run-step presentation projection (`StepPresentation`)

A single projector derives a **complete presentation view-model for any run step** from its declaration (`UnifiedTurnItem` kind + status):

```
StepPresentation = { tone, glyph, label, prominence, liveness }
```

Each facet **extends an authority that already exists** — this is the 559 engine running one more pass over one more element, not a new system:

| Facet | Source authority (extend, don't invent) | State today |
|---|---|---|
| **tone** | §3.B `statusTone` / `toneAccent` | EXISTS — the one tone authority; unchanged |
| **glyph** | a status→glyph sibling — the lifecycle-status analog of 559's **Display "name + ICON"** facet | **MISSING** — the genuinely-new facet (✓ done · spinner running · ✕ error · ⊘ denied · ◦ pending) |
| **label** | `composeToolLabel` **generalised** to a run-step microcopy projection over *every* kind | partial — tool-card-only today; generalise to present-participle (running) / specific-past (done) / specific-past (error) |
| **prominence** | §12.3.C `prominenceFor` | EXISTS — unchanged |
| **liveness** | `status === running` | trivial — drives the "alive" indicator |

**Every run-step surface composes this ONE descriptor through a shared run-node primitive** — the analog of `jf-tool-call-card` for the tool row. The spine threads node-primitives on a connector; the in-body trace row, the card header, the drawer row, and the presence row render the *same* descriptor. **No surface hand-authors a glyph, a tone, or a label** — they read the projection. The result: one similarity of "how a run step looks" across every place a step appears, by construction (the same collapse §3.A/§15.B achieved for the answer, applied to the step).

### §17.3 Anti-drift — the long-term prevention (the 548 ladder + 559's "project off the template")

The defect persisted because the presentation was hand-authored, reaching only ladder tier-1 (collapse to a primitive) + tier-4 (a grep-gate) — 559's diagnosed ceiling. The correct structure moves the seam **off the template**, the way 559 prescribes, so the *strongest* tiers become reachable:

1. **Tier-2 (unrepresentable-by-type), now reachable.** The descriptor is a typed value and the **run-node primitive only accepts a `StepPresentation`** — a renderer literally *cannot* draw a run-step node without going through the projection. A hand-rolled `<div>` with a bespoke status dot does not type-check against the primitive's contract. This is the §15.D.1 typed-seam idea applied to the step element (and, unlike the grounding *tier* which was a soft string-union, the step-node primitive's prop is a genuine opaque type — the brand bites here).
2. **Tier-4 register-gate (the §15.J pattern), as the backstop the type can't reach.** A `run-renderers.v1.json` sibling (or a new `step-presentation` facet) declares the ONE `StepPresentation` projector + the ONE run-node primitive + the surfaces allowed to render a step: **positive coverage** (every run-step surface composes the descriptor / mounts the primitive) + a **literal-scan** (no hand-rolled status glyph/tone/label — e.g. no `? '✓' : '✕'`, no `var(--accent-*)` on a step node — outside the authority), exactly the two checks §15.J's `groundingSemantics` gate already runs. Re-forking a run-step presentation becomes a **build failure**, not a future audit finding.

### §17.4 The spine's correct visual state as a consequence (not as the goal)

Adopting the descriptor + the run-node primitive + a legible connector yields *exactly* the §16.3 correct visual state — glyph+tone nodes, human present-participle labels, a living active node, readable prominence — **and** fixes the in-body trace, the tool-card, the drawer, and the presence row **at the same time, by construction**, because they now share one projection. The §16 "calibration" would have fixed the spine alone and left the other four sites to drift independently; the §17 structure fixes the *class*. This is why the correct design is the authority, not the calibration.

### §17.5 Reuse boundary, residual, and the meta-principle (honest accounting)

- **Reuses / extends (unchanged or generalised):** 559's projection engine (§4) and prevention ladder (§5); §3.B `statusTone`/`toneAccent` (tone); 559's Display ICON facet (the glyph's home); `composeToolLabel` (the label, generalised); §12.3.C `prominenceFor` (prominence); §12's `UnifiedTurnItem` (the input declaration) + `mergedTimeline` (the one ordered source).
- **Genuinely new (small, bounded):** the status→glyph facet; the run-step microcopy generalisation of `composeToolLabel`; the `StepPresentation` bundle + the run-node primitive; the register-gate. **No new kernel.**
- **Residual (named, not a design unknown):** the exact visual TOKENS — node sizes, connector weight, prominence contrast ratios, motion timings — remain an implementation-time calibration validated in the real browser + a measured UX audit (§9, the §13.8 stale-dist + worktree-Vite lessons apply).
- **Meta-principle (the long-term lesson, §15.E for this leaf):** a unification is complete only when its leaves are unforkable. §3.B unified the tone-trunk but did not reach the *presentation* leaf with a seam or a register, so it forked across five sites — the same shape as the grounding leaf §15 closed. The cure is the same shape too: **a typed seam (the `StepPresentation` the primitive demands) + a positive-coverage register-gate.** The general rule this adds: *when an authority unifies ONE facet of an element's presentation (here, tone), the remaining facets (glyph, label, prominence, liveness) are themselves leaves — bundle them into one projected descriptor and reach every render site through it, or they will each drift on their own.*

### §17.6 Validation discipline (unchanged, §9)

Every user-visible piece of any eventual implementation is declared done only on a **freshly-built dist in the real browser** (the §10/§13.8 stale-dist + worktree-Vite-roots-at-canonical lessons), with a **measured** whole-screen UX audit (axe / contrast oracle, auditor ≠ committer) — never on green unit tests alone. The anti-drift teeth (§17.3) are validated the §15.J way: the gate must pass on the authority AND **fail on a planted fork** (a hand-rolled status dot), green on revert.

### §17.G De-risk pass (2026-06-09) — verifies §17's load-bearing assumptions against source + a live probe, and CORRECTS §17.2 / §17.3

Before any implementation, §17's six load-bearing assumptions were verified against shipped code (`file:line`) + a live session-event probe (`/api/chat/sessions/{id}/events`). The **DIAGNOSIS is CONFIRMED and strengthened**; the **PRESCRIPTION is REFINED in four places**. As with §15.G / §10 / §13.6, the later section wins where it differs.

- **Site fork — CONFIRMED + strengthened (assumption 2).** The hand-authored tone-lookup `const color = status ? statusAccent(status) : 'var(--border-subtle)'` appears **verbatim and identical** at `UnifiedChatView.renderRunSpine:1511` AND `renderTraceNode:2026` — a literal copy-paste fork — plus `renderUnifiedItem` progress (`statusAccent(sev):2123`), `ToolCallCard` (status-word colour, `:34`), and `RetrospectivePanel` (`outcomeToTone`). **Five sites read the §3.B tone; NONE renders a glyph** (no status→glyph anywhere in the FE — only `NavigationReceipt` has an ad-hoc outcome→glyph for URLs). The fork is real and literal, not inferred.

- **Glyph facet — CORRECTED (assumption 1; a wrong-axis fix).** §17.2 framed the glyph as "extending 559's Display `present()` icon." Source refutes the framing: (a) `present.ts:45` declares `Presented.icon?` but **no `present()` case ever populates it** — a declared-but-empty slot; and (b) `present()` is keyed by an **EntityRef** (operation/surface/effect…), whereas a run-step glyph is keyed by **lifecycle status** — a *different axis* (status is not an `EntityRef` kind). So the glyph belongs NOT inside `present()` but as a **sibling of §3.B `statusTone`** — a `statusGlyph(status)` alongside `statusToTone(status)` in `statusTone.ts`, so glyph + tone are two facets of the ONE status authority. Crucially this **aligns with an existing backend model**: `AgentEvent.AgentProgress` already carries a `severity` (INFO/WARN/ERROR) whose stated purpose (561 #5, `AgentEvent.java:235-254`) is *"decorate a progress line by intent rather than tagging every routine phase with a warning glyph — routine phases (session start, 'Calling LLM') are INFO (no glyph)."* The glyph facet must therefore be **intentionally SPARSE** (routine INFO = quiet/no decorative glyph; running = alive; WARN/ERROR/done/denied = glyph) — a "glyph on every node" would CONTRADICT a deliberate design.

- **Label facet — REFINED (assumption 3; smaller than theorized).** The step labels are **backend-emitted `AgentProgress.message` content**, already sentence-case human — `AgentLoopService.java:550` "Starting agent session", `AgentStepRunner.java:267` "Calling LLM" — **confirmed live on the wire** (`progress.payload.message = "Starting agent session" / "Calling LLM"`, no `severity` → INFO). So the "ALL-CAPS machine label" defect (§16.4) is a **FE CSS `text-transform: uppercase`** over sentence-case human content, NOT raw event names. The run-step microcopy authority is thus a **FE transform/polish** (drop the uppercasing + present-participle the verbs) over backend content + `composeToolLabel` for tool steps — *smaller* than "project a label from event-kind from scratch." (Refines §16.4's "machine labels" wording too.)

- **Status data — REFINED (assumption 6).** Live + source: `tool-activity` carries `status` (unioned proposed→pending→completed/rejected, `unifiedThreadProjection.ts:96-110`); `progress` carries `severity` (default INFO when omitted — confirmed absent on the routine-phase wire); `user`/`assistant`/`error` carry NO explicit status — `renderRunSpine` **infers** them (assistant→completed, error→rejected). The data is present for the meaningful kinds, and **the per-kind status inference is itself ad-hoc logic in `renderRunSpine`** that the descriptor should OWN (one more facet to centralize) — confirming the descriptor's value.

- **Anti-drift tier — CORRECTED (assumption 4; the §15.D.1 lesson, again).** §17.3 claimed the typed `StepPresentation` makes the node "unrepresentable-by-type (tier-2) — the brand bites here." Source refutes the *strength*: `ToolCallCard.toolCall: ToolCall | null` where `ToolCall` is a **plain interface** (`ToolCallCard.ts:28,45`) — a consumer can fabricate one; a Lit prop typed as a plain interface is **soft (gate-primary)**, exactly the §15.D.1/§15.J finding. Tier-2 is reachable **only if `StepPresentation` (or its key) is BRANDED** — the `DisplayLabel = string & { __display }` idiom `present.ts:23` already uses, and which §3.B could mint. **Corrected §17.3:** brand the descriptor to reach tier-2 (the `DisplayLabel` idiom); otherwise the type is soft and the **register-gate is the real teeth** (gate-primary, like grounding §15.J). Name both honestly; do not claim type-primacy.

- **Primitive granularity — CORRECTED (assumption 5).** The five sites have genuinely different shapes (a 0.55rem spine dot vs a trace row vs the rich tool-card vs a drawer row). The correct structure is therefore **one shared `StepPresentation` descriptor + surface-appropriate primitives** (a lightweight run-node for the spine; a row for the trace; the existing `jf-tool-call-card` ADOPTS the descriptor for its status glyph/label) — NOT "one run-node primitive for everything." **Corrected §17.2's** "one run-node primitive (the jf-tool-call-card analog)."

**Net confidence after the pass.** *Diagnosis:* **HIGH** — the fork is literal (identical `statusAccent` lines at `:1511`/`:2026`), and the absence of any status→glyph authority is confirmed. *Prescription:* **HIGH for the shape** (one `StepPresentation` descriptor every site composes) and the **reuse boundary** (a §3.B sibling for glyph + the backend severity model + `composeToolLabel` + `prominenceFor` + `UnifiedTurnItem`), with the four corrections folded in: glyph is a `statusTone` sibling (not `present()`'s icon), sparse-by-intent; label is a transform over backend content; the descriptor owns the per-kind status inference; anti-drift is brand(`DisplayLabel`)+register-gate, honestly gate-primary unless branded; and it is one descriptor + surface primitives. No production code, schema, or test was changed in this pass — the output is verified confidence + these §17.2/§17.3/§16.4 corrections.

### §17.H Implementation outcome (2026-06-09) — the run-step presentation authority SHIPPED (static-green; live verification batched)

§17 is implemented, with the §17.G corrections folded in. Built in this worktree; NOT merged.

- **§17.A the authority + projection — SHIPPED.** `statusTone.ts` gained two SIBLINGS of `statusToTone`: **`statusGlyph(status): StepGlyph`** (sparse-by-intent — routine/info ⇒ `none`, running ⇒ `running`, the decisive states ⇒ `done`/`denied`/`error`/`warn`; aligned with the backend `AgentProgress.severity` model, 561 #5) and **`glyphChar(glyph): string`** (the ONE glyph-token → display-char map — `✓`/`⊘`/`✕`/`!`, the place the chars live). A new `views/runStepPresentation.ts` projects a **branded `StepPresentation` `{ tone, glyph, label, prominence, live }`** from a `UnifiedTurnItem` — the ONLY mint (the `DisplayLabel`-idiom brand, the §17.G tier-2 seam) — and OWNS the per-kind status inference once hand-rolled in `renderRunSpine` (with the §17.G correction: an `error` item is `error` ✕, a `rejected` tool is `denied` ⊘ — distinct glyphs the old spine conflated). The label reuses `composeToolLabel` for tool steps and the backend's already-human `AgentProgress` message for progress (no CSS-uppercasing). +7 `runStepPresentation`/`statusGlyph` unit tests.
- **§17.B the primitive + adoption — SHIPPED.** A new `<jf-run-node>` (`components/chat/RunNode.ts`) renders a `StepPresentation` — a decisive-state char (via `glyphChar`) or a CSS shape (dot / hollow ring / pulsing dot for none / pending / running), tone-coloured via `toneAccent`, with a `prefers-reduced-motion` guard. **Every run-step surface now composes it:** `renderRunSpine` and `renderTraceNode` mount `<jf-run-node>` (the byte-identical forked `statusAccent` lines deleted; `statusAccent` no longer imported by `UnifiedChatView`); `ToolCallCard` takes a `.stepPresentation` and mounts the node (its `running` glyph REPLACES the bespoke `<jf-pulse-dots>` — one alive-indicator everywhere). The spine connector was made legible (2px) and the nodes became sized disc-wrappers; the CSS-uppercased `.message-shape-tag` progress/handoff labels were replaced with plain-human `.trace-label`. **A second status-glyph site was subsumed (the structural / never-descope choice):** the advisory inbox's hand-rolled `v === 'SUCCESS' ? '✓' : '✕'` (`AdvisoryInboxDrawer.ts`) now reads `glyphChar(statusGlyph(…))` — the gate *found* this fork, and rather than scope it out, the authority was extended to own it.
- **§17.C the anti-drift gate — SHIPPED + proven.** `run-renderers.v1.json` gained a `stepPresentation` facet + `check-run-renderers.mjs` three checks: (8) only registered `toneSites` import the status authority symbols; (9) only registered `nodeSites` mount `<jf-run-node>`; (10) no file but the primitive hand-rolls a status-glyph char as a ternary. **Proven the §15.J way:** the gate PASSES on the authority and goes RED on a planted fork (all three checks fired on a scratch file), GREEN on revert.
- **§17.G corrections, as-built:** glyph is a `statusTone` sibling (not `present()`'s never-populated entity-icon); the brand is the typed seam, the register-gate the real backstop (honestly gate-primary); the label is a transform over backend content; one descriptor + surface-appropriate primitives (the rich `jf-tool-call-card` *adopts* the descriptor rather than being replaced).

**Verification (static, all green):** FE `npm run typecheck` clean; **FE unit suite 2458 tests pass** (248 files; +7 new); the `run-renderers` gate PASS + RED-on-planted-fork + GREEN-on-revert; the 11 presentation gates green except the pre-existing 568 `--font-body` token red (`TokenEditorPlugin.ts`, unrelated); `./gradlew.bat build -x test` green (class-size pass).

**Live-browser verification (2026-06-09, worktree Vite :5190 → model-backed canonical backend :57871, Meta-Llama-3.1-8B online).** A real agent run was driven; the §17 render is **confirmed live** — the worktree FE served the new code (the changes below exist only in it):
- **Human present-participle labels, not ALL-CAPS.** The trace renders "**Starting agent session**" and "**Calling LLM**" in sentence case — the CSS-`text-transform: uppercase` defect (§16.4) is gone (was "STARTING AGENT SESSION" / "CALLING LLM").
- **Glyph nodes** — routine progress steps render as filled dots (glyph `none`, neutral tone); the pending tool step renders as a **hollow ring (○)** (glyph `pending`) — the §17 glyph differentiation, live.
- **The tool-card ADOPTED the descriptor** — the same hollow-ring pending glyph renders in the `<jf-tool-call-card>` header (before "MEDIUM · PENDING"), i.e. the card shows the SAME glyph the trace does (Phase 2 cross-surface adoption, live).
- **The connector** reads as one thread (the trace's vertical rule).

**Honest scope of the live pass:** (a) the spine *gutter* (the far-left minimap) is `@media (min-width: 64rem)` and the MCP browser viewport caps below that, so the spine rendered its nodes inline (as the trace) rather than as a separate gutter — same `renderRunSpine → stepPresentation → <jf-run-node>` code path, not separately framed; (b) the `done` ✓ / `error` ✕ / running-pulse glyphs were not captured live because the 8B dev model repeatedly chose a gated `core_ingest_files` write (which can't *complete* on the worktree-FE + canonical-backend hybrid — the FE posts the §15.J `/api/chat/approve` the canonical backend retired) or hallucinated a 0-tool answer; those glyphs are pinned by the 7 unit tests + the `glyphChar` authority (and the advisory inbox now renders ✓/✕ through it). Net: the marquee §17 render (human labels + glyph nodes + cross-surface adoption + connector) is **live-confirmed**; the residual glyphs are unit-pinned, the spine-gutter is viewport-capped — both stated, not papered over.

## §18 The ④/⑤ grounding-honesty signals — SHIPPED (2026-06-09, static-green)

The two longest-standing named residuals (§14/§15.A — ④ a grounding-readiness signal, ⑤ an "N of M sentences grounded" coverage indicator) are implemented, exactly as the design dissolved them: **ONE read of the one §15.A grounding verdict**, not a new signal bolted on. A `groundingCoverage(citations, answerText)` projection was added to the grounding authority (`evidenceProjection.ts`) — it classifies each answer-sentence cite through the ONE `groundingClass` (no second classifier) and returns `{ ready (④), grounded, weak, cited (N), total (M), label }`; `countSentences` gives the best-effort M. `UnifiedChatView` renders a **grounding badge beside the answer** (record + live agent paths) — "Grounded · N of M sentences" — making the answer's grounding explicit rather than buried (the §14 honesty rule). **Verification:** +4 `evidenceProjection` coverage tests (13 total in that file); FE `typecheck` clean + **2462 unit tests pass**; `check-run-renderers` (the grounding gate still green — `groundingCoverage` reads `groundingClass` IN-file, adds no out-of-authority classifier) + `check-color-tokens` + `check-controls-a11y` + a11y/presentation gates green. **Residual (honest):** M is a prose heuristic (an honesty HINT, not an exact metric, by design); the "Not grounded" *explicit* state for a sources-less agent answer is scoped to absence-of-badge for now (the grounded path is the shipped case); live-browser confirmation of the badge wants a grounded answer on a citation-scorer-loaded stack (the dev scorer is offline) — the same env limit as the §15.A calibration. The one item that remains genuinely blocked here is the **§15.A tier-number calibration** (needs the production cross-encoder distribution, unavailable in this dev env).

## §19 Density-adaptive run-step representation (design theory → SHIPPED §19.H, 2026-06-09) — the Adaptivity authority's missing FILL half

Design theory: the correct long-term structure for the issue a **live look at the shipped §17 spine** exposed — and the structure that prevents the class. Feasibility disregarded; major re-seats in scope; extends existing authorities (559's Adaptivity, the §17 `StepPresentation`, the §13 spatial tier, `prominenceFor`), invents no new kernel. The goal is NOT a node-size tweak; it is to make a step ALWAYS render legibly at every scale, by construction.

### §19.1 The corrected diagnosis — §17 unified the SEMANTICS but not the SCALE

Driving a real run and forcing the wide layout on (§17's spine gutter is `≥64rem`-only) showed: the spine gutter renders, the scroll-spy active ring works, the connector threads, the tone shows — **but the §17 glyph (✓/⊘/✕) is illegible at the gutter scale.** The gutter nodes are 0.3–0.8rem (`RunNode` renders one fixed glyph/shape, scaled only by the parent em — no container adaptation), so the glyph collapses to a tiny tone-dot; the glyph richness only pays off in the bigger in-body trace + the tool-card. The routine (`ambient`) nodes (opacity 0.45) are nearly invisible.

§17 unified the run-step's **SEMANTICS** — the `StepPresentation` descriptor `{ tone, glyph, label, prominence, live }` is the one authority every step-surface composes. But it did **not** reach the **SCALE / DENSITY** of the rendering: the node primitive draws the *same* representation (the glyph) at every size, so the smallest scale (the gutter) renders illegibly. This is tempdoc **559's disease one dimension over**: a hand-authored presentation property — *the element's representation at a given size* — that the projection engine never owned. And it is, specifically, the **unrealized half of 559's Adaptivity authority**: 559 §4 declares Adaptivity as *"overflow + **fill** under constrained space ← the item registry's declared priority/policy."* The OVERFLOW half is built (`primitives/adaptiveBar.ts` `OverflowController` — which leading items fit a bar — + `governance/adaptive-regions.v1.json` + `check-adaptive-closure.mjs`). The **FILL / DENSITY** half — *how ONE element represents itself at the available size* — is **unbuilt** (investigation: "NO multi-density / multi-scale rendering concept exists; each item renders one fixed representation"). The run-step node is where that gap bit. It is also the §15.E/§17 meta-principle extended with a NEW dimension: a unification of an element's semantics is incomplete until its rendering is legible at every SCALE it appears.

### §19.2 The correct structure — density-adaptive representation (the FILL half, completed)

An element that renders at multiple scales **declares a representation ladder by density** — `minimal` (a dot / icon only) → `compact` (glyph + label) → `full` (glyph + label + detail) — and the engine **projects the legible representation for the available size**, exactly the way `OverflowController` projects *which items fit* a bar (a `ResizeObserver` / container query reading the node's box, not a hand-set scale). The run-step node becomes this:

- The §17 `StepPresentation` stays the SEMANTIC authority (unchanged).
- The node primitive renders it at a **declared density**: the spine gutter declares `minimal` → a **tone-dot + the active ring** (the glyph COLLAPSES — there is no illegible glyph; the dot's tone + the ring + the connector position carry the status at minimap scale); the in-body trace declares `compact` → glyph + the human label; the tool-card declares `full` → glyph + label + detail.
- **"A glyph rendered too small to read" becomes UNREPRESENTABLE** — the primitive never draws a sub-legible glyph; below its legible threshold it falls to the dot. The density is declared by the surface OR auto-derived from the container's measured size (the `OverflowController` mechanism, generalised from "which items" to "which representation").

This is the 559 engine's Adaptivity pass completed for the FILL facet, applied to the run-step leaf: one semantic descriptor, rendered at the legible density for each scale, BY PROJECTION — not three hand-tuned representations that drift.

### §19.3 The prominence grading becomes a declared scale (projected, not hand-CSS'd)

Today `prominenceFor` returns a token (`primary`/`secondary`/`ambient`) but the **size + opacity per token are hand-authored CSS** (0.62/0.36/0.3rem, opacity 1/0.65/0.45) — the same "presentation hand-authored, not projected" disease, which is why the ambient nodes read as too faint. The correct structure projects prominence → **(size, contrast)** from a DECLARED scale (the §13 "generate, don't hand-author" + 559 "project the fill"), so the contrast is a single tuned, gate-coverable declaration that cannot drift across the spine / trace / card. The density ladder (§19.2) and the prominence scale compose: a node's final size is `densityScale(density) × prominenceScale(prominence)`, both declared.

### §19.4 The spine's spatial form — a §13 spatial-composition decision, named (not defaulted)

The gutter is a compact node-**STACK** (a flex column packed at the top, gap 0.6rem), NOT aligned to its conversation items' scroll positions; the scroll-spy active ring is the ONLY spatial link. So it reads as a status *cluster*, not a spatial minimap. The correct form is a §13-tier decision to NAME, not default: either a true **position-proportional minimap** (each node at its content's scroll fraction, so the spine is a genuine map of the conversation) OR the **accepted compact status-cluster** with the active ring as the deliberate link. Both are defensible; the point is that the choice is a declared spatial-composition decision (the §13 `composeGridStyles` tier owns the frame), not an accident of a flex stack.

### §19.5 Anti-drift — the recurrence cure (extend the Adaptivity gate to DENSITY)

The issue recurs whenever an element renders at multiple scales without a density-adaptive representation. The cure extends the Adaptivity authority's gate (`check-adaptive-closure`, today "overflow only") to also cover **density**: an element rendered at multiple scales must declare its representation ladder + render through the density-adaptive primitive — **no hand-fixed representation that fails at small scale**. A new multi-scale element then *cannot* hand-render an illegible-small glyph; "illegible-at-scale" becomes a build failure. This is the 548 ladder (Collapse > Unrepresentable > Generate > Gate) applied to the density facet — the same shape as the §15.J / §17 register-gates.

### §19.6 Reuse boundary + meta-principle

- **Reuses / extends:** 559's Adaptivity authority (`OverflowController` + `adaptive-regions.v1.json` + `check-adaptive-closure`), the §17 `StepPresentation` descriptor + the `jf-run-node` primitive, the §13 spatial-composition tier (`composeGridStyles`), `prominenceFor`.
- **Genuinely new (small):** the density-ladder declaration (`minimal`/`compact`/`full`) + the density-adaptive primitive behaviour (project the legible representation for the measured size) + the gate's density coverage + the prominence→(size,contrast) declared scale.
- **No new kernel.** Meta-principle (extending §15.E/§17): **a unification of an element's SEMANTICS is incomplete until its rendering is legible at every SCALE it appears** — reach each scale with a declared density-representation, or the smallest scale renders illegibly. The §17 leaf had one more dimension — *scale* — the semantic unification did not reach; this names and closes it.
- **Validation discipline (unchanged, §9):** any eventual implementation is declared done only on a freshly-built dist in the real browser at the relevant breakpoint(s) + a measured UX audit — the discipline whose absence let the §17 spine ship with an illegible-gutter glyph in the first place (the live look that produced this section was that audit, after the fact).

### §19.H Implementation outcome (2026-06-09) — density-adaptive representation SHIPPED (static-green; live verification batched)

§19.2–§19.5 are implemented, exactly as the design theory framed them. Built in this worktree; NOT merged. No new kernel — the FILL half of 559's Adaptivity authority + the §17 descriptor + the §13 spine, extended.

- **§19.2 the density primitive — SHIPPED.** A new `primitives/adaptiveDensity.ts` is the FILL-half SIBLING of `adaptiveBar.ts`: a `RunNodeDensity` ladder (`minimal`/`compact`/`full`), the declared legibility thresholds (`GLYPH_LEGIBLE_PX = 11`, calibrated to the run-step surfaces — the trace node ~11.5px reads, the gutter ambient nodes ~5–6px do not), a PURE `representationFor(measuredPx, declared)` decision (effective = `min(declared, sizeAfforded)`; unmeasured → the declared density verbatim, so jsdom/SSR never blank), and a `DensityController` ReactiveController owning a `ResizeObserver` (rAF-deferred, mirrors `OverflowController`). +7 unit tests pin the decision (small→minimal; legible→compact; detail→full; legibility CAPS a `full` declared on a tiny box → minimal — the backstop; the declared density is a CEILING a big box never exceeds; unmeasured honours the declared).
- **§19.2 the node self-adapts — SHIPPED.** `RunNode.ts` composes `DensityController` and renders the legible representation for its measured box: at `minimal` a DECISIVE glyph char (`✓/⊘/✕/!`) COLLAPSES to a tone dot (`.g-dot`, the tone already carries success/danger), while the %-sized shape-glyphs (none/pending/running dot/ring/pulse) keep their shape at any scale; at `compact`/`full` the char renders. **"A glyph too small to read" is now unrepresentable** — the primitive never paints a char below `GLYPH_LEGIBLE_PX`. Each surface DECLARES its ceiling via the `density` attribute: the spine gutter `minimal`, the in-body trace `compact`, the tool-card `full`.
- **§19.3 prominence → a declared scale — SHIPPED.** `PROMINENCE_SCALE` + `TERMINAL_NODE_WEIGHT` are declared ONCE in `unifiedThreadProjection.ts` (the size+opacity per prominence, the values formerly hand-CSS'd); the spine projects node size/opacity from them inline, and the four hand-authored `.run-spine-node.prominence-*`/`.terminal` CSS rules are deleted. The node's final box = the declared prominence size; its own `DensityController` then picks the legible representation for that size — the two compose (`densityScale × prominenceScale`).
- **§19.4 the spine is now a position-proportional minimap — SHIPPED (user-chosen form).** `renderRunSpine` was reworked from a top-packed flex STACK to a true minimap: each node is absolutely placed at its conversation item's scroll fraction (`computeSpinePositions` — anchored user/assistant turns at their measured `offsetTop/scrollHeight`, the intra-turn tool/progress/error steps interpolated evenly between the surrounding anchors as texture). A `ResizeObserver` on `.conversation` (`measureSpineFractions`) re-measures on layout change; the scroll-spy `.active` ring + click-jump are unchanged. The `.run-spine` zone became a full-height relative track.
- **§19.5 the anti-drift gate — SHIPPED + proven.** `adaptive-regions.v1.json` gained a `densityPrimitive` + `densityElements` section (run-node); `check-adaptive-closure.mjs` gained the FILL-half pass (D1 the `DensityController` primitive exists; D2 each registered density element composes it — so a new multi-scale element cannot hand-fix one representation that fails small). **Proven the §15.J way:** the gate PASSES on the authority, goes RED on a planted fork (a density element that composes `OverflowController` but not `DensityController`), GREEN on revert.

**Verification (static, all green):** FE `npm run typecheck` clean; **FE unit suite 2469 tests pass** (249 files; +7 new `adaptiveDensity` tests); the `adaptive-closure` gate PASS + RED-on-planted-fork + GREEN-on-revert; `check-run-renderers` + the presentation/a11y/layout/composition gates green except the pre-existing 568 `--font-body` token red (`TokenEditorPlugin.ts`, unrelated). The `UnifiedChatView` spine test was re-targeted (not weakened) from the retired `.prominence-*`/`.terminal` CSS classes to the new DECLARED inline scale (assert the answer carries `--node-size:0.8rem`, the user turn `0.62rem`, the tool step `0.36rem`, and each node a `top:%` placement).

**Live-browser MEASURED UX audit (2026-06-09, worktree Vite :5193 → model-backed canonical backend :60000, Qwen3.5-9B online, viewport 2133px / `matchMedia('(min-width:64rem)')` = true — the spine gutter renders at its real breakpoint).** A real agent run was driven; the §19 render is **confirmed live**:
- **The gutter renders clean tone-dots, not illegible glyph mush.** A measured shadow-DOM probe of the live spine nodes: boxes **2.8–7.9px**, every one resolving `DensityController.density === 'minimal'` and rendering a `.g-none`/`.g-pending` dot/ring (no char) — the cyan active user-node, the amber pending-tool ring, the gray ambient progress dots, threaded by the connector. The in-body trace nodes measure **9.5px → `compact`**, the tool-card **13.6px → `compact`** (the glyph-bearing tiers).
- **The decisive-glyph collapse + the legibility backstop, proven live.** Standalone `<jf-run-node>`s mounted in the running page with an injected `done` (✓) descriptor: at the gutter box (8px, declares `minimal`) → `.g-dot`, **no char** (the ✓ collapses to a tone dot); at the trace box (10px, `compact`) and card box (14px) → the **✓ char renders**; and the BACKSTOP (a `full` declared on a **6px** box) → `.g-dot`, no char — *an illegible-at-scale glyph is unrepresentable by construction*, even when a surface over-declares.
- **The position-proportional minimap + prominence grading read** — nodes placed down the connector at their conversation scroll fraction, size-graded (the cyan active turn largest, the ambient steps smallest).
- **Calibration the audit drove:** the measured trace box is **9.5px** (its 0.72rem disc minus the 1px border), so the initial `GLYPH_LEGIBLE_PX = 11` would have wrongly collapsed the trace's *decisive* glyphs to dots; the live measurement lowered it to **9**, cleanly separating the gutter (≤7.9px → dot) from the trace/card (≥9.5px → glyph). Re-verified green after the change. This is exactly the measured-audit discipline (§19.6) catching a calibration error that eyeballing or unit tests alone would not.
- **Honest scope:** the dev 9B model repeatedly chose a gated `core_ingest_files` write that cannot reconcile on the worktree-FE + canonical-backend hybrid (the same `/api/chat/approve` endpoint gap §17.H noted), so no model-produced `done`/`denied` step was captured *in the spine itself* — the decisive-glyph collapse is proven via the live standalone harness (the actual shipped primitive, running in this browser) + the 7 unit tests, while the real spine nodes' `density==='minimal'` resolution is the live-measured DOM fact. Net: the marquee §19 claim — *the gutter glyph is legible at every scale because the illegible representation is never drawn* — is **live-confirmed**.

### §19.I Residuals, critical-analysis findings, and the cross-tier remaining-work ledger (2026-06-09)

The §19 critical-analysis pass + the live measured audit surfaced these — named, not descoped. They are small relative to the shipped authority; none blocks §19's correctness claim.

**§19's own residuals (this work):**
- **R1 — first-paint density default (a real one-frame correctness gap; one-line fix).** `RunNode.render()` reads `this.densityCtl.density` directly, and the `DensityController` initializes to `'full'` (the field-initializer reads `RunNode.density` before the `density` attribute is applied, so `declared()` sees `undefined ?? 'full'`). So a gutter node that declares `minimal` renders at `full` for the first frame *before* the rAF recompute — a *decisive* glyph would flash its char for ~1 frame before collapsing to the dot. In practice the window is narrow (a step is `pending`/`none` on mount and turns `done` later, when the node is already measured-`minimal`), and the live probe showed the real spine nodes settled at `minimal`; but the invariant should hold *by construction, not by timing*. **Fix:** render `effective = min(this.density /*declared ceiling, available synchronously*/, this.densityCtl.density)` — caps to the declared ceiling from frame 0 while preserving the measured cap (strictly an improvement, since `ctl.density` is already `min(declared, afforded)`). This is the one residual worth fixing immediately to make "illegible glyph never drawn" timing-independent.
- **R2 — observer re-creation churn (minor perf).** `setupSpineResize()` (and the pre-existing `setupSpineScrollSpy()`) disconnect+recreate their observers on *every* `updated()`. Correct but wasteful; guard to set up once per `.conversation` mount. Follows the existing scroll-spy pattern, so not a §19 regression — logged for both.
- **R3 — minimap anchor precision when a trace is expanded (refinement, not a defect).** Intra-turn steps (tool/progress/error) live inside the collapsible `<details>` trace and are *interpolated* between turn anchors; a collapsed step genuinely has no scroll position, so interpolation is correct there — but when a trace is *expanded* its steps have real positions that could anchor precisely. A faithful-when-expanded refinement.
- **R4 — prominence projects (size, opacity), the design said (size, contrast).** Opacity is a contrast *proxy* that degrades non-linearly on dark backgrounds and across themes (the ambient 0.45 may read inconsistently). A true contrast-token projection (a declared luminance step, not raw opacity) would complete §19.3's "(size, contrast)" ideal. Minor.
- **R5 — threshold ↔ node-size coupling (documented, likely YAGNI to fix).** `GLYPH_LEGIBLE_PX = 9` is calibrated to the current 0.72rem trace disc; if the trace/card/gutter sizes change it must be re-tuned. A structural alternative (derive the legible bar from font metrics rather than a fixed px) is over-engineering absent a second size-change incident — noted so the coupling is explicit.
- **R6 — density coverage is ONE element (the register's honest limit, §19.5).** The `adaptive-closure` density pass covers only the registered `RunNode`. The discovery step: sweep the shell for *other* multi-scale elements that hand-fix a representation (evidence chips, status metrics, the sparkline?) and either register them onto the density primitive or confirm `RunNode` is the only one. Same "a register covers only declared concepts" limit as every other 565 gate.

**Cross-tier remaining-work ledger (the whole tempdoc, reconciled here so it is not scattered):**
- **Blocked by dev environment (not code):** §15.A tier-number calibration against the production cross-encoder distribution, and the §18 grounding badge's grounded-answer live-confirm — both need the citation *scorer* (a cross-encoder, distinct from the chat LLM) which is offline in this dev env. The chat LLM loads in ~11s; the scorer does not. Unblocks on a scorer-loaded stack.
- **Intrinsic runtime, not build-gateable (named, accepted):** §6's "answer *rendered* without evidence" is a runtime WARN by nature — a render-time fact no static gate can assert.
- **Unrelated red, tracked elsewhere:** the 568 `--font-body` `theme-token-closure` red (`TokenEditorPlugin.ts`) is pre-existing and outside 565's scope.

**The open tier question (named, NOT asserted as owed — applying `structural-defects-no-repeat` in reverse):** the run-step element is now projected across tone (§3.B) · glyph/label (§17) · prominence-as-scale (§19.3) · spatial position (§13/§19.4) · scale/density (§19). The ONE facet still expressed as a *flag* rather than a projected grammar is **liveness/motion**: `StepPresentation.live` → a single pulse, and lifecycle transitions (`pending → running → done`) *swap* representations without a declared motion. This is the natural "next dimension" after scale (the §19 meta-principle's time analog) — BUT there is **no observed motion fork or defect** (the pulse lives in one place; transitions are instantaneous, not hand-authored-divergent). So it is recorded as an *open question*, not owed work: a temporal tier should be opened only if a real motion fork or a jarring-transition defect is observed, never speculatively.

**Closure readiness.** Every substantive tier of 565 is now shipped (content · composition · spatial · leaf · run-step-presentation · ④/⑤ honesty · density). What remains is: R1 (a one-line correctness fix worth doing), R2–R6 (minor/refinement/discovery), the two env-blocked calibrations, the intrinsic §6 WARN, and the temporal open-question. Recommendation: land R1 with §19; spin R2–R6 + the env-blocked items into a short follow-up tempdoc (or `observations.md` lines) so 565 can close rather than stay open indefinitely on a long minor-residual tail — the env-blocked calibrations in particular gate on infrastructure (a scorer-loaded stack), not on 565 design work.

### §19.J Residuals resolved (2026-06-09) — R1–R4 + R6 SHIPPED, §18 narrowed, R5 + temporal held by discipline

All actionable §19.I residuals were implemented + verified this pass (static-green; R3/R4 live-measured). NOT merged.

- **R1 — SHIPPED + unit-pinned.** `RunNode.render()` now caps by the declared ceiling synchronously (`minDensity(this.density, this.densityCtl.density)`), and `minDensity` is exported from `adaptiveDensity.ts`. The first-paint flash is gone *by construction*, not timing. Regression: a new `RunNode.test.ts` mounts a `minimal`-declared node with a `done` (✓) descriptor in happy-dom (no ResizeObserver → controller stuck at `full`) and asserts it renders `.g-dot` / no char — i.e. the cap fires *without* any measurement (the exact first-paint condition). +4 tests.
- **R2 — SHIPPED.** `setupSpineResize()` observes the stable `.conversation` once (guarded) instead of disconnect+recreate every `updated()`.
- **R3 — SHIPPED + LIVE-CONFIRMED.** Trace-rows now carry `data-item-id`; `measureSpineFractions` skips zero-height (collapsed) elements. Live measured DOM: with a run's trace expanded, `spineFractions` anchored **5 ids — three of them `trace-row`** (heights 18/18/152px) at real scroll fractions (0.78/0.81/0.83), so expanded steps map precisely while collapsed steps still interpolate. Bonus: a spine tool/progress node now click-jumps to its row (previously unmatched).
- **R4 — SHIPPED (measured).** A live contrast probe found the neutral `ambient` dot sat right ON the WCAG 1.4.11 non-text bar (~2.86–3.05:1 vs the real dark surface `{15,15,18}`, depending on the composite) — borderline, matching §19.3's "too faint" flag. Raised `PROMINENCE_SCALE.ambient.opacity` 0.45 → 0.55 (deterministic recompute over the real bg: ~3.99:1), kept below `secondary` (0.65) so the grading order holds. *Interrogate-results note:* the first live reading (2.86, under the bar) used an assumed `{18,18,18}` bg; the real bg gave 3.05 (just over) — so this is a borderline-lift for margin + the named faintness, not a hard-failure fix; the comment states this honestly.
- **R6 — RESOLVED (the discovery step ran).** An independent read-only sweep of the shell-v0 tree concluded **`RunNode` is the ONLY genuine multi-scale-with-hand-fixed-glyph element**: `ProvenanceChip` (✓), `NavigationReceipt` (✓/✗/→/?), `StatusDeck` status dots, and `AdvisoryInboxDrawer` (✕) are each SINGLE-scale (one fixed context). So the `adaptive-closure` density gate's one-element coverage is **complete, not a gap** — no new registration owed.
- **§18 — NARROWED, not unblocked.** A live RAG/Documents query rendered a grounded answer with **5 sources + inline `[n]` citations** — so the citation *scorer works* in dev; §18's blocker is the dev 9B model not producing a clean grounded **agent** answer (it loops on a gated `core_ingest_files` write even under explicit read-only steering), NOT the scorer. Also surfaced (logged to `observations.md`, a §18 scope question, not fixed here): the grounding badge is wired to the **agent** answer path only and does NOT render on the Documents/RAG grounded answer, which IS grounded.
- **R5 + the temporal tier — HELD by discipline, deliberately not built.** R5 (threshold↔node-size coupling) and the liveness/motion "next tier" are genuine speculative-abstraction cases with no observed defect; per `structural-defects-no-repeat` / YAGNI they stay documented (above), to be acted on only on a real second incident or an observed motion fork — not pre-emptively.

**Verification:** FE `typecheck` clean; **2473 unit tests pass** (250 files; +4 `RunNode` tests); `adaptive-closure` + `run-renderers` + color-token/controls-a11y/a11y-closure/layout-purity gates green; `./gradlew.bat build -x test` SUCCESSFUL. R3 + R4 live-measured against the model-backed stack.

### §20 — Post-ship hardening (2026-06-10, branch `gate-fixes-main-green`): run-spine correctness + answer-content leak

Work done AFTER §19.J on the integration branch. Every user-visible item was validated LIVE on the model-backed stack and independently reviewed (reviewer ≠ committer) per the presentation-authority closure discipline. NOT merged.

**Run-spine correctness — found by a live dot-by-dot trace audit (the §13/§19 minimap):**
- **The spatial "dual-bound to reading position" half, finally built (the §13 piece specified but never shipped):** a PAVA min-separation placement primitive (`primitives/adaptiveSpacing.ts` `computeSpacedPositions`) so dense runs never overlap markers; a viewport-window indicator (`primitives/scrollViewport.ts` `viewportWindow`) drawn as a box tracking the reading position; and `jumpToItem` now opens ancestor collapsed `<details>` before `scrollIntoView` — the intra-turn step nodes (~half the markers) were silently un-jumpable inside a closed `<details>`.
- **Position-faithful dots.** A balance blend (α=0.25 toward even spacing) I had added was caught by a dot-trace audit pushing the TURN landmarks up to **19% of the track** off their content. Removed — dots sit at their true scroll fraction (`computeSpinePositions` → `computeSpacedPositions` directly; de-overlap is the ONLY adjustment). Live: turn divergence **19% → 0**. (Lesson: the "dead gap" under a long answer is CORRECT minimap behaviour — the viewport box marks position there — not a defect to flatten.)
- **One terminal "Answer" per turn.** Every assistant message got `TERMINAL_NODE_WEIGHT` + the "Answer" label, but the agent loop emits MULTIPLE assistant messages per turn → several "Answer" peaks. New pure `terminalAssistantIds(items)` (`unifiedThreadProjection.ts`) marks the LAST assistant of each `user→…→user` segment; only it is the terminal "Answer", intermediates demote to `secondary` "Working step".
- **Click highlight = the clicked dot** (pre-existing bug). `jumpToItem` set the active ring to the clicked item, but the scroll-spy `IntersectionObserver` overrode it to the topmost-in-view item after the centring scroll → clicking a dot highlighted its NEIGHBOUR (content-dependent, "some dots"). Fix: a `spinePinnedId` pins the ring on click; the scroll-spy adoption (extracted to a testable `adoptScrollSpyTop`) early-returns while pinned; released only on a genuine user scroll (`wheel`/`touchstart`/`keydown`). Live sweep: **15/15 dots highlight themselves**.

**Tool-call JSON recovery (backend — the answer-CONTENT correctness leaf).** A local model leaked its tool call as assistant TEXT (`; {"type":"function","name":"core_search_index","parameters":{…}}`) and it rendered AS the answer; the leaked call also carried a search the structured channel never ran (a DROPPED action, not cosmetic noise). Root cause: `AgentLlmCaller.tryParseHermesTextToolCalls` recovered only the `{name,arguments}` grammar, newline-split, and only when ZERO structured calls fired — the leak slipped all three. Hardened into `recoverInlineToolCalls`: both grammars (`{name,arguments}` + `{type:"function",…,"parameters"}`), a balanced-brace scan (inline / `;`-separated), run ALWAYS with the existing known-tool gate + dedup vs the structured calls + surgical span strip. **Chosen fix = RECOVER, not strip** — the leak IS a tool call the model expressed as text, so it executes through the normal safety/approval path (intent preserved); echoes are stripped; unknown-tool spans left as possible content. Fixed at the answer/action boundary (`callLlmWithTools`) so EVERY consumer — UI, persisted thread, exports, the model's own echoed history — gets clean text. +8 deterministic unit tests on the exact leaked payload.

**Verification (this session):** FE typecheck + **2651 unit tests** green; presentation/a11y/run-renderer gates green; `:modules:app-agent:test` + `build -x test` SUCCESSFUL; live model-backed validation of every user-visible item; **independent reviewer PASS (zero defects)** on the three dot fixes + the highlight fix.

### §13.9 — Layout-space audit (2026-06-10): the fixed-zone grid strands the reading column

A live whole-screen space audit of the §13 SPATIAL-COMPOSITION tier — the `composeGridStyles`-generated `.conversation-zone` (`CONVERSATION_ZONES`, `UnifiedChatView.ts:208`). At a 1920px window the grid computes to `[1fr] · [spine ≤2.5rem] · [conversation ≤40rem] · [evidence-rail minmax(15rem,20rem)] · [1fr]`. Measured findings:

1. **The reading column is hard-capped at 40rem (640px)** — it never grows, so wider monitors only add gutter (the §13.8 comment already concedes "~76% empty at 2400px").
2. **The evidence-rail track cannot collapse when empty.** Its `minmax(15rem, 20rem)` has a NON-ZERO min, so in Documents/RAG mode (rail unmounted) it reserves ~320px of DEAD space AND shoves the conversation **~280px LEFT of true centre** (asymmetry). The §13.8 "empty wide-only zone collapses its track" claim holds only for the `minmax(0,…)` spine, NOT the rail. Measured empty width: **65% (Documents) / 44% (Agent)**.
3. **The outer `1fr` margins strand a ~1050px content group** in ~800px of empty gutter even at the best case (agent, panels populated).
4. The conversation's scrollbar is functionally needed but floats mid-page (Documents) or doubles next to the sources-panel scrollbar (Agent) — symptoms of #1–#3, not independent bugs.

**Proposed (to be designed + live-validated in the follow-up plan):** collapse the rail track to 0 when sourceless (fixes the 320px dead + the 280px asymmetry); grow the reading column (`minmax(40rem, ~56rem)`); cap the outer `1fr` margins so the group isn't stranded at wide viewports; tighten the spine column toward its real width.

### §13.9 — SHIPPED (2026-06-10, live-validated + independently reviewed)

`CONVERSATION_ZONES` (`UnifiedChatView.ts:208`) re-zoned + `.conversation-zone` centred:
| zone | was | now |
|---|---|---|
| outer margins | `minmax(0, 1fr)` | `minmax(0, 8rem)` (CAPPED) |
| spine | `minmax(0, 2.5rem)` | `auto` (collapses when unmounted) |
| conversation | `minmax(0, 40rem)` | `minmax(0, 50rem)` (≈88ch) |
| evidence-rail | `minmax(15rem, 20rem)` | `fit-content(20rem)` (collapses to 0) |
+ `.evidence-rail { min-width:15rem; max-width:20rem }`, reading measure `74ch → 88ch`, and `.conversation-zone { justify-content: center }`.

**Key correction (verified live):** `minmax(0, max)` does NOT collapse an unmounted zone — the spine's `minmax(0, 2.5rem)` still measured **40px** with the spine absent (bounded tracks claim free space up to their max). Only CONTENT-sized tracks (`auto` / `fit-content`) collapse to 0. The §13.8 "empty zone collapses its `minmax(0,…)` track" claim was wrong.

**Measured, both modes at 1440/1920/2560 (independent reviewer PASS, zero findings):**
- **Documents/RAG** (rail+spine unmounted): `grid-template-columns: 128px 0px 800px 0px 128px` at every width — rail + spine tracks **collapsed to 0** (was a 320px dead column); conversation **centred, asymmetry 0** (was ~280px left-shift); conversation **800px** (50rem; was 640px); margins **128px** (8rem).
- **Agent** (rail present): the spine+conversation+rail GROUP is **centred** (group-off-centre 0); rail 320px, spine ~14px, conversation up to 800px (shrinks to 670px at 1440 — the `minmax(0,50rem)` minimum), margins 128px. %empty 22–52% (was 44%).
- **Scrollbars (finding #4):** the conversation + sources scroll regions live in the view's shadow root, so the global 6px thin scrollbar (`tokens.css`) couldn't reach them (`::-webkit-scrollbar` doesn't cross the shadow boundary) → they fell back to a chunky **15px native** bar at the column edge. Added `scrollbar-width: thin; scrollbar-color: var(--border-subtle) transparent` to `.conversation` + `.evidence-rail` → a **thin (~10px), subtle** scrollbar (live-measured 10px), token-based (color-tokens gate clean). The regions still scroll (the composer stays pinned; the sources list scrolls independently) — just unobtrusive now.

The reviewer's width method (resize_window is clamped in the dev env → simulate widths via the zone container, which is what the grid responds to) was cross-checked faithful (sim-1920 == native). Static: typecheck clean, 2652 FE tests + `compositionLayout`/`UnifiedChatView` tests green, composition-surfaces + layout-purity + presentation/a11y gates green. NOT merged.

*Out-of-scope finding (logged to observations.md, not part of this layout work):* a model tool-call-JSON leak (`{"name":"core_search_index","parameters":…}`, the `{name,parameters}` grammar) still renders in an agent answer bubble on the running `:64778` backend — the §20 `recoverInlineToolCalls` fix may not be in that jar or has a gap for that exact grammar; needs a backend re-verify.

### §13.10 — spine-AS-scrollbar (idea raised 2026-06-10; surfaces a navigation-authority question)

The thin-scrollbar fix (#4) treated the symptom. The raised idea: make the run-spine's viewport box DRAGGABLE (drag-to-scroll, the code-editor minimap pattern) so the spine IS the conversation's scroll control, and the native scrollbar becomes redundant where the spine is present.
