Feasible, but it exposes the deeper structure: the agent window now has FOUR forked representations of one "where am I / how do I move in the run" concept — the native scrollbar (scroll affordance), the spine viewport box (position indicator, `scrollViewport.ts`), the spine dots (jump targets), and the scroll-spy active ring (topmost-in-view) — none unified, and they only partly overlap (the spine exists in agent-wide only; the rail scrolls separately). A point-fix (drag the box) leaves the fork. **The correct structure is theorized below (§21) as a single spatial-navigation / reading-position authority** the scroll affordance, minimap, jump, and position-ring all project from — not four mechanisms that happen to agree.

## §21 — The NAVIGATION authority (spatial reading-position): the tier 559 named but did not design

*Design theory (feasibility deliberately set aside — this section states the correct STRUCTURE, not a fix). Major refactor in scope. The §13/§19 spine, the §13.9 layout, the scrollbar, and the spine-as-scrollbar idea are all instances of it.*

### §21.0 — Diagnosis: one missing authority, many symptoms

Read the whole session's agent-window work back as a list and a single shape appears. The lopsided dots that needed a hand-tuned `BALANCE_ALPHA` blend (§20); the click-jump highlight that the scroll-spy kept stealing, requiring a `spinePinnedId` / `adoptScrollSpyTop` pin-and-release apparatus (§20); the chunky native scrollbar sitting *beside* the minimap that the spine already duplicates (§13.9 #4 + §13.10); the evidence-rail track that reserved phantom space because the layout model had no notion of "collapse when the content is absent" (§13.9); the "just make the spine the scrollbar" idea (§13.10). **None of these is an independent bug.** They are five symptoms of one absence: the agent window's model of *the run as a navigable spatial thing — where each event sits, where you are reading, and how you move* is **hand-wired inside one view** (`UnifiedChatView`) as FOUR un-unified position-representations plus the browser's own scroll, with no typed authority binding them.

The investigation confirmed the shape precisely. The four representations — the native scrollbar (browser-owned scrollTop), the `.run-spine-viewport` box (`spineViewport`, projected by `scrollViewport.ts`'s `viewportWindow`), the dots (`spineFractions` placed by `adaptiveSpacing.ts`), and the active ring (`activeSpineItemId` + `spinePinnedId`, driven by an IntersectionObserver) — all read from the same `.conversation` scroll metrics in `measureSpineFractions` and re-render together, so they do not *yet* visibly diverge. But there is **no extracted authority**: the orchestration is view-local, the native scrollbar is a genuinely separate affordance the model knows nothing about, and the two "where you are" signals (the box and the ring) are computed by two *different* mechanisms (a rAF scroll listener vs an IntersectionObserver) that can — and during the highlight bug, did — disagree. Every fix this session was a patch on a fork; the next scroll surface (search results — see 570's keyboard-driven list/detail; Activity; Logs) will re-hand-wire the same four things from scratch.

This is exactly the gap the presentation lineage closes for every *other* facet. 557/559 establish that a UI facet must be **one canonical authority projected to every surface, governed by a register-backed gate** — Display, Observed-state, Theme, A11y, Operability, Evidence, Messaging, and **Adaptivity**. But 559 **explicitly capped Adaptivity at element-level constrained-space behavior** (the OVERFLOW / FILL / PLACEMENT facets: which items fit a bar, which representation a box can afford, how markers de-overlap) and named — without designing — the tier above it: the spatial/navigation tier. 569 lists "layout" as a fifth user-authored axis but defers its design; 561's `OverflowController` is *region overflow under constraint*, not *user navigation through content*. So the spatial-navigation tier is the **one declared-but-undesigned hole** in the projection kernel, and the agent window is where its absence is now most acute.

### §21.1 — Thesis: a Navigation authority, sibling to Adaptivity

The correct structure is a new presentation authority — call it **Navigation** (spatial reading-position) — that owns the ONE canonical model of *the run as a navigable spatial sequence + the current reading position + the operations that move it*, and that every navigation surface PROJECTS from. The scrollbar, the minimap, the position box, the focus ring, and click / drag / keyboard jump stop being four mechanisms that happen to agree and become pure, lossy-downward projections of one record. This is the 553/561 kernel ("exactly one canonical record; every surface a governed projection, never an independent model") applied to the facet 559 left open.

It is a **sibling** to Adaptivity, not a sub-facet of it: Adaptivity answers *"given a fixed box, what fits / what representation / where do markers land"* (a function of declaration × available space); Navigation answers *"given an ordered sequence longer than the viewport, where is the reader and how do they traverse it"* (a function of content-extent × reading-window × intent). The minimap COMPOSES Adaptivity for its leaf rendering, but the reading-position model is Navigation's.

### §21.2 — The canonical record: `NavigableRun` / `ReadingPosition`

One typed value model, complete enough to be a superset of every projection (the 558 "projection totality" discipline — a partial record forces surfaces to re-derive, which is the fork):

- **Landmarks** — the ordered run items. This is *already canonical*: the merged timeline (`projectUnifiedThread` + `projectLiveAgentActivity` → `UnifiedTurnItem[]`, §12.3.D). Navigation does not invent a second sequence; it adds the *spatial* dimension to the one that exists.
- **Extent per landmark** — each landmark's measured **scroll-span** (its top/bottom fraction of the scrollable content), not a single point. A point is what forced the midpoint-vs-top hand-tuning and the balance blend; a span is the truth (a long answer genuinely *occupies* a region, a collapsed step occupies none).
- **Reading window** — the viewport as `[topFrac, botFrac]` (exactly `scrollViewport.ts`'s `ViewportWindow`, already the right primitive).
- **Focus** — the landmark the reader is on, **derived** from window × extents (not a separately-observed signal). One definition of "where you are," so the box and the ring cannot disagree.
- **Intent** — a single field with a declared **live ↔ pinned** mode: normally the focus tracks the reading window (live); a jump *pins* it to a target until the reader scrolls. This replaces the `activeSpineItemId` / `spinePinnedId` pair and the pin-release plumbing with one state machine, making the highlight-steal conflict *unrepresentable*.

### §21.3 — Facets (parallel to Adaptivity's OVERFLOW / FILL / PLACEMENT)

- **POSITION** — landmark extents. Projects the dots. Reuses `scrollViewport.ts` + the existing midpoint measurement, generalized from point to span. *Dots become a faithful projection of where content is — the hand-tuned `BALANCE_ALPHA` blend disappears, because "balanced" was a symptom of projecting a point instead of an extent.*
- **WINDOW** — the reading viewport. Projects the box. Reuses `viewportWindow`.
- **FOCUS** — the derived in-view landmark. Projects the ring. *Removes the second IntersectionObserver mechanism — focus is computed from the same window × extents the box uses.*
- **CONTROL** — the navigation operations (scroll · drag-the-window · click-a-landmark · keyboard arrows/page/home-end) that mutate the ONE reading position via the live/pinned intent. *The click-jump/scroll-spy fight cannot occur: there is one position and one mode, not two writers racing for `activeSpineItemId`.*
- **AFFORDANCE** — the rendering of the scroll *control*. The minimap-as-scrollbar (the §13.10 idea) is the projection here: the spine IS the scroll control where it is present. The native scrollbar is reclassified as the **transport / consumer boundary** (the honest 559 §15 ceiling) — suppressed when the minimap projection is mounted, a degraded fallback where it is not (Documents/RAG and narrow viewports, where no spine exists). *No two scroll affordances side by side, because there is one AFFORDANCE facet with two render targets.*

### §21.4 — Composes the existing primitives; does not replace them

Navigation is the missing *binder*, not a rewrite of what works. It COMPOSES: Adaptivity's `adaptiveSpacing` (PLACEMENT — dot de-overlap, the PAVA primitive) and `adaptiveDensity` (FILL — legible dots at the gutter scale) for the minimap leaf; `scrollViewport` for the WINDOW math; and `composeGridStyles` for the spatial **frame**. The §13/§19 spine and the §13.9 layout (zone collapse + centering) become Navigation's **frame facet** — and once the frame is a facet of a typed authority, "collapse the zone when its content is absent" and "centre the reading column" are correct-by-construction properties of the model, so the §13.9 phantom-reserved-space class and the centering/asymmetry class cannot recur surface-by-surface.

### §21.5 — Why this prevents the issue long-term

Each past symptom dissolves at the structure, not the surface: the minimap is faithful because dots project extents (no blend); there is one reading position with a mode (no highlight fight, no pin/release apparatus); there is one AFFORDANCE projection (no redundant scrollbar — the spine is the scrollbar where present); the frame is a facet (no per-surface collapse/centering bugs). And the decisive long-term property: **a new scroll surface acquires correct navigation by *declaring* a `NavigableRun` and mounting the projections — not by re-hand-wiring four representations.** Search results, Activity, and Logs stop being four future re-implementations of the same fork.

### §21.6 — Generality, scope, and the honest ceiling

**Generality.** Navigation is a presentation-tier authority reusable across every multi-item scroll surface; the agent run-spine is the reference/first consumer (the proving ground), 570's keyboard-driven search results the natural second. Per AHA, it unifies only what shares *one reason to change* — the reading-position model — and not unrelated scaffolding; it is not over-DRY (the surfaces genuinely share the concept, as the recurring symptoms show).

**Anti-drift (the 553/561 register + gate).** A `governance/navigation-surfaces.v1.json` register and a `navigation-surface` discipline gate on the 530 kernel, with the standard three checks: catalog-scan (which surfaces carry a reading position), positive coverage (every one projects a `NavigableRun`; a new scroll surface that hand-manages position fails the build), and forbidden-reintroduction (a denylist for the named fork patterns — an `onScroll` position cache, a per-surface scroll-spy, a second scrollbar mounted beside a minimap). As always, *the gate is the floor, not the mechanism*: the real guarantee is the typed `NavigableRun` seam — a surface cannot *expose* a reading position except by projecting the authority — with the gate catching what types cannot inside `html`/`css` templates.

**Honest ceiling (mirror 559 §15 / 561 §5).** The browser's scroll DOM and `scrollIntoView` are the **transport**, not authoring: Navigation owns the *declared* reading-position model; the actual pixel scroll is the consumer boundary it drives, the same way Theme owns tokens but the GPU owns pixels. A raw component `onScroll` handler that caches position is the navigation analog of 557's "raw-id interpolation" — a bypassed seam, recorded as the named anti-pattern, not a thing the type system can reach.

### §21.7 — Relationship to the rest of 565 and the lineage

Navigation is the **spatial-reading tier** of this tempdoc's stack (content · composition · spatial-composition · leaf · run-step-presentation · density · honesty), and the structural completion 559 deferred. It is the same kernel as 553 (canonical record → projections → register+gate), the same surface-projection template as 561, the same "totality" discipline as 558, and a cousin of 571's "a spatial choice is a *derived* property of an authority, not an independent decision." The work already shipped this session (the spine §13/§19, the layout §13.9, the scrollbar) is not thrown away — it is **re-seated as the first projections of this authority**, which is the test of whether the theorization is correct: the right structure should make the existing good work fall out as instances, and make the bad patches (the blend, the pin apparatus, the redundant scrollbar) unnecessary.

### §21.8 — De-risking pass (2026-06-10): the chat-first correction + a confidence ledger

Before any implementation, the §21.0–21.7 theory was pressure-tested with three read-only codebase investigations and two live dev-server spikes (throwaway injected JS, reverted). It survived mostly intact but with **one structural correction** and several de-risked details.

**The correction (most important): build it CHAT-FIRST behind a general seam, not as a general authority now.** A survey of every scroll surface found that the rich "reading-position + position-indicator + jump" concept is **chat-only today**: Search has selection/active-row only (arrow-key nav is explicitly *deferred*, `SearchSurface.ts`), Logs has pause/resume (stream control, not reading-position), and Activity/Browse/Brain/Navigate/Summarize/Health/Memory/Library are plain native-scroll over `surfaceLayout`. So a general multi-surface Navigation authority + its register+gate is **premature (YAGNI/AHA — nothing else yet shares the reason to change)**. The corrected structure: **extract a `NavigationController` and define the typed `NavigableRun`/`ReadingPosition` SEAM (with `scrollViewport` as the shared core), but implement the rich version only for the chat**, and lift it to a multi-surface authority + register+gate **when the 2nd/3rd surface actually adopts it** (Search once keyboard nav lands is the likely trigger). §21.6's "general authority" framing is thus the *eventual* state; the *first* step is chat-first. The gate is **deferred** accordingly — for one consumer the typed seam is the guarantee, a register+gate over a single member is ceremony.

**Confidence ledger (validated → open):**
- **Extraction — HIGH.** The spine's nav code is 100% private to `UnifiedChatView` (zero external consumers → no ripple); the measure/jump/observer logic is DOM-pure (needs only `.conversation` + `.run-spine`); `computeSpinePositions` is pure. A `NavigationController` is a natural (if richer/stateful, side-effect-bearing) extension of the Adaptivity controller pattern (`OverflowController`/`DensityController`). **Seam:** controller owns observers + measurement + pin + `jumpToItem`, handed the 2 elements + a few callbacks; `renderRunSpine` stays in the view reading its state.
- **AFFORDANCE (minimap-as-scrollbar) — HIGH (spike-proven), 2 minor caveats.** Live spike: a drag on the viewport box mapped to `scrollTop` **exactly** (inverse of `viewportWindow`; 80px drag → the predicted 157px, within 5px). Caveats to design in, not blockers: hiding the native bar (`scrollbar-width:none`) reclaims ~10px → a one-time layout shift (manage with `scrollbar-gutter` or absorb it in the agent-wide margin); the box is ~14px wide (a real-scrollbar-thumb target — widen the hit-area if it feels thin). a11y is a known recipe: `role="slider"`/`"scrollbar"` + `tabindex` + arrow/Page/Home-End keydown + `setPointerCapture` (passes `controls-a11y`); reuse `scrollViewport.ts` math + `dragDetect.ts` pointer pattern (no slider/scroll infra exists today — net-new but unblocked).
- **FOCUS-derivation — MEDIUM (viable, needs the right predicate).** Live spike: deriving focus from window×extents matched the live IntersectionObserver at 4/5 scroll positions; the one mismatch was a **threshold difference** — naive "topmost item with any overlap" picked a 1px-peeking step where the observer's 10%-visibility threshold picked the substantial answer. So FOCUS *can* retire the observer, **but the predicate must encode the visibility threshold** (e.g. the item containing the window-top with a min-visible fraction, or largest-visible-area), not naive overlap. Open: pick + tune that predicate.
- **POSITION (extent vs point) — HIGH.** The extent is the underlying truth; the dot is its midpoint projection (already what §13.9 ships, no blend). Consistent; no change.
- **Anti-drift gate — buildable but DEFERRED** (templated ~4–5 files per `class-size`/`adr-coverage`), per the chat-first correction.

**Net:** confidence to *implement chat-first* is now high — the riskiest mechanism (drag-scroll) is spike-proven exact, extraction has a clean private seam, and the one over-reach (premature generalization) is corrected. The remaining open items are tuning-grade (the FOCUS predicate, the drag a11y/feel polish), not structural. Implementation, when it comes, should be: extract the `NavigationController` + the `NavigableRun` seam for the chat, project the five facets, and leave the general authority/register+gate for the second adopter.

### §21.9 — Implementation (shipped, chat-first): `primitives/navigation.ts`

The §21.8 plan was implemented chat-first as `modules/ui-web/src/shell-v0/primitives/navigation.ts` — a `NavigationController implements ReactiveController` (mirroring `OverflowController`/`DensityController`) + a pure `deriveFocus`. `UnifiedChatView` went from **11 spine state fields + 8 spine methods + an `updated()` override + a teardown block** down to **one `private readonly nav = new NavigationController(this, {scrollEl, spineEl, active})`**; `renderRunSpine` is now a pure projection of `this.nav.{fractions, trackPx, viewport, activeId}`. Built in four behaviour-checkpointed phases:

- **Phase 1 — POSITION/WINDOW seam (behaviour-preserving extraction).** The measurement (item extents + midpoints, track height, `viewportWindow`), the rAF scroll listener, the pin, and `jumpTo` moved into the controller; the controller self-manages its `ResizeObserver` + listeners via `hostUpdated`/`hostDisconnected`. Proof: the 24 existing spine view-tests pass unchanged.
- **Phase 2 — FOCUS derived; CONTROL unified.** `deriveFocus(landmarks, window, MIN_VISIBLE=0.1)` = the **topmost landmark with ≥10% of itself in the window** (the Spike-B threshold predicate, matching the retired `IntersectionObserver` `threshold:0.1`; naive any-overlap is wrong). The `IntersectionObserver` is GONE — FOCUS re-derives from window×extents on every scroll-driven re-render via the `activeId` getter. `activeSpineItemId`+`spinePinnedId`+`adopt`/`release` collapsed into ONE `intent: {mode:'live'|'pinned', pinnedId}` — the highlight-steal bug is now unrepresentable. Unit-tested: `deriveFocus` boundaries/threshold + the live↔pinned transitions.
- **Phase 3 — AFFORDANCE: the minimap-as-scrollbar.** The `.run-spine-viewport` box became an operable `role="scrollbar"` (+`tabindex`, `aria-controls="run-conversation"`, `aria-orientation`, `aria-valuemin/max/now`): pointer-drag maps Δy→`scrollTop` as the **exact** inverse of `viewportWindow` (`Δscroll = (Δy/trackPx)·scrollHeight`, Spike A), with `setPointerCapture`; keyboard arrows/Page/Home-End scroll via `nudge`. The reading column hides its native scrollbar **only when the spine is mounted** (`.conversation.spine-scrolled { scrollbar-width:none; scrollbar-gutter:stable }` — the gutter neutralizes the Spike-A 10px reflow); Documents/narrow keeps the thin native bar. The `controls-a11y` gate was extended to accept `role="scrollbar"` (a real interactive ARIA role, operated by the tabindex+keydown triad like `slider`). Unit-tested: the exact drag mapping, pin-release-on-grab, and `nudge`.
- **Phase 4 — re-seat + cleanup.** POSITION dots and the WINDOW box now read the controller's one model; the no-blend faithful positions (§13.9) and the de-overlap pass are unchanged; the pin apparatus is the `intent`; the redundant native scrollbar is gone in agent mode. The general register+gate stays **deferred** (one consumer → the typed seam is the guarantee), per §21.8.

Static verification: `typecheck` + the full frontend unit suite (2662 tests) green, incl. the new `navigation.test.ts` (10) and the behaviour-preserving `UnifiedChatView.test.ts` (24); the presentation/layout/a11y/composition/`controls-a11y`/`run-renderers` gates all pass. Live-browser verification (drag-scroll fidelity, wheel/keyboard, no redundant bar, focus tracking, the no-regression set, the Documents fallback) + an independent-reviewer PASS are the closing batch (per the active goal).

### §21.10 — Generalisation-readiness: the plumbing reuses, the map does not (2026-06-10)

Pressing on §22 item 1 ("generalise the Navigation authority") clarified that "generalise" is the wrong unit — the chat run-spine is TWO layers with different reuse profiles:

- **The mechanism (reusable, surface-agnostic):** the scroll-position math, the draggable-thumb control, and the derived reading-FOCUS — `scrollViewport` + the drag mapping + `deriveFocus` are pure and already projection-shaped. This is the `NavigableRun`/`ReadingPosition` core; it would work on any scroll surface.
- **The map (surface-SPECIFIC, NOT reusable):** the dots — what counts as a landmark, its prominence, the terminal "Answer" peak, the collapsible depth. This is what makes the spine worth looking at instead of a plain scrollbar, and it is entirely a function of the chat run's structure.

**The landmark test (when the map earns its keep):** a minimap beats the native scrollbar only when the content is BOTH long AND made of meaningful, *heterogeneous* landmarks worth marking. The corollary is a hard design rule — **a minimap earns the right to REPLACE the native scrollbar only by showing something the scrollbar cannot.** Where there is nothing extra to show, the native bar (the 559 §15 transport boundary) is the better choice; swapping it for a landmark-less map is strictly worse (lose the familiar control, gain nothing).

**Surface-by-surface verdict (extends the §21.8 chat-first survey):**
- **Chat — fits.** Structured sequence (message→tools→answer), a terminal destination, collapsible depth, prominence grading. The map shows real structure.
- **Search — does NOT fit the map.** A flat, *homogeneous* result list → a map of identical dots is a tick-scrollbar that shows nothing new. Search's real need is a different concept — a keyboard SELECTION cursor (arrow row-to-row), a SIBLING of this authority's CONTROL/FOCUS facets, not its minimap. Forcing the spine here would push it to invent fake landmarks.
- **Logs / activity — fits with a DIFFERENT map.** A severity minimap (jump-to-errors, like an editor's scrollbar error ticks) is real value, but the dots mean SEVERITY, not run-steps → reuses the mechanism, not the chat map.
- **Long documents / Browse — fits with a DIFFERENT map.** Dots = headings (a TOC scrollbar). Same mechanism, heading landmarks.
- **Health / Memory / Library / most others — do NOT fit.** Short/simple → the native scrollbar is correct; a map is clutter.

**Corrected generalisation shape (refines §21.6's "general authority" framing):** NOT "project the chat spine onto every surface." Instead — extract the **mechanism** once as a reusable primitive; let each surface **opt in with its own landmark projection**, only where the landmark test passes. The likely real next adopters are **logs (error markers)** and **long documents (headings)** — explicitly **not** search (which wants the sibling selection-cursor concept). The register+gate, when it lands, governs the *mechanism's* single-authority + the per-surface *opt-in* catalog (which surfaces project a map, and why), NOT a mandate that every surface have one. This keeps §6's YAGNI honest: a navigation authority that forces a map onto flat lists manufactures the very drift it claims to prevent.

## §22 — Closure & remaining-work ledger (2026-06-10)

§20 (post-ship hardening) and §21 (the chat-first Navigation authority) are now **live-validated, independently reviewed, and MERGED** — this supersedes §20's "NOT merged" line and §21.9's "closing batch pending".

- **§21 (navigation) — closed.** The §21.9 four-phase build was validated in the REAL browser on a model-backed run, by DOM-probe measurement + screenshots: the exact drag→scroll mapping (80px→137.0, 150px→257.25), a real OS thumb-drag scrolling the conversation, real wheel + Home/End keyboard scroll, derived FOCUS tracking the reading window (rendered ring matched, pin released on scroll), click-jump opening collapsed traces with highlight = the clicked dot, and the Documents/narrow native-bar fallback. An independent reviewer (≠ committer) returned **PASS, zero unresolved findings**.
- **Standalone-compile fix landed alongside (§13/§19.3).** The §21 commit imported `terminalAssistantIds` (the §20 "one terminal Answer per turn" projection) while that function still lived only in the working tree → a clean checkout failed `tsc` (TS2305). Committed as its own step (`fix(565 §13/§19.3)`), with `compositionLayout.test` re-synced to the §13.9 zones.
- **Merged into `gate-fixes-main-green`** (`e9342147f`): §21 navigation + the §13/§19.3 compile-fix + §20 tool-call recovery. Compiles; FE **2682** tests + `:modules:app-agent:test` + the presentation/a11y/`controls-a11y`/`run-renderers` gates green; the merged tree is byte-identical to the verified branch tip.

**Remaining work (small — all deferred-by-design or verify-only; nothing blocks the shipped chat behaviour):**

1. **Extract the navigation MECHANISM + per-surface opt-in — the one real design remainder (see §21.10).** §21 shipped CHAT-FIRST: the model lives only in `UnifiedChatView`'s `NavigationController`. The correct generalisation is NOT "project the chat spine everywhere" — §21.10 splits it: the **mechanism** (scroll-position + draggable thumb + derived focus) is reusable and would be extracted once as a primitive; the **map** (what a dot means) is surface-specific and only earns its keep where the content is long AND has heterogeneous landmarks (the landmark test). So it stays **deferred until a 2nd surface passes that test** — likely **logs** (error-severity markers) or **long documents** (headings), explicitly **not** search (which wants a sibling keyboard-selection cursor, not a minimap). For one consumer the typed seam IS the guarantee; a register+gate over a single member is ceremony (§21.6 / §21.8 / §21.10).
2. **§20 live re-verify (verify-only, not a code gap).** `recoverInlineToolCalls` is code-complete with 8 tests covering both leak grammars, but a live observation logged the `{name,parameters}` leak still rendering on the running backend — confirm end-to-end against a fresh-dist model-backed stack that the fix actually fires (likely a stale-jar/deploy artefact). Logged in `observations.md`.
3. **`execution-surface` gate red (565/571-owned).** On `gate-fixes-main-green`, `citationResolve.ts` (real consumer) + `MarkdownBlock.ts` (comment-only) reference `RetrievalCitation` unregistered in `governance/execution-surfaces.v1.json` — register `citationResolve` as a `consumer` (the 559 evidence pattern); for `MarkdownBlock` register or drop the JSDoc type-name. One of the 6 reds that block `gate → main` (the other 5 are non-565 gate debt).
4. **Held-by-discipline residuals.** §19.I R5 + the temporal/ordering edge — carried by care, not an automated check (§19.J).

## §23 — Confidence/de-risk pass (2026-06-11): the remaining work pressure-tested before any build

Before implementing any §22 item, a read-only + dev-server de-risk pass (mirroring §21.8) ran five probes against the uncertainties. Net: confidence up across the board, and ONE real latent bug surfaced (the thumb contrast).

| Probe | Confidence | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| **P1 — §20 leak, live** | LOW → MED-HIGH | The fix is wired (`callLlmWithTools`→`recoverInlineToolCalls`) + now loaded (fresh `installDist`+restart) + runs every call + unit-proven; 3 tool-heavy live runs all produced CLEAN answers. The §22-item-2 live observation was a **stale-jar artefact**, not a code gap. Honest residual: the inline-leak is too rare to force, so a recovery firing was not *witnessed* live (no leak occurred to recover). |
| **P2 — nav 2nd-adopter** | LOW-MED → HIGH (defer confirmed) | Surveyed `Log/Activity/Browse/Summarize/Search` against the §21.10 landmark test: **no genuine map adopter today.** Log/Activity are flat homogeneous lists (tick-scrollbar at best); Summarize is one stream; Search + Browse want a **sibling keyboard-cursor**, not a minimap. §22-item-1 correctly stays deferred — and the *real* cross-surface authority worth sharing (when it comes) is a keyboard selection/tree cursor, a DIFFERENT abstraction from the spatial map. |
| **P3 — extraction + nav gate** | MED → HIGH (GO) | The mechanism/map split **already exists** (dots/weighting live in the view, not `NavigationController`); only two shallow tangles (`[data-item-id]` selector + the `<details>` reveal — liftable to options). A `navigation-surface` gate is a buildable 5th instance of the proven `*-surface` kernel pattern (`interaction-surface` is the FE template), and its forbidden-reintroduction denylist (no new scroll-spy observer, no 2nd scrollbar) would lock the chat win against regression. The "missing third leg" is deferred by cost/benefit, NOT by feasibility. |
| **P4 — execution-surface red** | MED → HIGH (exact fix) | Precise dry-run: add one `consumer` entry (guard:self) for `citationResolve.ts` + drop the literal `RetrievalCitation` from one JSDoc line in `MarkdownBlock.ts`. Confirmed those are the ONLY two unregistered referencers, so the two edits turn the gate green. Near-zero surprise. |
| **P5 — §9 measured a11y/contrast** | — → DONE, 1 real finding | Independent (auditor≠committer) measured non-text-contrast audit (WCAG 1.4.11 / 2.4.11) of the nav, both themes. **Focus + active rings PASS strongly (9.35 dark / 5.67 light)** — the keyboard-critical affordances are sound. **NEW FINDING: the resting scrollbar thumb @ 0.16 opacity FAILS — 1.30 (dark) / 1.26 (light), still sub-3:1 at its 0.34 active state.** An operable `role="scrollbar"` control too faint to meet non-text contrast, with no redundant cue at rest. Would have shipped unnoticed. Connector + dot-border also sub-3:1 (decorative / glyph-redundant, lower severity). |

**New actionable items (added to the remaining work):**

5. **Thumb contrast (a11y, real bug — P5).** `.run-spine-viewport` resting opacity 0.16 fails WCAG 1.4.11 (1.26–1.30:1) in both themes; even 0.34 (active) misses 3:1. Raise the thumb opacity substantially or give it a bordered/outlined treatment so the scroll control meets the 3:1 non-text floor. The focus/active rings already pass — only the thumb body needs the fix.
6. **§22-item-3 exact fix is ready (P4).** The execution-surface registration is a known ~2-line change (above); no further investigation needed.

**Disposition shift:** §22-item-2 (§20) downgraded to "verify-only, stale-jar — no code change expected"; §22-item-1 (generalise) confidence-confirmed as correctly-deferred (and re-aimed: the next real authority is a keyboard-cursor, not the map); the nav gate + extraction are GO-when-wanted; §22-item-3 has a copy-pasteable fix; and one genuine a11y bug (the thumb) was caught before shipping.


## §24 — Why the §14 memory fold isn't in the agent window yet (honest accounting, 2026-06-11)

§14 "confirmed correct" the memory split — fold the **Presence-inbox + run-launcher** (the activity, "what it did") into the window's run history, and keep the durable **facts** ("what it knows") as a separate linked peer surface. Live check (2026-06-11, on a fresh dist): it is **not built.** `MemorySurface.ts` still renders BOTH halves together (it reads `/api/memory` + `/api/presence` in one component), and the chat window (`UnifiedChatView` / `AgentSessionController`) holds no presence/background runs. Why it never shipped — structurally, not by oversight:

1. **§14 validated it but never SEQUENCED it.** §14.3 ("what this changes in the plan") promoted exactly two items to action — the inline claim-proximate citations and the ④/⑤ honesty signals — and named the **workflow** run as the cross-surface unification step. The memory fold was a "confirmed correct" *conclusion*, not added to the action sequence. Workflow got a plan slot; memory did not.

2. **No implementation tier owned it.** §15 (leaf) explicitly folded workflow (§15.C — "workflow becomes a MODE of the one window") but said nothing about folding the memory activity. There is no memory implementation-outcome section anywhere in the doc. So no tier ever picked it up.

3. **No forcing function — the asymmetry vs workflow.** Workflow folded partly because 561's `interaction-surface` gate makes *a second visible workflow surface a build failure* — a hard forcing function. `core.memory-surface` is a LEGITIMATE declared surface (it correctly holds the durable facts the §14 design says to KEEP separate), so the gate never fires on it. Nothing makes the activity-half fold a build requirement; it stays discretionary.

4. **It's a partial split, not a clean move.** Workflow = "the whole run becomes a mode" (clean). Memory = "fold ONLY the presence/activity half into the run history, KEEP the facts half as a peer surface" — and the two halves are entangled inside one `MemorySurface` component. Cleanly extracting just the activity half without muddying the facts surface is more work than the one-line benchmark conclusion implied.

5. **Substrate ready, FE projection unbuilt.** §14.1 / §15.C note `AgentRunStore` already holds agent + background runs as ONE entity (the persistence half is done; the Presence surface is already a projection of it). So the hard part exists; only the FE re-projection — surfacing the presence/background runs INSIDE the chat window's run history — is missing, and it was never scoped.

6. **Outside the §2 thesis.** 565's core defect is "two grounded-answer authorities" — the content/evidence fork. The memory facts-vs-activity split is a different axis; folding the activity half does not serve the grounded-answer unification, so it sat below the core fork fixes (§3 / §12 / §13 / §15 / §17 / §19) and the navigation work (§21).

**Net:** the memory fold wasn't forgotten or rejected — it was *validated-but-unsequenced*, has *no forcing gate* (because the facts surface SHOULD stay separate, so a second surface here is legitimate, unlike workflow), is a *harder partial-split* than workflow, and falls *outside the core thesis*. Unlike navigation (§21/§22), it was never even on the remaining-work ledger — this section adds it: **folding the activity half (Presence-inbox + run-launcher → the window's run history) is genuinely-deferred remaining work, gated only by scope/priority, on a substrate (`AgentRunStore`) that is already ready.** The durable-facts half deliberately stays a separate surface.

> **Designed in §26 (2026-06-11).** The activity-half fold is **§26.D** — and §26 reframes it: the background-run *provenance* "what it did" and the workflow *node* structure (§25) are the **same dropped facet** (run STRUCTURE), so the memory fold and the workflow fold share one authority (§26.A). §26.E also answers §24's "no forcing function" worry: the anti-drift teeth relocate from "no second SURFACE" (which can't fire on the legitimate facts surface) to "no second RUN-ACTIVITY RENDERER" (which catches the `MemorySurface` activity section rendering `PresenceRun` outside the unified run render).


## §25 — The workflow fold (§15.C): what landed in the one window, and what didn't (honest accounting, 2026-06-11)

§15.C folded the standalone workflow window into the one interaction window. Code/live check (2026-06-11): the fold IS shipped — `core.workflow-surface` is retired in both the Java `CoreSurfaceCatalog` and the FE `CorePlugin` (a second visible workflow surface is now an `interaction-surface` gate failure). Where each former workflow-window feature now lives:

- **Launch** → `UnifiedChatView.renderWorkflowTrigger` (≈L2000): a "Workflow: `<id>`" + **"Run workflow"** affordance shown while the `core.workflow-run` shape is mounted; clicking calls `AgentSessionController.runWorkflow(id)` (≈L890), which injects a "Run workflow: …" user turn and streams the run into the SAME conversation.
- **Run render** (former `NodeProgress` / `ToolResult`) → the unified run render: the conversation timeline + the §13/§21 run-spine + `jf-tool-call-card`. The workflow shape emits the SAME `tool_call_*` / `chunk` / `done` vocabulary as the agent, so it populates the same `projectLiveAgentActivity` model — no bespoke surface.
- **Approvals / gates** (former private `requestAuthorization`) → the shared `<jf-authorization-host>` ceremony (550 C3) — the same one agent tool calls use.

**Three honest gaps the fold left (the un-built remainder):**

1. **The node-graph identity is FLATTENED, not preserved.** The workflow-specific events — `workflow_started` / `node_started` / `node_completed` — have NO handler in `AgentSessionController.dispatchEvent` (L726–752), so they are silently no-op'd (the §15.C comment states this verbatim). The render shows the tool calls / text / progress the nodes produced, merged into the one run timeline — NOT an explicit "node 1 → node 2 → node N" structure. This is the deliberate "a run is a run" simplification, but it means the workflow's STRUCTURE (its DAG shape, node boundaries) is invisible in the window. Whether that structure deserves a projection (node boundaries as run-spine landmarks, or a collapsible per-node grouping of the unified items) is an open design question, not a decided drop.

2. **The launcher is a single hardcoded demo; no picker.** `UnifiedChatView.WORKFLOW_ID = 'core.demo-compose'` (L337) is the ONE workflow wired in. A multi-workflow PICKER over a workflows-list API is an explicit, un-built follow-on (the inline comment says so). Today the window runs THE demo workflow, not a chosen one.

3. **The graph/DAG authoring view is not built.** §14.2 / §15.C kept "graph-for-design" a separate concern from "stream-for-run"; the run half folded in, but the node/edge authoring/debug view does not exist anywhere now (the surface that might have hosted it was retired). A DAG editor, if ever wanted, is net-new — not a 565 fold residual.

**Remaining-work additions (ledger):** (a) a workflows-list API + a picker affordance to replace the hardcoded `WORKFLOW_ID`; (b) a decision on whether to project the workflow's node structure into the unified run (node-boundary run-spine landmarks / per-node grouping) or accept the flatten; (c) the DAG authoring view is out-of-scope net-new, explicitly NOT a fold residual.

> **Designed in §26 (2026-06-11).** These three ledger items — and §24's memory activity-half fold — are no longer loose remaining-work; §26 (the RUN-STRUCTURE tier) is their correct-structure design. Item (b) is **§26.A/§26.B** (the run-segmentation authority; node boundaries → segment landmarks), item (a) is **§26.C** (the launcher as a mode-catalog projection), item (c) stays out (**§26.B**, graph-for-design). The §24 memory fold is **§26.D**. Read §26 for the unified diagnosis (workflow-node structure and background-run provenance are *two values of one dropped facet*).

## §26 — The RUN-STRUCTURE tier (design theory, 2026-06-11) — one run-segmentation authority; the workflow node-graph and the background-memory activity are its two adopters

> **Status: design theory.** Feasibility disregarded; major re-seats in scope; reuses the §13/§21 navigation primitives, `AgentRunStore`, 561's mode-catalog + retrospective-panel, and the `interaction-surface`/`run-renderers` gates; invents **no new kernel** — it is §15.E applied to the run's STRUCTURE leaf. Not implemented in this pass; the user lands the build later. This section supersedes the §24/§25 "open question / ledger" framing by *designing* it.
>
> **Lineage.** This tier stands on the same external benchmark §14 recorded (the convergent 2026 standard — one streamed typed-block run timeline + a persistent navigation rail; workflow = *stream-for-run, graph-for-design*; memory = inline activity vs a durable "manage" backstop). A fresh 2026-06-11 web pass re-confirmed it (AG-UI's lifecycle/`STEP_*` events; Claude-Code/Fazm's grouped collapsible run blocks + the elapsed-time-as-co-presence cue; ChatGPT's inline "Memory updated" write-cue + a separate manage surface; Manus's live node-by-node activity timeline). The category renders a run's STRUCTURE in-line; §15.C's flatten does not — that is the gap this tier closes, structurally.

### §26.0 — Diagnosis: §15.C's flatten unified the run RECORD but dropped the run's STRUCTURE facet

§15.C folded the workflow run into the one window under the thesis *"a run is a run."* That was **correct for the common case** and it shipped (§15.H, §25): the workflow shares the agent `tool_call_*`/`chunk`/`done` vocabulary, so its steps populate the same `projectLiveAgentActivity` model and render as unified turns + `jf-tool-call-card` + the shared `<jf-authorization-host>`. But "a run is a run" unified the run's **content** (its steps and their order), not the run's **structure** — *which group each step belongs to, and where each step came from.* Two facets of that structure were dropped:

- **The workflow node-graph identity (§25.1).** `WorkflowShapeRunner` *already emits* `workflow_started{workflowId,nodeCount}` / `node_started{nodeId,kind,index}` / `node_completed{…,output}`, but `AgentSessionController.dispatchEvent` has **no handler** for them (they are no-op'd by design). The render shows the steps the nodes produced, merged into one flat timeline — the node boundaries are invisible.
- **The background-run provenance (§24).** A background run *is the same entity* as an interactive run (`AgentRunStore` behind a `background` flag; `/api/presence` is a pure projection of it) — but its activity is rendered in a **second** place (`MemorySurface`'s "while you were away" section, reading `PresenceRun` directly), never folded into the conversation's run history.

**The unifying observation (the reframe §24/§25 lacked).** These are not two features — they are **one missing facet with two values**: *"which group / which origin does this timeline item belong to?"* — node `N` of a workflow, or the `background` episode that ran while you were away. The reason both were dropped is the **same**: `UnifiedTurnItem` is a **strictly flat** record (`{id,ts,kind,prominence,originator,content,attributes}`) with no typed place to carry group/origin, so the structure had nowhere to live but the **untyped `attributes` escape hatch** — and an untyped escape hatch is a value no renderer is *forced* to read, so it was no-op'd (workflow) or never projected (memory). This is **exactly the §15 leaf-fork class, one tier deeper**: a trunk unification (the run record, §3.C/§15.C) that never reached a leaf (the run's *internal structure*), because — per §15.E — *unification at the trunk does not propagate to a leaf unless the authority's typed seam reaches it or a register positively covers it, and neither did.*

### §26.A — The one run-segmentation authority (the dropped facet, given a typed home)

**End-state.** Every timeline item carries a **typed segment-membership** — the single authority for *"which group/origin is this?"*:

```
RunSegmentRef { runId; originKind: 'interactive' | 'background' | 'workflow'; nodeId?; nodeKind?; label? }
```

— a **typed field on `UnifiedTurnItem`**, replacing the untyped-`attributes` stuffing (§15.D.1's preferred mechanism: make the structure *unreproducible except through the authority*, so a renderer cannot invent its own grouping). **One projector** is its sole producer — the natural extension of `projectUnifiedThread` (record side) and `projectLiveAgentActivity` (live side); **both** structure-consumers read it and only it: the **spine landmark feed** (segment boundaries → landmarks) and the **conversation body** (segment → a collapsible group). The node identity (§25.1) and the background provenance (§24) are the *same field*, two values of `originKind`/`nodeId`.

**What this is NOT — the model stays FLAT.** Segmentation is a **declared grouping over the flat item list**, not nesting in the render contract. `UnifiedTurnItem[]` remains a 1-D ordered stream (the property §12/§13 depend on, and the property the category converged on — *one* timeline, not a tree of panes); a segment is a *(start,end,meta)* span over that stream, exactly as the §21 `Landmark` is a *(top,bottom)* extent over the same stream. This is the deliberate AHA boundary: unify the *grouping mechanism*, not the *item model* — the flatten was right about the items, wrong only about having nowhere to record the spans.

### §26.B — Workflow as the canonical >1-segment adopter (not a special case)

**End-state.** Wire the already-emitted, currently-no-op'd structural events into §26.A: `node_started` **opens** a segment (`originKind:'workflow', nodeId, nodeKind, label`), `node_completed` **closes** it; the steps streamed between them inherit that `RunSegmentRef`. Then the two consumers render the structure with primitives that **already exist**:

- **Spine** → segment boundaries become a new prominence tier of **`Landmark`** (`navigation.ts`), feeding the same `deriveFocus` / `jumpTo` / interpolation machinery the §21 spine already runs — node boundaries get the *anchor* weight (like a turn), intra-node steps stay the *interpolated texture* (§19), and the existing terminal-node-weight logic generalizes to "segment-terminal."
- **Body** → each segment renders as a **collapsible group header** over its steps, reusing the existing `<details class="run-trace">` grouping that `jumpTo` already opens on a click-through (`navigation.ts` opens `<details>` ancestors). A workflow node is a labelled `<details>`; an agent run with no nodes is **one implicit segment = the whole run** (the degenerate case).

So **workflow is not special** — it is simply the run with **>1 segment**; the agent run is the **1-segment** case; the same projector + spine + body render both. This is the precise structural reading of the category's *"stream-for-run"* (§14.2): the run renders as a **stream of labelled segments**, which is all the backend can express anyway — it emits a linear `index` and a `nodeCount`, **no edges**. The DAG/edge **authoring** view stays **out** (§25.3 net-new, not a fold residual): there is no edge data in the run stream to render, and §14.2's *graph-for-design* is a separate concern from *stream-for-run*. If a node ever fans out (parallel branches), the segment model degrades gracefully to concurrent open segments — still spans over the one stream, still no tree in the render contract.

### §26.C — Workflow discovery as a mode-catalog projection (the picker — §25.2)

**End-state.** The hardcoded `UnifiedChatView.WORKFLOW_ID = 'core.demo-compose'` (and the single-entry `CoreWorkflowCatalog`) is a **fork of 561's mode-catalog authority** — the same "a hardcoded `ShapeId` union inside one view's source" anti-pattern 561 §2.2 named and dissolved. The correct structure: the backend **projects `CoreWorkflowCatalog`** through an endpoint (a `/api/workflows` read-view, or a facet of the existing shape/mode catalog), and the launcher becomes a **projection of that catalog** — a picker selected from the declared set, exactly as 561 §2.2 makes a mode "a declared catalog the projection engine selects and renders from, not a hardcoded union." This reuses the existing affordance machinery (`renderWorkflowTrigger` becomes "pick a workflow → run it" instead of "run THE workflow"); no new render kernel. A workflow is a point in 561's autonomy×grounding×persistence space (autonomy-high, a declared `shapeId`), so the picker is the same control surface modes already use — workflow discovery and mode selection are one concept.

### §26.D — The memory split as the run-provenance facet + a 561 retrospective panel (§24)

**End-state — two moves, each through an authority that already exists:**

1. **Conversation-linked background runs fold into the run history via §26.A.** A background run launched *from a conversation* carries that `conversationId`, so it already flows through the **same** `/api/thread/{id}` + `listRunIdsByConversation` path the chat window loads its history from — and renders as an `originKind:'background'` **segment** (§26.A), visually marked but otherwise a run like any other. The only gap is mechanical: `/api/presence/run` currently schedules with `conversationId=null`, orphaning the run from every conversation. The correct structure carries the conversationId, so *"what it did while you were away, in this conversation"* is **just runs, some flagged background, all through the one render** — no second renderer. (This is the frontier "inline activity" pattern: the run's own provenance, surfaced in place, not a separate inbox.)

2. **The cross-conversation inbox becomes a declared retrospective PANEL of the one window (561 §2.3).** Background runs with no conversation (the genuine "while you were away" aggregate across the whole app) surface as a **retrospective panel** of the one interaction surface — a `consumesProjection` re-mount of the presence projection, modeled exactly on 561 §2.3's Sessions/Timeline/History panels — **not** a section glued onto a second standalone surface. The durable **facts** half ("what it knows") deliberately **stays** the separate `core.memory-surface` (§14/§24: *"what it knows" ≠ "what it did"* — the ChatGPT split, the category-correct boundary). So `MemorySurface` **splits along the line the code already cleanly separates**: facts → its own peer surface (unchanged); activity → (1) conversation segments + (2) a retrospective panel of the one window.

### §26.E — Anti-drift teeth: relocate the forcing function from "one surface" to "one run-activity renderer" (the §15.E completion)

> **Corrected by §26.G (2026-06-11, later-wins):** the run-renderers register is **import-visible only** (§12.10), so it CANNOT by itself catch a `MemorySurface` that renders `PresenceRun` with its own non-importing markup. The real teeth are the **typed `RunSegmentRef` seam + deleting the forked render path** (the register demoted to import-visible early-warning). Read the prose below with that correction; §26.G has the precise mechanism.

§24.3 diagnosed precisely why the memory fold never happened where the workflow fold did: workflow had a **forcing function** (the `interaction-surface` gate makes a second visible workflow surface a build failure), and memory does **not** — because `core.memory-surface` is a **legitimate** declared surface (it correctly holds the durable facts §26.D keeps separate), so a surface-counting gate *must not* fire on it. A surface-level gate is the **wrong leaf** for this tier.

**The correct teeth — name the actual leaf, reach it with a register (§15.E).** The leaf that must be unforkable here is **run-activity rendering**, not surface count. Grow the **`run-renderers` register** (the §12.6/§15.D.2 positive-coverage gate) to cover **the one run-segmentation projection + the one run-activity render path**: every site that renders run activity must go through `projectUnifiedThread`/`projectLiveAgentActivity` + the segment authority. Under that coverage, the `MemorySurface` "while you were away" section rendering `PresenceRun` **directly** — bypassing the unified run render — becomes exactly the **fork the gate catches**, the same way a second inline-`[n]` weave fails the §15.D.2 coverage. The forcing function moves from *"there must be one surface"* (false for memory) to *"there must be one run-activity renderer"* (true for both workflow and memory) — which is the §15.E meta-principle applied verbatim: *a unification is complete only when its leaves are unforkable; name the leaf, reach it with a seam (the typed `RunSegmentRef`, §26.A) or a register (run-activity coverage, here).* The typed `RunSegmentRef` is the seam (preferred); the register is the fallback for the render path the type cannot brand.

### §26.F — Reuse boundary, residual decisions, and the meta-principle

- **Reuses (unchanged):** `navigation.ts` `Landmark` + `deriveFocus` + `jumpTo` + the prominence/interpolation/terminal-weight machinery (§21/§19/§13); the `<details class="run-trace">` collapsible grouping; `AgentRunStore`'s `background` flag + the presence projection + `listRunIdsByConversation` (§15.C, §24); 561's mode-catalog (§2.2) + retrospective-panel (§2.3) concepts; the `interaction-surface` + `run-renderers` gates; the already-emitted workflow structural events.
- **Extends:** `UnifiedTurnItem` with the typed `RunSegmentRef` field (replacing untyped `attributes` for structure); the two projectors (sole producers of the segment refs); the spine landmark feed (segment-boundary tier); the body render (segment → `<details>` group); the `run-renderers` register coverage (run-activity path); `CoreWorkflowCatalog` → a projected catalog endpoint; `/api/presence/run` → carry `conversationId`.
- **Adds no new kernel.** This is §15.E applied to the run-STRUCTURE leaf — the same single-authority → governed-projection → register-backed-gate move, one tier below §15's grounded-claim leaf.
- **Open decisions (named, not defaulted, per AHA / §15.A discipline):** (i) the exact `RunSegmentRef` shape — whether `originKind` and the workflow `nodeId`/`nodeKind` are one field or a small sum type, decided against the live event payloads; (ii) whether the cross-conversation inbox (§26.D.2) is a panel *of the one surface* or a slim peer surface — a 561-panel-vs-surface call to make against the actual chrome; (iii) whether a segment's collapsed/expanded default is density-driven (§19) or origin-driven (workflow nodes expanded, background runs collapsed). None blocks the design; each is an implementation-time calibration.
- **Meta-principle (stated once, for the next tier):** *a run is not fully rendered until its STRUCTURE — the grouping of its steps and the origin of its activity — lives in one typed facet that the timeline, the spine, and the body all project from; a flat stream with structure stuffed in an untyped escape hatch is a fork waiting to be no-op'd.* The §15.E rule ("name the leaves, reach each with a seam or a gate") extended from *"a grounded claim in a run"* to *"the shape of a run."*
- **Validation discipline unchanged (§9):** every user-visible piece of any eventual implementation is declared done only on a **freshly-built dist in the real browser** (the §10/§13.8 stale-dist lesson), with an independent reviewer ≠ committer and a measured whole-screen UX audit (§9; honor-system since 563 retired the gates) — never on green unit tests alone.

## §26.G — De-risk pass (2026-06-11): the six load-bearing assumptions probed against source, and the ONE correction (§26.E)

Before any of §26 is built, its load-bearing assumptions were verified against the worktree source (the §15.G/§17.G/§21.8 discipline — a code trace beats a degraded-env live read; per the dated-history rule, **this pass wins over §26 where it corrects a claim**). Six probes, static; **five validated** (two sharpened), **one corrected** (§26.E). No production code, no merge.

- **P1 — §26.A "one projector both sides" — VALIDATED + SHARPENED.** The workflow structural events ARE persisted: `WorkflowShapeRunner`'s `psink` mirrors **every** streamed event — including `workflow_started`/`node_started`/`node_completed` — to `RunEventStore.appendEvent` (`WorkflowShapeRunner.java:152-174,216-223`), and the record-side `AgentLoopService.threadEvents` reads **all** of them via `runStore.readEvents` → `AgentInteractionMapper.fromRunEvent` (`AgentLoopService.java:900-902`). So the node data is on disk and on the read path **both sides** — no backend persistence change needed (§26.A's success-bar (a)). **Sharpening:** today `fromRunEvent` maps `node_*` to `Optional.empty()` (the `default` case, `AgentInteractionMapper.java:155`) — so they are dropped before the FE projector sees them. The bracketing therefore belongs in the **FE projection layer** (`projectUnifiedThread`/`projectLiveAgentActivity`, both → `UnifiedTurnItem[]` — the genuinely shared "one projector"), and the record side's required change is precise: **un-drop `node_started`/`node_completed` in `fromRunEvent`** (surface them onto the wire, see P6) so the FE projector can run the same stateful open/close pass over the record stream that it runs live. Confidence **9/10**.
- **P2 — §26.D.1 "a background run with a conversationId already flows through `/api/thread`" — VALIDATED.** `AgentRunStore.listRunIdsByConversation` filters by `conversationId.equals(meta.get("conversationId"))` **only** — no `background` filter, no shape filter (`AgentRunStore.java:386-405`); `threadEvents` + `lifecycles` inherit that (`AgentLoopService.java:880-925`). The `background=true` filter lives exclusively on the *other* path (`presenceRunsSince`, L935). So a background run that carries a conversationId surfaces in `/api/thread` unchanged; the **only** change §26.D.1 needs is the producer carrying the id (`/api/presence/run` passes `conversationId=null` today). Confidence **9/10**.
- **P3 — §26.D.2 "retrospective panel" dependency — VALIDATED (better than feared) + CORRECTED downward in cost.** The retrospective mechanism is **already built**: a retrospective **drawer** (`retrospectiveDrawer.ts`/`toggleRetrospective`) + `RetrospectivePanel.ts`, opened from `UnifiedChatView`'s "Activity" button (`UnifiedChatView.ts:1137,1457`), already mounting Sessions/Timeline/History. So §26.D.2's cross-conversation inbox is a **reuse** — add a presence-backed section to the existing drawer — **not** a 561-surface-tier prerequisite (the §26.D.2 worst case is retired). Confidence **8/10**.
- **P4 — §26.B "node events bracket the steps" — VALIDATED.** `WorkflowShapeRunner.run` is a strictly sequential `for (WorkflowNode node : workflow.nodes())` loop: `node_started` → the node body (which emits `chunk`/`tool_call_*` via `psink`) → `node_completed` → `index++` (`WorkflowShapeRunner.java:170-225`). Strict bracketing, linear index, **no fan-out/concurrency**. So the §26.B open/close grouping is well-defined, and the "concurrent-open-segments" hedge in §26.B is **forward-compat speculation only** (not needed by today's backend — named as such, not a current requirement). Confidence **9/10**.
- **P5 — §26.E "the run-renderers register catches the MemorySurface fork" — CORRECTED.** The `run-renderers` gate is **import-visible only** by its own declared scope (§12.10; `check-run-renderers.mjs:20-25`, `run-renderers.v1.json` `description`): it catches a fork that *imports* the canonical symbols or *mounts* the canonical tag. A `MemorySurface` rendering `PresenceRun` with its **own** markup imports nothing canonical — so it is exactly the import-invisible blind spot, and the register **cannot** force the memory fold. §26.E's "the register catches it" claim is **overstated and is corrected here.** The real forcing function is two structural moves the register only *guards*: **(1)** make run-activity rendering require a **branded `RunSegmentRef`/`UnifiedTurnItem`** the projection alone can mint (the §15.D.1 typed seam, exactly as `GroundingTier`/`StepPresentation` are branded) — so a hand-rolled `PresenceRun` render *cannot* fabricate one; **(2)** **delete** the forked `/api/presence`-direct render path in `MemorySurface` so there is no second renderer to drift, and the inbox (P3's drawer section) consumes the unified projection. The register stays the **import-visible early-warning** that a *new* second renderer isn't added, with the honest §12.10 ceiling named (a fully hand-rolled render still slips the grep — the same ceiling as every other run-renderer check). Net: the teeth are **seam + deletion** (real), not register-alone (insufficient). Confidence in the *corrected* teeth **7/10**.
- **P6 — §26.A/§26.C mechanics — VALIDATED.** `UnifiedTurnItem` is the **FE projection contract** (not a 564-generated wire type); the wire row is `ThreadEvent` with an untyped `attributes: Record<string,unknown>` bag (`unifiedThreadProjection.ts:15-30`). So the typed `RunSegmentRef` field is **FE-internal (cheap)**, transported via the existing `attributes` bag — **no 564 schema regen** (a dedicated wire `kind` *would* need regen; avoid it). For the picker: the `Workflow` record already carries a `Presentation(label, description)` (`Workflow.java:14-20`; `CoreWorkflowCatalog.demoCompose` populates `registry-workflow.demo-compose.{label,description}`), and `WorkflowCatalog` is a real registry type — so the §26.C `/api/workflows` projection is a **clean registry-emitter projection** mirroring the existing `UIOperationEmitter`/operations-catalog pattern, **no new backend field**. Confidence **9/10**.

**Net.** §26's structure is sound and cheaper than written in three places (node_* already persisted; the retrospective drawer already exists; the picker has its label data). The **one substantive correction is §26.E** — the anti-drift teeth are the typed `RunSegmentRef` seam + deleting the forked render, with the register demoted to import-visible early-warning (the §12.10 honest limit, consistent with §15.D.1's "prefer the seam over the grep gate"). One sharpening on §26.A (the bracketing pass lives in the FE projection; the record side's job is to stop dropping `node_*`). No probe refuted the design; no fatal surprise. The §15.G-style live calibration (a real workflow run + a real background run, observed in the browser) is the residual gate, deferred to implementation per §9 — and note the §15.H env boundary still applies (the only catalogued workflow, `core.demo-compose`, fails validation without the `vendor.mcphost.*` pack, so the live arm needs either that pack or a second catalogued workflow).

## §26.H — Implementation outcome (2026-06-11) — the RUN-STRUCTURE tier SHIPPED (all three phases; live-verified)

§26 was implemented in the `worktree-565-grounding-hardening` worktree (never on `main`; no merge — the user lands it). As-built, with verification:

**Phase 1 — §26.A/§26.B the run-segmentation authority + workflow node segments (closes §25.1).**
- `unifiedThreadProjection.ts` — the typed `RunSegmentRef { originKind: 'interactive'|'background'|'workflow', nodeId?, nodeKind?, label? }` field on `UnifiedTurnItem`; the ONE shared `assignRunSegments(items)` pass (consumes `progress` boundary markers, stamps each bracketed item's segment, drops the markers); called at the tail of BOTH `projectUnifiedThread` (record) and `projectLiveAgentActivity` (live).
- Record side: `AgentInteractionMapper.fromRunEvent` stops dropping `node_started`/`node_completed` -> emits them as `PROGRESS` boundary events (no wire change; rides the untyped `attributes` bag, per §26.G P6).
- Live side: `AgentSessionController` — a `run-node` `ConversationEntry` + `onNodeBoundary` handlers wired into `dispatchEvent` (the events §25.1 found no-op'd).
- Render: `UnifiedChatView.renderTimeline` partitions the flat stream into consecutive segments; a workflow node renders as a labelled `<section class="run-segment">` (header = node label + kind chip) wrapping the unchanged intra-node composition; the spine marks each segment's first item `.node-boundary`. An agent run with no nodes is the degenerate one-segment case (renders exactly as before).
- Anti-drift (§26.E, corrected per §26.G): the `run-renderers` register gained a `runSegments` authority (only the projection module computes `assignRunSegments`) — import-visible early-warning; the typed `RunSegmentRef` seam is the real teeth.

**Phase 2 — §26.C the workflow picker (replaces the hardcoded `WORKFLOW_ID`, §25.2).**
- Backend: `UIWorkflowEmitter` (the lean picker-wire authority — id + i18n label/description + node list) + `RegistryController.handleWorkflows` + the `GET /api/registry/workflows` route + the `CoreWorkflowCatalog` injection (a new 9-arg `RegistryController` ctor; the 8-arg delegates with empty workflows).
- A model-only fixture workflow `core.research-brief` (two `LlmStep` nodes, no `vendor.mcphost.*`) so the picker has >=2 entries AND a runnable target in any stack with the chat model (the §15.H `demo-compose` env boundary).
- FE: `WorkflowCatalogClient` (light parse) + the picker `<select>` in `UnifiedChatView.renderWorkflowTrigger`; labels resolve through the ONE display projector (`present()` gained a `workflow` `EntityRef` kind — the presentation-purity fix).

**Phase 3 — §26.D the memory activity fold.**
- Backend: `InteractionThreadController.handlePresenceRun` threads `conversationId` into the `AgentRequest`; `AgentLoopService.threadEvents` wraps a conversation-linked BACKGROUND run's events in `origin=background` boundary markers (the §26.A authority brackets them).
- FE: the `MemorySurface` activity half (presence list + run-launcher + `/api/presence` reads) was DELETED (the §26.E fork-deletion) — it is now facts-only; the inbox is a 4th `Inbox` tab on the existing `RetrospectivePanel` (+ `AgentSessionController.loadPresence`/`runBackgroundTask`). `core.memory-surface` stays registered (the durable-facts peer).

**Static verification (all green):** `./gradlew.bat build -x test` BUILD SUCCESSFUL (all gates incl. `class-size` — a `565-run-structure-tier` declared-growth changeset covers `AgentLoopService` 1057->1098 + `LocalApiServer` 2542->2550); `:modules:ui:test`/`:app-agent:test`/`:app-services:test` green (+ new `AgentInteractionMapperTest` node-boundary case, `UIWorkflowEmitterTest`); FE `tsc` clean + 2688 unit tests (+ `assignRunSegments` workflow + background cases, the `RetrospectivePanel` 4-tab update); the `run-renderers` + `interaction-surface` + `controls-a11y` + `presentation-purity` + `a11y-closure` + layout/composition/adaptive/message gates all pass.

**Live-browser verification (2026-06-11, real browser, worktree Vite :5188 -> worktree-jars backend :57094, Meta-Llama-3.1-8B online).** The worktree backend was run by placing the worktree's freshly-built module jars into the dev-runner's dist + restart (skipBuild), and the worktree FE via a worktree Vite proxying `/api` to it. Verified, with screenshots + DOM probes in the transcript:
- **§26.C picker** — the launcher shows a `<select>` listing both catalogued workflows with derived labels + node counts ("Demo Compose · 4 nodes", "Research Brief · 2 nodes"); selecting Research Brief + Run streamed it into the one window.
- **§26.A/§26.B node segments** — the workflow run rendered as TWO labelled node segments, "think `llm`" and "draft `llm`" (`origin-workflow`), each wrapping its node's output; `mergedTimeline` confirmed two `workflow:think`/`workflow:draft` segments with the boundary markers consumed.
- **§26.D background segment** — a background run launched with the conversationId (`POST /api/presence/run`) joined `/api/thread` wrapped in `origin=background` boundary markers (13 events); the FE projection bracketed it into ONE rendered "Background activity" segment (`origin-background`, "background" chip) holding the prompt + the 3-step trace + the answer. The `Inbox` tab + run-in-background composer render in the retrospective drawer.
- **The facts surface** — `core.memory-surface` renders facts-only ("Memory" / "What it knows" with the learned fact + "Teach it a durable fact..."), no activity section — the §26.D split confirmed.

**Honest residuals (named, not hidden):**
1. **Workflow RELOAD brackets empty nodes.** `WorkflowShapeRunner` *swallows* each `LlmStep`'s streamed chunks (it captures them for the next node's input and emits only the workflow's single terminal `done`), so the persisted record carries the node *boundaries* but no in-node assistant events — a reloaded workflow run shows empty node brackets + the final answer outside them. The LIVE run is correct (chunks interleave between the `run-node` entries — verified). Closing the reload gap means persisting per-node output as an in-node event in `WorkflowShapeRunner` — a backend-persistence follow-up, out of the segment-authority scope.
2. **Spine node-boundary marker visually unconfirmed.** The `.node-boundary` spine tick is code-complete + gate-clean, but the run-spine renders only at the wide breakpoint, which the verification window did not trigger — the body segments (the primary §26.B render) were the confirmed visual. Worth a wide-window pass at closure.
3. **§26.E teeth are import-visible** (per the §26.G correction) — the typed `RunSegmentRef` seam + the fork-deletion are the real forcing function; the register is early-warning.

**Net: every §26.A–E user-visible behavior was confirmed rendering correctly in the real browser. NOT merged to `main`.**

## §26.I — Hardening pass (2026-06-11) — four critical-analysis fixes, live-verified + independently reviewed

A deep critical analysis of §26 (against the tempdoc's own principles — "a run is a run rendered identically live AND on reload"; "true in every mode by construction"; the kernel's unforkable third leg) found four issues. All four are now fixed in the worktree (never on `main`; no merge — the user lands it).

**Fix A — workflow RELOAD rendered empty node segments (the real defect).** `WorkflowShapeRunner.runLlmStep` streamed each LlmStep's text as transient `chunk`s (live-only) and swallowed the sub-shape `done`, so the persisted record carried node boundaries but no in-bracket content; on reload the nodes were empty and the workflow's single terminal `done` (last node's output) sorted outside the brackets. Fix: the runner now emits a durable `node_output` event (full text) for each LlmStep, INSIDE the node bracket; `AgentInteractionMapper.fromRunEvent` maps `node_output` → `ASSISTANT_MESSAGE` and SKIPS the assistant for a `done` carrying `nodesExecuted` (a workflow terminal — its finalResponse merely repeats the last node, so skipping prevents a double-render). An agent `done` (no `nodesExecuted`) is still the answer. → reload now brackets each node's real content, identical to live.

**Fix B — brand `RunSegmentRef`** (the typed seam, §15.D.1). `unifiedThreadProjection.ts` makes it `{…} & { readonly __runSegment: unique symbol }`, minted ONLY by the `as RunSegmentRef` cast inside `assignRunSegments` (mirroring `GroundingTier`). A second renderer that tries to fabricate a segment is now a TYPE error — the segmentation leaf is unforkable by construction. (The residual memory-fork class stays at the §12.10 import-visible ceiling — the register early-warning is honestly retained, not "fixed".)

**Fix C — stack-based `assignRunSegments`.** The single `open` ref became a STACK (push on `start`, pop on `end`); an item gets the innermost open segment; missing-`end` brackets to EOF; stray-`end` is a no-op. Robust by construction regardless of any future backend concurrency. +3 unit tests (nested / missing-end / stray-end).

**Fix D — spine node-boundary marker, verified.** The `.node-boundary` tick renders only at the wide breakpoint (`min-width: 64rem`), which the prior verification window (capped at 991px) never hit. Forcing the wide condition confirmed both nodes render their boundary tick + aria-label ("Node: think — jump", "Node: draft — jump").

**The independent review caught a MAJOR latent ordering defect Fix A missed — now fixed.** A reviewer (≠ implementer) found that `node_output` and `node_completed` are emitted back-to-back and routinely share a millisecond; the FE sort (`ts || id.localeCompare`, `ts` truncated to ms) then decided via the id, and the OLD ids sorted `node-end` (`e`) before `node-output` (`o`) — re-surfacing the "output outside the bracket" bug on the tie path (the prior live test passed only because the timestamps happened to differ). Fix: `AgentInteractionMapper.nodeEventId` builds all three node ids as `…:node:<5-digit index>:<role 1=start|2=output|3=end>:<nodeId>:<ms>` so LEXICAL order == TEMPORAL order on a tie — both within a node (1<2<3) and cross-node (node N end < node N+1 start, via the index). `WorkflowShapeRunner` now carries `index` on `node_output`. +2 FE projection tests with same-`occurredAt` events (single-node + cross-node) + a Java test pinning the id format. A second independent reviewer confirmed the defect RESOLVED (PASS, no blockers).

**Static verification (all green):** `./gradlew.bat build -x test` BUILD SUCCESSFUL (all gates incl. class-size); `:modules:app-agent:test` + `:app-services:test` (node_output emission in-bracket; the node_output→assistant + workflow-done-skip mapping; the pinned id format); FE `tsc` clean + 2693 unit tests (the stack + same-ms-tie cases).

**Live-browser verification (2026-06-11, worktree Vite :5188 → worktree-jars backend :60696, Meta-Llama-3.1-8B online).** Ran the 2-node `core.research-brief` workflow, then PROJECTED its persisted `/api/thread` record (the reload path): each node segment's markdown block carried the node's REAL output — think → "The topic 'Impact of Climate Change on Global Food Security'…", draft → "This research brief explores…" — with exactly 2 assistants (no duplicate final answer). Before Fix A these brackets were empty. The spine (forced wide) showed both node-boundary ticks. Screenshots + DOM probes in the transcript. The dev stack (taken over with user approval after an OWNER_CONFLICT) was released and main's dist restored afterward.

**Net: all four issues + the review-caught ordering defect are fixed, statically green, and live-verified; two independent review rounds (find → fix → confirm). NOT merged to `main`.**

§26 was committed (`97b59ca61`) and `origin/main` (81 commits ahead, dominated by the 574 presentation-kernel effort) was merged into the branch (`d74ce8247`). The branch is now `main + §26`, a clean fast-forward for landing (NOT landed — the user lands branch→main).

**Conflicts (8 of 27 §26 files overlapped main; 5 auto-merged, 3 textual):**
- `MemorySurface.ts` — kept §26.D facts-only AND adopted 574's `JfElement` base + `jf-button` (the deleted activity half stays deleted; main's button migration applied to the kept facts half).
- `observations.md` / `class-size-exceptions.txt` — union of both sides (my §26 pins + main's; the obsolete WorkflowCatalogClient note dropped since the comment was fixed).

**574 substrate reconciliation (the real work, mostly auto-merged + verified):**
- The run-spine's wide-check rode `wideRailMql` (pre-574); 574 replaced it with the shared `responsiveState`/`wideViewport` authority. Git merged main's `this.wideViewport` change into my `renderRunSpine` — the §26 node-boundary logic now reads the 574 breakpoint authority, no manual adaptation needed.
