**Live re-verify on the merged 574 substrate (worktree Vite :5188 → merged-jars backend :59947, model online):** the §26.C picker renders ("Demo Compose · 4 nodes"); a `core.research-brief` run renders as labelled node segments ("think llm", "draft llm") with their content; the §26.I Fix A reload persists each node's output as an `ASSISTANT_MESSAGE` inside its bracket with no duplicate — all rendering correctly on 574's `JfElement`/`responsiveState`/token substrate (no presentation-kernel regression). The Inbox tab is unit-verified on the merged code (`RetrospectivePanel.test.ts` 4-tab assertion). Stack released + main's dist restored afterward.

**Net: §26 is merged up to current main, conflict-resolved, 574-reconciled, fully green, and live-confirmed on the merged substrate.**

**LANDED 2026-06-11 — `origin/main` fast-forwarded to `da41cb77b`.** Post-merge fix: the merged `LocalApiServer` measured 2566 LOC (not the provisional 2559 pin set during conflict resolution — the worktree gate had passed only because the §26 changeset masked the discrepancy); the pin + the §26 class-size changeset were corrected and the post-merge `build -x test` re-verified green against the origin/main baseline before the push.

## §27 — Indirect / follow-on work surfaced by §26 (ledger, 2026-06-11)

§26 landed (origin/main da41cb77b). Implementing + landing it surfaced indirect ripples — work §26 *creates or exposes* rather than work §26 *is*. Recorded here, prioritized by obligation vs robustness vs optional. (Design theory; not yet implemented; the confidence/de-risk pass is §27.G.)

**§27.1 — Canonical-doc drift (an OBLIGATION; the hard rule "canonical docs must not drift").** §26 shipped architecture/API changes the *tempdoc* (dated history) records but the *canonical* docs do not:
- `docs/reference/api-contract-map.md` — add `GET /api/registry/workflows` (the §26.C picker wire; currently only operations/resources/prompts are listed) and the `conversationId` field now accepted by `POST /api/presence/run` (§26.D).
- `docs/explanation/22-agent-system-architecture.md` — the §26 RUN-STRUCTURE authority (the workflow run renders its NODE structure, not a pure §15.C flatten), the workflow PICKER, and the memory ACTIVITY fold (background runs as `background` conversation segments + the drawer inbox). The doc already cites §15.C, so it is the natural supersession site.
- `docs/explanation/10-ui-ux-design.md` (or the memory-surface description) — the memory surface is now FACTS-ONLY; the activity/inbox moved to the retrospective drawer.
- Then the post-edit discipline: `node scripts/docs/llmstxt-generate.mjs` + `node scripts/docs/skills-sync.mjs`.

**§27.2 — The live-side entry-id ordering (a robustness gap §26.I EXPOSED).** §26.I made the RECORD-side node ids temporally sortable (`…:node:<index>:<role>:…`) so same-ms ties cannot mis-bracket. But the LIVE side still keys entries `e-N`, which sorts lexically (`e-10 < e-2`) — the same tie-inversion the record side is now immune to, on any run with >9 entries. §26.I made the asymmetry conspicuous. The fix (zero-pad `AgentSessionController.nextEntryId`, OR a numeric sort tiebreaker in `projectLiveAgentActivity`) hardens the whole live projection's tie-ordering, not only node boundaries. Contained; finishes the §26.I pass.

**§27.3 — Verification / baseline ripples.**
- ui-shot baselines: the memory-surface render changed (facts-only). If a `jseval ui-check` step captures it, its baseline is stale and should be regenerated, else the visual gate flags the intended §26.D change as a regression.
- Two live residuals §26.H/§26.J left unconfirmed by harness limits: the spine node-boundary tick (only FORCED-verified — the automation viewport capped at 991px below the 1024px breakpoint) and the inbox drawer render (mounts in an overlay host the JS probe could not reach). A real wide-window pass closes both.

**§27.4 — Enabled-but-optional polish.** i18n labels for `registry-workflow.{demo-compose,research-brief}.{label,description}` (the picker currently falls back to `deriveTitle`). NOTE a real side effect to track, not necessarily act on: adding `core.research-brief` also added an agent operation `core.workflow-research-brief` (the workflow→operation projection, 560), so the agent can now invoke it as a tool.

**§27.5 — Deliberately NOT chasing.** The §26.E memory-fork ceiling (a second run-activity renderer that imports nothing is un-greppable, §12.10 — fundamental; the branded `RunSegmentRef` already hardened the segmentation leaf); the DAG authoring view (§25.3); more core workflows (product scope).

**Recommended batch:** §27.1 (docs — mandated) + §27.2 (live-id symmetry — real robustness) + §27.3's baseline regen. The rest stay logged follow-ons.

## §27.G — De-risk pass (2026-06-11): the §27 batch probed against source; TWO scope corrections + the high-risk item validated

Before building the §27 batch, its load-bearing assumptions were verified against the worktree source (the §23/§26.G discipline — corrections here win over §27, later-wins). Four probes; the highest-risk item validated, and the batch SHRANK (two items proved no-ops).

- **P1 — §27.2 (the live-id fix) — VALIDATED; zero-pad `nextEntryId` is safe (HIGH).** The `e-N` entry id (`AgentSessionController.nextEntryId` = `e-${++counter}`) is consumed by EXACTLY two things: (1) the sort tiebreaker `a.ts - b.ts || a.id.localeCompare(b.id)` in `projectLiveAgentActivity` (the bug — `e-10 < e-2`), and (2) the `data-item-id` (nav `jumpTo` / Lit key — format-agnostic, needs only uniqueness). It is NOT used for matching anywhere: `mergedTimeline` dedups live-vs-record by `(kind, content)` / `callId` ("live/record ids are different spaces" — `UnifiedChatView.ts:2041-2052`), and `renderLiveOverlay` dedups by the BACKEND record ids / `(kind,content)` (`:2412-2423`), not `e-N`. No test asserts the `e-N` format (grep clean). → **Zero-padding `nextEntryId` (`e-${String(++c).padStart(6,'0')}`) is a one-method, low-blast-radius change** that fixes the tiebreaker symmetrically with the §26.I record-side fix; the alternative (a stable-sort-by-ts dropping the id tiebreaker) is viable but subtler. The surprise is removed.
- **P2 — §27.1 (docs) — REFINED + one item CORRECTED to a no-op (HIGH).** `api-contract-map.md` lists the registry endpoints (operations/resources/prompts) + the `/api/messages/registry-operation/{locale}` i18n pattern (`:189-193`) — adding `GET /api/registry/workflows` + the `presence/run` `conversationId` is a purely ADDITIVE edit at a clear insertion point. `llmstxt-generate.mjs` + `skills-sync.mjs` exist (regen is clean). **CORRECTION: the memory-surface doc update is a NO-OP** — the memory surface is documented in NO canonical doc (`docs/{explanation,reference,how-to,decisions}` grep for "memory surface"/"jf-memory"/"what it knows"/"/api/memory" is empty), so there is no drift to fix there. §27.1 narrows to two additive edits (api-contract-map + the §15.C-citing region of `22-agent-system-architecture.md`).
- **P3 — §27.3 (ui-shot baseline) — CORRECTED to a no-op (HIGH).** No `ui-check` step captures the memory surface (`ui_step_index.json` / `ui_check.py` have no `memory`/`jf-memory` step), so there is NO stale baseline to regenerate. §27.3's baseline half is dropped; only the two live-verification residuals (spine wide-window tick + inbox drawer render) remain — and those are verification gaps, not baseline regens.
- **P4 — §27.4 (i18n labels) — ACTIONABLE, scope named (MED-HIGH).** The registry i18n labels live in `modules/app-api/src/main/resources/messages/registry-{operation,resource,prompt,diagnostic}.en.properties`, served by `MessageCatalogController` as `/api/messages/registry-{primitive}/{locale}`. There is NO `registry-workflow.en.properties` yet. So authoring workflow labels is a NEW properties file + registering the `registry-workflow` namespace in `MessageCatalogController` (mirroring `registry-operation`) — slightly more than "add labels", but well-scoped and low-risk. (Optional polish; the picker's `deriveTitle` fallback works without it.)

**Net.** The de-risk **shrank the batch** (the memory-surface doc + the ui-shot baseline were assumed-work that proved no-ops) and **validated the only high-risk item** (the live-id fix is a safe, localized one-method change — no hidden dedup/reconciliation/test dependency). The remaining batch is: §27.2 zero-pad (1 method + a tie test), §27.1 two additive doc edits + regen, §27.4 optional i18n (new properties + namespace). No probe surfaced a fatal surprise; two assumptions were corrected DOWNWARD (less work). NOT implemented in this pass.

## §28 — §27 implemented + live-verified (2026-06-11): the batch landed, all four browser conditions proven, reviewer PASS

The §27 batch (de-risked in §27.G) was implemented in a worktree off main as Phases A/B/D (the §27.3 live residuals fold into the final batch below as Phase C verification). Commits `8ea3c6118` (§27 A+B), `7c3e1eb7d` (§27.4 D), `<§28 test commit>` (the reviewer-MINOR guard test) on base `6c870beb5`. NOT merged — landed by the user.

**What shipped.**
- **A — live-id ordering symmetry (§27.2).** `AgentSessionController.nextEntryId` now zero-pads (`e-${String(++c).padStart(6,'0')}`), so the `projectLiveAgentActivity` same-ms tiebreaker (`ts || id.localeCompare`) is temporally correct past the 9→10 boundary — the live mirror of the §26.I record-side fix. + a projection tie test (a >9-entry one-timestamp run brackets correctly) AND a production-emitter format guard in `AgentSessionController.test.ts` (the reviewer's MINOR — the format itself is now pinned, not just the consumer's assumption).
- **B — canonical-doc drift (§27.1).** `api-contract-map.md`: `GET /api/registry/workflows` (the picker wire) + the registry-workflow i18n endpoint + the previously-undocumented interaction cluster (`/api/thread`, `/api/presence`, `/api/presence/run` with the §26.D `conversationId`, `/api/memory`). `22-agent-system-architecture.md`: the §26 run-STRUCTURE authority note. Regen ran. `docsApiDriftCheck` green: a pre-existing `/api/agent/hard-stop` false-positive (the `/api/agent/*` ban over-matches a real current route at `LocalApiServer:2011-2012`) surfaced by editing the file; resolved with the gate's sanctioned `drift-allow` markers.
- **D — i18n workflow labels (§27.4).** `registry-workflow.en.properties` (authored label+description for `core.{demo-compose,research-brief}`, keys matching the `CoreWorkflowCatalog` `I18nKey` values exactly) + a `registryWorkflowMessages` `MessageCatalogController` + `GET /api/messages/registry-workflow/{locale}` route (mirroring registry-operation/resource) + a `bootWorkflowCatalog` FE loader wired into the i18n boot. So `present({kind:'workflow', labelKey})` resolves the authored label instead of the `humanizeId` fallback. LocalApiServer +11 LOC → class-size pin 2566→2577 + a `declared-growth` changeset.

**Static gates.** FE typecheck + `test:unit:run` green (incl. the live-id tie test + the production-format guard + the 3 `bootWorkflowCatalog` tests). `./gradlew.bat build -x test` green (all gates incl. class-size re-measured + `docsApiDriftCheck`) + `:modules:ui:test` + `:modules:app-api:test` green.

**Live-browser batch (the hard gate — fresh `installDist`, full §27 jar set staged into the dev dist, dev stack + chat model `Meta-Llama-3.1-8B-Instruct` active, worktree Vite at a 2400px-wide viewport). DOM-probe + screenshots:**
- **(A) long run renders in correct order.** Three sequential `core.research-brief` runs → a 12-item thread. DOM probe: ids in visual (temporal) order = `e-000001,…,e-000009, e-000011, e-000014, …, e-000024` (crosses the 9→10 boundary), and `[...ids].sort()` === the visual order (`lexMonotonic: true`). The pre-fix `e-N` would have inverted (`e-11` < `e-9`). **Confirmed.**
- **(C, spine) node-boundary ticks at a wide viewport.** A >1-node workflow run rendered `.node-boundary` ticks in the `run-spine` — `nodeBoundaryCount: 2` (one per node) at `windowInnerWidth: 2400` (> the 1024px breakpoint the prior automation capped below at 991px). **The §26.H residual is closed.**
- **(C, inbox) retrospective drawer + composer + background run.** `runBackgroundTask(...)` launched; the Activity drawer's **Inbox** tab rendered "Background run — 1 tool, 2 iterations / DONE" plus the "Run a task in the background" composer. **The §26.J residual is closed.**
- **(D) picker authored labels.** The `<select#workflow-picker>` rendered `Compose demo · 4 nodes` / `Research brief · 2 nodes` — the authored i18n labels (DOM probe of `workflowLabel(w)` + the rendered picker), not the `humanizeId` fallback ("Demo Compose"). **Confirmed.**
- A backend nuance the batch caught + fixed: the main-checkout dist's `app-services` jar predated §26.C (`UIWorkflowEmitter` absent), so `/api/registry/workflows` returned 500; staging the full consistent worktree jar set restored HTTP 200. (A staleness artifact of the shared dev dist, not a code defect — the worktree build was correct.)

**Independent review.** A reviewer subagent (≠ implementer) returned **VERDICT: PASS**, zero MAJOR findings. Its one MINOR (no test guarded the *production* `nextEntryId` format, only the projection sort via a local helper) was resolved by the added `AgentSessionController.test.ts` format guard; its NIT (6-digit ceiling at 999,999, per-session in-memory counter) is purely theoretical and left as-is. The key adversarial checks it cleared: the i18n property keys match the `CoreWorkflowCatalog` `I18nKey` values byte-for-byte (no silent fallback), the drift-allow markers are justified (hard-stop is a real route), and the class-size pin matches `wc -l` exactly.

§27 is complete. The §27.5 "deliberately NOT chasing" items (memory-fork ceiling, DAG view, more workflows) stay logged follow-ons.

**§28 follow-up (post-review fix) — the cold-boot catalog clobber.** A critical re-review of the §27
changes surfaced one substantive integration hazard the live batch passed by timing luck: `bootResourceCatalog`
was the lone catalog boot that REPLACED the shared `coreCatalog` (`coreCatalog = body.messages`) while every
sibling — surface/health/operation/**workflow** — MERGES via `Object.assign`, all co-scheduled in one
`i18n.ts` `Promise.all` with no ordering. On a cold boot (first launch / cleared cache), a registry-resource
`200` resolving after the workflow boot would WIPE the just-merged authored labels → the picker falls back to
`humanizeId` ("Demo Compose"), defeating Phase D's deliverable on first encounter (self-healing on reload via
the `304` early-return). Fix: `bootResourceCatalog` now MERGES like its siblings (both the cache-seed and the
`200` path), making the whole catalog family order-independent — the sole replacer is gone. + a deterministic
race regression test (`resourceCatalog.test.ts`) whose teeth were verified (it fails under the old replace
semantics with exactly the clobber symptom). FE typecheck + 2732 tests green. (Live cold-boot re-verify not
re-run — the dev backend was torn down after the §28 batch; unnecessary given the proven-teeth unit guard on
this pure catalog-merge logic.)

## §29 — Post-implementation: what the foundation ENABLES (research-grounded idea ledger, 2026-06-11)

**NOT committed work — ideation.** After the kernel shipped, a frontier scan (LangGraph Studio/LangSmith, Langfuse, Devin, Cursor, Claude Code, Perplexity, NotebookLM, Elicit, scite, n8n, Gumloop, Dify, Manus, ChatGPT Tasks, GitHub Copilot App, LangChain Agent Inbox, …) was mapped against the SHIPPED kernel + verified against the code. Each idea is tagged [POLISH]/[SIMPLIFY]/[EXTEND]/[NEW], named with the authority it extends and an honest lift.

**Meta-finding (the important one): the kernel is already at/ahead of the frontier.** Verified-against-code, 565 already ships the patterns the external research holds up as best practice: TIERED grounding (`GroundingTier` high/medium/low + grounded/weak/ungrounded, minted once, register-gated — NOT a binary badge), inline per-sentence citations + a `CitationHoverCard` hover preview, the watch/assist/auto AUTONOMY DIAL (shipped + surfaced as the agent-mode toggles), tool-call cards with risk metadata, the global HARD-STOP, the run-spine minimap with node-boundary ticks + click-to-jump + viewport indicator, and the retrospective Sessions/Timeline/History/Inbox drawer with background-run JOIN. So these are EXTENSIONS, not catch-up. The leverage test below is therefore "which existing authority does it project through," and the bias is toward LOCAL-FIRST differentiators (things a cloud agent structurally cannot do).

### Tier 1 — STEERING: the next 565-style authority (highest leverage)
> **SUPERSEDED by §30 (2026-06-11) — read §30 instead.** A code investigation corrected this Tier's premise: the gating/Consent authority is NOT "half-applied" — it is mature and already graded (`GateBehavior` AUTO/INLINE/TYPED). The real gap is a *different concept* (DIRECTION, the proactive peer of Consent), and "graded friction" is mostly already built. §30 is the correct design; this paragraph is kept as dated history.

The trust FACTS exist (autonomy level + per-grant trust + per-tool risk metadata + hard-stop), but FRICTION is rendered UNIFORMLY: the autonomy dial decides *whether* to gate, yet the gate itself isn't graded by risk, and the only mid-run control is kill-everything (hard-stop) or a per-tool-call redirect — there is no free-form run-level steer. This is the exact "kernel half-applied to presentation" disease 565 kept curing (§17/§19): one authority's facts present, its rendering forked/flat. The structural move is **ONE Steering authority projected to GRADED control**, so "a destructive action confirmed at the same visual weight as a safe one" and "interrupt = only kill" become unrepresentable.
- **Graded confirmation friction** [EXTEND] — project the gate from the tool's risk + trust tier: low to a silent toast, medium to a "proceeding in 3s · cancel" countdown, high/destructive to the full dialog. *Authority: authorization ceremony + risk metadata (exist); only the graded rendering is new.* The single most-cited HITL pattern (Cursor/Claude-Code/ChatGPT-agent "proportional friction").
- **Action-preview diff for write/delete** [EXTEND/NEW] — before a destructive tool runs, render before→after in its tool card; the confirm is gated on having seen it. *Authority: tool-call card (exists); needs a backend "compute the would-be change" preview.* (Copilot data: full preview-before-apply raises acceptance ~28% AND prevents over-approval.)
- **Free-form mid-run steer** [NEW] — a persistent "redirect…" input in the run frame that injects guidance the agent reads at the NEXT step boundary, without killing. *A per-tool-call redirect status exists; a run-level steer queue does not (backend: agent loop drains a steer queue at boundaries).* Devin/AgentScope's most-valued feature.

### Tier 2 — RUN LEGIBILITY: mostly free polish on shipped authorities
- **Per-segment elapsed time** on segment headers [EXTEND] — node_started/node_completed already carry timestamps; render "2.4s" density-adaptively. *Authority: segments + density (free).*
- **Spine health ticks** [EXTEND] — a second mark layer on the spine for nodes that hit a tool error / retry, so a 20-node run's 2 bad nodes are visible without scrolling; click jumps. *Authority: run-spine geometry + the error signals already in the stream.*
- **Keyboard step-nav (J/K)** across segments [POLISH] — a new input gesture to the existing Navigation authority (it already owns segment positions + the focus path). *Authority: navigation (free).*
- **Completed-run summary card** [EXTEND] — collapse a finished run to {label · duration · step-count · outcome}, expand on click; a new density signal ("run complete to minimal"). *Authority: density.*
- (Token/cost badges need a backend payload field — defer until a cost signal exists.)

### Tier 3 — LOCAL-FIRST EVIDENCE: narrow, but the differentiators live here
Most evidence UX is SHIPPED (tiers, inline + hover citations). What's left is small and uniquely local:
- **Open the actual file at the cited line** [NEW] — grep-clean today: a citation has the local path+line+snippet but no "reveal in OS / jump editor to line." The Tauri shell makes this trivial and it is the one citation affordance NO cloud product can match (their sources are URLs; ours are the user's real files). Highest-delight, lowest-risk local idea.
- **Provenance axis (extracted vs inferred)** [NEW, subtle] — grounding STRENGTH is tiered (cross-encoder score); grounding PROVENANCE (directly-quoted vs reasoned-over vs model-prior) is a DIFFERENT axis not captured. The "what I know vs what I guessed" pattern. Genuinely new but needs a backend signal; lower priority, flagged honestly.
- **Offline-provenance trust chip** [POLISH] — "answered fully offline, grounded only in your files" — a trust signal cloud agents can't offer; cheap.

### Tier 4 — REUSE / AUTHORING: the structural answer to the deferred "more workflows" (§27.5)
Workflows are hand-coded in `CoreWorkflowCatalog` (Java). The non-hand-coded path:
- **Save-run-as-workflow** [NEW] — capture a successful run's linear node/tool sequence as a draft catalog workflow. The run IS the spec, and the linear no-edge stream model fits PERFECTLY — this is "more workflows" without the §25.3 DAG editor (correctly still avoided: no edge data to render). *Needs a run→catalog projection + user-catalog persistence (the catalog becomes user-authorable, a real architectural extension).*
- **Parameterized workflows** [NEW] — typed input slots on a catalog workflow + a small form in the picker, so workflows become reusable tools. *Catalog schema + form.*
- **Inbox kanban** [POLISH] — group the Inbox by Running/Needs-review/Done/Failed (pure reorg of `AgentRunStore` status). *Free at scale.*
- **Background-result to inject into conversation** [EXTEND] — an Inbox action that pulls a finished background run's output into the live chat via the existing JOIN mechanic. *Closes the async→sync loop.*
- (Scheduling/recurring runs + DSL export/import are bigger backend lifts; reasonable but lower priority pre-production.)

### Anti-patterns — do NOT chase (all three research strands + our constraints converge)
- **DAG / graph-canvas editor** — the backend emits a linear index+nodeCount, NO edges; a graph view would fabricate or fake topology. The spine is the correct metaphor for a linear stream (§25.3 stands).
- **Checkpoint time-travel / fork / "re-run from node N"** — needs durable per-node state the forward-only stream doesn't persist; large backend lift, not free.
- **Confidence PERCENTAGES** — research is consistent that binary/tiered beats numeric (analysis-paralysis); we already tier — keep it, don't add "73% grounded."
- **Cloud/multi-user/marketplace/external (email/Slack) notifications** — local-first, single-user, no-users; the Inbox drawer IS the notification surface; share-via-file (DSL), not share-via-cloud.
- **Run comparison/diff** — premature; needs stable cross-run node identity we don't have.
- **External URL "sources panel"** — our sources are local files; the right move is open-file-at-line, not a URL list.
- **Timeout = auto-approve** — a governance failure; a pending gate should persist (the app is paused), hard-stop is the abandon path.

**Recommended order if ever pursued:** Tier 1 (Steering — highest leverage, it's the one place the trust kernel is half-applied) → the Tier-3 open-file-at-line (cheap, uniquely local, high delight) → Tier 2 legibility polish (near-free) → Tier 4 save-run-as-workflow (the structural "more workflows"). None is committed; all are viable; no rush.

## §30 — The correct long-term design: DIRECTION (steering) as the missing peer of CONSENT (design theorization, 2026-06-11)

**Genre: correct structure, not a build plan** (per the 557/559/561/569 convention). General, not implementation-level. This SUPERSEDES the §29 Tier-1 framing ("the trust kernel is half-applied / graded friction"): the code investigation showed that framing was wrong — the gating authority is already excellently unified and already graded. The real gap is a different concept, named below.

### §30.1 The thesis in one move
Human-in-the-loop over an agent run is **two distinct axes**, and the codebase has built only one of them:

- **CONSENT** (reactive) — *the agent proposes; the human authorizes or denies.* This is MATURE and UNIFIED: one chokepoint `IntentGateEvaluator.evaluate(risk, transport) → GateBehavior {AUTO|INLINE_CONFIRM|TYPED_CONFIRM|DENY}` (tempdoc 550 thesis III), read by enforcement + preview + the wire; a (SourceTier × RiskTier) lattice + consent capsules (single-use proof) + durable grants (allow-always) + the one `AuthorizationHost` ceremony + the global hard-stop. The verdict is ALREADY a 4-tier graded behavior. Consent is not the gap.
- **DIRECTION** (proactive) — *the human sets or changes what the agent should DO.* This is FORKED across disconnected mechanisms, **with the continuous case entirely missing**:
  - the **initial prompt** = the t=0 directive,
  - the **autonomy dial / posture** (561's autonomy×grounding×persistence coordinate) = a *standing* directive ("how much leash"),
  - the **hard-stop** = the *terminal* directive ("stop entirely"),
  - **(absent) mid-run interjection** = the *continuous* directive ("actually focus on Q3 / skip that / try the other folder") — there is NO channel to direct a live run, only to consent to (or kill) what it proposes.

These four are one concept — **the human's directional intent over a run's trajectory** — rendered as four unrelated widgets (a text box, a 3-way dial, a kill button) with the middle missing. That is exactly the 565 disease (one concept, forked projections), now at the *control* layer rather than the *render* layer.

**The correct structure: ONE Direction (Steering) authority** — a typed, time-extended CONTROL CHANNEL over a run, a stream of directives `{ initiate, set-posture, interject, halt }` with a uniform lifecycle (`issued → acknowledged-at-next-boundary → effected | superseded`), projected to the run window's control surfaces (composer, dial, a mid-run steer input, stop), so that the prompt box / dial / steer input / stop button become **projections of one directional-intent model, not four independent mechanisms** — and "you can START and KILL a run but cannot NUDGE it" becomes unrepresentable (the continuous directive is a first-class value, not a missing feature).

### §30.2 What already exists — EXTEND, do not replace
The design is mostly a *re-homing* of shipped parts under one concept + filling one gap. Honest inventory:
- **The Consent authority is untouched.** `IntentGateEvaluator`/lattice/capsules/`DurableGrantStore`/`AuthorizationHost`/`GlobalHardStop` stay exactly as they are. Direction does NOT gate; it DIRECTS. (Replacing or duplicating the lattice chokepoint is explicitly forbidden — 550 thesis III, the Preview-vs-Enforcement drift risk.)
- **The autonomy dial is the proto-`set-posture` directive.** 561 already models it as a posture *coordinate* and "collapsed autonomy to one backend issuance authority" (P-D) — i.e. the dial is already a *preference input the gate reads*, not a gate itself. Direction adopts the dial AS-IS as its standing-posture facet; nothing about the dial→gate relationship changes.
- **`AgentSessionController.pushAutonomy` is the embryonic channel.** It already *pushes a posture change mid-run* to the backend (≈L260–278). The Direction authority is the **generalization of `pushAutonomy`** from "push a posture change" to "push ANY directive" over the same live channel — a clear extend-not-invent anchor.
- **The run-STRUCTURE tier (§26) is the injection substrate.** §26's segment/node boundaries (`node_started`/`node_completed`) are precisely the well-defined points at which a directive is read. Direction **composes** the run-structure authority: an interjection lands at the next boundary. (This is why this design is *565's* — it is a presentation+interaction concern of the run window, sitting directly on the run-structure I just shipped.)
- **The hard-stop is the `halt` directive** — the terminal value of the same channel, not a separate subsystem.

### §30.3 The correct structure (conceptual)
1. **One canonical model — `RunControlIntent`**: a per-run, append-only stream of typed directives. Directive kinds: `initiate(prompt)`, `set-posture(autonomy/grounding/...)`, `interject(free-form guidance, optionally targeting a node/segment)`, `halt(scope)`. The standing posture is the last `set-posture`; the initial prompt is the first `initiate`; hard-stop is a `halt`. The continuous nudge is `interject` — the genuinely new value.
2. **Uniform lifecycle**: every directive — prompt, dial-move, nudge, stop — flows the same path (`issued → acknowledged-at-next-boundary → effected | superseded-by-later-directive`), so a mid-run nudge is not a bolted-on special case but the same shape as the initial prompt.
3. **Boundary semantics (composing §26)**: directives are drained by the run at segment/node boundaries (the §26 structure). This gives steering a *predictable* effect point (no mid-token chaos) and a render: a directive shows on the run-spine as a human-origin landmark between segments (it IS a run event).
4. **Clean separation from Consent**: Direction shapes WHAT the agent attempts; Consent governs WHETHER a specific attempt proceeds. They meet at the action: the human directs ("search Q3"), the agent proposes a tool-call, the Consent authority decides the gate. The dial's *effect on gating* stays a projection — Direction owns the dial as a posture value; the Gating authority *reads* that posture as one input (already true post-561-P-D). This dissolves the map's "dual-authority muddiness" by naming which authority OWNS the dial (Direction) vs which CONSUMES it (Consent).
5. **Projection**: the composer, the dial, the (new) mid-run steer input, and the stop button all render from / write to the one `RunControlIntent` channel. No control affordance authors run-direction except through it.

### §30.4 Anti-drift (the 565 register-gate, recursively)
A **steering-surfaces register + gate** (sibling of the navigation/transient/modal registers). **Implementation correction (§32 review):** the gate enforces the **PER-RUN directives that act on the live controller — initiate · interject · halt** — not posture. *(1)* Positive coverage: every adopter composes the one `dispatchRunControl` seam. *(2)* Forbidden reintroduction: each per-run directive's controller call (`.steer(` for interject, `.cancelSession(` for halt) has EXACTLY ONE dispatch site (the seam), so a second mid-run steer input **or a hand-rolled stop button in a view is a build failure** — enforced, with teeth (those calls appear only in the seam). **`set-posture` is deliberately OUT of this seam**: posture is the GLOBAL **561 P-D autonomy store** (`setAutonomyLevel`/`subscribeAutonomy`), a peer channel the run's gate *consumes* — the dial writes it directly; folding a global store into the per-run dispatch would be conflation, not unification. (The first cut overclaimed "every affordance through the seam"; the dial bypassed the dead `set-posture` branch — corrected by scoping the seam to per-run directives + gating `.cancelSession(` too.) A new per-run control affordance is a discovery-step row; the teeth live in the typed seam + the forbidden-call scan, not a grep of intent.

### §30.5 Relationships & honest ledger
- **vs 550 (Consent):** peers, not nested. 550 owns consent; 565's Direction owns direction; the dial is owned by Direction and consumed by Consent. No overlap, no replacement.
- **vs 561 (posture/modes):** Direction is the *generalization* of 561's posture axis from a static coordinate to a live directive stream; modes remain projections of the posture facet.
- **vs 569 (user-authored behavior):** §29-Tier-4 "save-run-as-workflow" / parameterized workflows are **569's** domain (workflows = user-authored statecharts over closed vocabularies). Direction is orthogonal: it steers ANY run (ad-hoc, agent, or a 569-authored workflow). Do not fold workflow-authoring into Direction.
- **EXTENDS:** autonomy dial (→ posture directive), `pushAutonomy` (→ general directive channel), §26 boundaries (→ injection points), hard-stop (→ halt), composer (→ initiate).
- **GENUINELY NEW (the only net-new):** (a) the `RunControlIntent` channel as a named authority; (b) the **continuous `interject` directive** + the backend agent-loop **boundary-drain** that reads pending directives between steps (the one real backend seam — the agent loop must check a directive queue at each node boundary); (c) the steering-surfaces register+gate.
- **§29 reconciliation:** §29-Tier-1's "graded confirmation friction" is largely ALREADY BUILT (the AUTO/INLINE/TYPED gradation); the survivor from Tier-1 is `interject` (free-form mid-run steer) + the **action-preview diff** (which is a *Consent* enrichment — extend `AuthorizationPrompt`/`OperationPreviewController` with a before→after view, an edge-extension of 550, not part of Direction). §29-Tiers 2/3 (legibility polish, open-file-at-line) are unaffected projections of existing authorities.

### §30.6 Scope & non-goals
- This is the **structure**, not a phasing/feasibility plan. The only genuinely-hard piece is the backend boundary-drain for `interject` (the agent loop reading a directive between steps); everything else is re-homing shipped parts under one model.
- NOT in scope / explicitly avoided: turning Direction into a gate (Consent owns that); a free-form *argument-edit* of a proposed tool call (breaks the capsule's single-use args-hash binding — 550 invariant; the right primitive is `interject` "next time use X", not mutate-the-pending-call); per-token interruption (boundary-drained, not mid-token); any cloud/multi-user control surface (local-first, single-user).

**One-line statement of the correct design:** *a run is not fully human-in-the-loop until ONE authority owns the human's direction over it — initiate, posture, interject, halt as values of one control-intent channel drained at the run's own §26 boundaries — sitting as the proactive PEER of the mature reactive Consent authority, so "start and kill but never nudge" is unrepresentable.*

## §31 — De-risk pass for §30 (the Direction authority): every load-bearing assumption verified against code (2026-06-11)

Read-only confidence pass before any §30 implementation (the §10 / §27.G discipline). Six uncertainties probed; **all resolved positively — no architectural surprise surfaced.** Corrections here win over §30 prose (later-wins).

- **R1/R2 (the only "genuinely-hard" piece — mid-run directive delivery) → LOW-RISK EXTENSION.** The agent run is a single blocking thread, addressable by `sessionId` in a `sessions` map, and **already has a per-run `CompletableFuture` mailbox**: `AgentSession.approvalGates` — the loop BLOCKS on `gate.get(timeout)` and an external `POST /api/chat/approve` completes it, **pausing/resuming the same run in place** (`AgentLoopService.tryApproveToolCall`); plus `virtualToolFutures` (`/api/chat/agent/tool-result`) and a `volatile autonomyLevel` re-read at each tool gate. So a per-run **directive queue slots in identically to approval gates**, drained at the post-checkpoint / pre-LLM boundary — NOT new transport/state-machine. Hard-stop is the simpler pull-at-action-time precedent for the `halt` value. §30's central bet (steering is an extension, not net-new plumbing) is **confirmed**.
- **R3 (`pushAutonomy` = embryonic channel) → CONFIRMED.** It POSTs `/api/chat/agent/autonomy` → `setSessionAutonomy` → mutates the `volatile AgentSession.autonomyLevel`, read at the NEXT gate. That is literally the "HTTP mutates a per-run field read at a boundary" shape the `interject`/`set-posture` directives generalize — the extend-not-invent anchor is real.
- **R4 (human-origin directive as a run event) → CONFIRMED extensible.** `RunSegmentRef.originKind` (`'interactive'|'background'|'workflow'`) is a branded union minted at one site (`assignRunSegments`); a steer origin is a one-line union add. Items already carry `originator: 'user'|'agent'`, so the render already distinguishes human from agent events.
- **R5 (steering register+gate) → CONFIRMED template.** 10+ `governance/*.v1.json` catalogs each paired with a `scripts/ci/check-*.mjs`; `steering-surfaces.v1.json` + `check-steering-arbitration.mjs` is a trodden path.
- **R6 (§29 cheap items) → BOTH SEAMS EXIST.** Tauri `invoke('open_file', {path})` is already wired (`platform.ts`) — the §29-Tier-3 open-the-cited-file transport is built (line-jump may need a param). `IntentPreviewer` + `OperationPreviewController` give the action-preview-diff a home in 550's lane.

**Residual (implementation detail, not architecture):** exact drain placement + directive supersede semantics; how `interject` text enters the next iteration's LLM context (the loop rebuilds the prompt per iteration — straightforward); whether `open_file` takes a line arg. None is a surprise.

**Net.** The de-risk found the agent loop is already built on the exact synchronization primitive (`sessions` map + per-run `CompletableFuture` mailbox + volatile boundary-read field) that §30's channel needs, so the design is an extension of a proven pattern rather than new plumbing. Confidence to implement §30 is HIGH. NOT implemented in this pass.

## §32 — §30 + §29 implemented, live-verified, reviewer-PASS (2026-06-11)

The §31-de-risked plan shipped in a worktree off main (NOT merged — the user lands it). Phase 1 (§30 DIRECTION authority), Phase 2 (§29 Tier-2 legibility), Phase 3 (§29 Tier-3/4 features). Commits `7ffccdb72` (§30) · `ed867bda9` (Tier-2) · `bcd02066e` (Tier-3/4) · `a8b0e9c3d`/`5914193e5` (review fixes).

**What shipped.**
- **§30 — the DIRECTION (steering) authority.** The mid-run `interject` channel, built exactly as the §31 de-risk predicted (an extension of the approval-gate mailbox, not new plumbing): `AgentSession.pendingInterject` (AtomicReference, drain-once) → `AgentStepRunner` drains it at the step boundary (after `isCancelled`) and folds the text into the next LLM call as a system steering note (mirroring the handoff append) → a `DirectiveAcknowledged` SSE event (added to the sealed `AgentEvent` + all 9 emit/schema sites) → `POST /api/chat/agent/steer` (mirrors `/autonomy`). FE: `AgentSessionController.steer()` + `onDirectiveAcknowledged`; a live-run steer input; a `steer-directive` projection → a human-origin point item the spine renders as a `.steer-landmark` + the body as a "Your direction" chip. The per-run directives (initiate · interject · halt) route through one `dispatchRunControl` seam; a `steering-surfaces` register + `check-steering-arbitration` gate locks it (positive coverage + a forbidden-`.steer(`/`.cancelSession(` scan). **Posture is a peer channel** (the 561 P-D autonomy store the dial writes), out of the per-run seam by design.

The new `check-steering-arbitration` gate green (wired into ci.yml + CLAUDE.md).

- **§30 (decisive):** a multi-step agent run (`toolGroups: 2`) accepted a mid-run steer; DOM probe — `spineSteerLandmarks: 1`, `bodySteerChips: 1`, and the **final answer = "PINEAPPLE." with `answerHonorsSteer: true`** — the agent ABANDONED its climate-search task mid-run and obeyed the injected directive. **Independent review (condition c).** A reviewer subagent (≠ implementer) first returned **FAIL** on one MAJOR: the steering gate/prose OVERCLAIMED — it asserted "every affordance (incl. set-posture/halt) through the seam / a hand-rolled stop is a build failure", but the gate only banned `.steer(`, and the `AutonomyDial` wrote `setAutonomyLevel` directly (the seam's `set-posture` branch was dead) — the project's own wrong-gate class. **Resolved:** dropped the dead `set-posture` case (the seam unifies the PER-RUN directives; posture is the peer 561 P-D store), and the gate now forbids BOTH `.steer(` (interject) AND `.cancelSession(` (halt) outside the seam — so a hand-rolled stop button in a view is NOW a real build failure (the re-reviewer scratch-tested the teeth). Prose corrected to match. **Honest residuals (noted, not defects).** The steer landmark is live-only — the record path has no `directive_acknowledged` projection, so after a run folds into `/api/thread` the chip/landmark are ephemeral (the directive's *effect* persists; §30.6 scopes record-persistence out). The cited-file OS-open requires the packaged Tauri shell. A standalone background-run's result re-association (vs JOIN-on-launch) needs the prompt/result on `PresenceRun` — a backend follow-on.

§30 + the actionable §29 are complete. The 565 kernel now has its proactive control peer to the reactive Consent authority: a run is fully human-in-the-loop — you can start it, steer it, and stop it through one channel.

## §33 — Four review fixes for §30/§29: each affordance now appears only when it works, gives feedback, is reachable, and labels correctly (2026-06-11)

A critical review of the shipped §30/§29 work found four integration/edge/vocabulary gaps around an otherwise-sound core (the drain mechanism, the gate, and the wire are correct and live-proven — §32). The four fixes close them. Shipped in a worktree off main (NOT merged — the user lands it). Commits `0cb145cda` (the four fixes) · `3875f37c8` (the in-batch critical gate fix) · `da696dfb3` (reviewer-finding test coverage).

**What shipped (the four fixes).**
- **FIX A — the steer input shows ONLY for a steerable agent run.** `AgentSessionController` gained a `runKind: 'agent'|'workflow'|'background'|null` field, set synchronously on `send`→`'agent'`, `runWorkflow`→`'workflow'`, `resumeSession`→`'agent'`, cleared to `null` on every terminal (`onDone`/`onError`/`cancelSession`). `runBackgroundTask` is detached (sets neither `isStreaming` nor `runKind`), so the AND-gate already excludes it. `UnifiedChatView.renderSteerInput` now gates on `affordance==='agent' && agentCtrl.isStreaming && agentCtrl.runKind==='agent'`. A workflow run streams in the agent affordance too but goes through `WorkflowShapeRunner` (no interject drain) + isn't an `AgentLoopService` session, so steering it 404s — the affordance never appears where it can't work.
- **FIX B — a late steer never vanishes silently.** `AgentLoopService.runAgent` now drains any still-pending directive ONCE in its `finally` (before the session is removed) and emits `DirectiveAcknowledged` for it — because the per-iteration drain (`AgentStepRunner`) only runs at iteration STARTS, so a steer queued after the last step boundary (final answer / single-LLM-call run) was silently dropped. Reuses the existing `drainInterject()` (a `getAndSet(null)` atomic — no double-emit) + event. FE complement: `AgentSessionController.steer()` surfaces a one-line `'warn'` system note "Could not steer — the run already finished." on a 404/network failure, so a failed steer is never silent.
- **FIX C — J/K step-nav is reachable for a keyboard user.** The handler moved from the non-focusable `#run-conversation @keydown` (which never fired on a fresh run — nothing inside is focused) to a WINDOW-level keydown listener added in `connectedCallback` / removed in `disconnectedCallback` (via the stable `boundWindowKeydown` field, mirroring the view's existing bound-listener pattern). It acts only when `affordance==='agent'` + `wideViewport`, and descends through nested shadow roots from `document.activeElement` to bail if the truly-focused element is an `INPUT`/`TEXTAREA`/`contentEditable` (so typing `j`/`k` in the composer or steer input never navigates).
- **FIX D — the Inbox kanban uses the REAL lifecycle vocabulary.** `RetrospectivePanel.renderInbox` replaced its ad-hoc `RANK`+title-case (whose keys matched NONE of the real states except `done`) with a typed map over the actual `LifecycleState` names: `READY_FOR_LLM` & `AFTER_TOOL_RESULT` → `{0,'Running'}`; `WAITING_APPROVAL` → `{1,'Needs approval'}`; `DONE` → `{2,'Done'}`; `ERROR` → `{3,'Failed'}`; unknown → `{9, humanized}`. Groups by the mapped bucket (the two `Running` states MERGE), orders by rank, labels the header from the map.

**The critical discovery (found DURING the live batch).** FIX A's gate exposed a pre-existing §30 bug: `renderSteerInput` keyed on the VIEW's own `this.isStreaming` — which tracks the non-agent answer plane and is **FALSE during an agent run** — so the steer input had **never rendered for real users**. The §30 live batch (§32) only injected steers programmatically via `c.steer()`, never through the UI, so it missed this. Corrected to gate on the CONTROLLER's `agentCtrl.isStreaming` (commit `3875f37c8`). Without this, FIX A's whole affordance was dead. This is exactly why the §32 work needed the live-through-the-UI batch that §33 ran.

**Static (condition a).** FE `typecheck` + `test:unit:run` green (**2744**; incl. new tests — `runKind` set/cleared per run type; the steer-success path asserts NO failure note; 4 FIX C window-J/K tests covering direction, the light-DOM input guard, the **nested-shadow-root descent**, and listener-removal-on-disconnect; the Inbox groups `READY_FOR_LLM`+`AFTER_TOOL_RESULT` under one `Running` header and `ERROR` under `Failed` in rank order; the Java `steeringDirective_afterLastBoundary_drainedAtRunEnd` proving the end-of-run drain). `./gradlew.bat build -x test` green — all gates incl. **class-size re-measured (AgentLoopService 1115→1124 + changeset `565-direction-end-of-run-drain.md`)** + `docsApiDriftCheck`. `check-steering-arbitration` green (no new `.steer(`/`.cancelSession(` outside the seam). `:modules:app-agent:test` + `:modules:ui:test` green.

**Live-browser batch (condition b) — fresh dev stack + `Meta-Llama-3.1-8B-Instruct`, worktree Vite. DOM-probe measurements + screenshots surfaced in the transcript:**
- **FIX A:** during a real agent run — `{isStreaming:true, runKind:'agent', steerPresent:true, placeholder:"Redirect the agent…"}` (screenshot: the steer input visible above the composer); during a `runWorkflow` run — `{isStreaming:true, runKind:'workflow', steerPresent:false}`. Present iff steerable.
- **FIX B:** a steer injected during the FINAL-answer stream (`sawFinalAnswer:true`, past the last step boundary) → `steerPostOk:true` → a `steer-directive` chip appeared (count 0→1) with the exact text "Late steer: prioritize the newest items only." + label "Your direction" — provable ONLY via the end-of-run drain. After the run ended, a further `steer()` → `returnedFalse:true` (404) → the "Could not steer — the run already finished." `warn` note appeared (count 0→1).
- **FIX C:** over 51 landmarks, a real `window` `'j'` keydown advanced `nav.activeId` (a0→a1→a2) and `'k'` retreated; with the `.run-steer__input` (`steerInputFocusedTag:'INPUT'`) focused, `window 'j'` did NOT move nav (`guardBlocked:true`); after blur, `window 'j'` moved it again (`navMovedAfterBlur:true`). The keydown was dispatched on `window`, not the div — proving the window-listener path.
- **FIX D:** the shipped `renderInbox` over the full seeded vocabulary rendered headers `["Running · 2", "Needs approval · 1", "Done · 1", "Failed · 1"]` with `data-status` `["running","needs-approval","done","failed"]` in rank order, `anyRawEnum:false` (screenshot: the merged "RUNNING · 2" group). The real single-DONE backend presence rendered "Done · 1".

**Independent review (condition c).** A reviewer subagent (≠ implementer) returned **VERDICT: PASS** — no substantive correctness/completeness defects, no anti-patterns (the pre-existing `catch {}` in `steer()` was made *less* silent, not broadened), class-size changeset honest (`wc -l` = 1124 = the pin). Its two non-blocking findings were both test-coverage: (1) FIX C shipped no test (the nested-shadow-root descent — the error-prone part — uncovered); (2) the steer-success path didn't assert *absence* of a failure note. Per "never descope," both were RESOLVED by adding the tests above (commit `da696dfb3`), not waved off. A second independent reviewer (≠ implementer) confirmed **VERDICT: RESOLVED, REMAINING ISSUES: none** — verifying the FIX C tests are precise and revert-catching (the assertions dispatch on `window` so a div-bound listener would fail them; the descent test's top-level `activeElement` is a non-input HOST so removing the descent loop would let `jumpTo` fire) and the success-path assertion is sound. Net: PASS with zero unresolved findings.

**Honest residual (logged, not a defect).** The Inbox per-run CARD badges still show the raw underscored `LifecycleState` (e.g. `READY_FOR_LLM`) — FIX D humanizes the group HEADER vocabulary (its defined scope); the per-run badge is a separate pre-existing element. Logged to `docs/observations.md` for a follow-on.

The four fixes complete the §30/§29 hardening: each control affordance now appears only when it can act, confirms when it does, is reachable by keyboard, and speaks the real lifecycle vocabulary.

## §34 — Landing + a §30 correction: "halt" is unwired, so "stop it through one channel" was overclaimed (2026-06-11)

**Landed.** §29 (Tier-2/3/4) + §30 (DIRECTION authority) + §33 (the four review fixes) merged into `main` and pushed to `origin`. The merge-forward over `main` (which had advanced via 574 §23.B/§25, 575 §17, 576, 560) auto-merged cleanly except for one real content conflict — `RetrospectivePanel.ts`, where 574 §23.B's `jf-status-badge` atom + `TransientController` met §33's Fix-D inbox grouping. Resolved as a union (my grouping + main's atom), which *also* closed Fix D's per-run atom-fork residual (the badge now composes `jf-status-badge`, not a raw `.badge` span). FE typecheck + 2767 unit + all 12 presentation gates (incl. the 574 ratchets my branch predated: atom-fork / style-literal / ambient-purity / transient-arbitration) + `build -x test` + app-agent/ui tests verified green on the merged tree before landing.

**Correction (dated-history discipline).** §30.3 framed the DIRECTION channel as `{initiate · interject · halt}` and §32 concluded "a run is fully human-in-the-loop — you can start it, steer it, and **stop it** through one channel." Verified against source post-landing, the **stop** leg does not hold:
- `halt` (the directive whose seam case is `ctrl.cancelSession()`) has **ZERO live dispatchers** — only a doc-comment mentions `dispatchRunControl({kind:'halt'})`. So the only path to a real backend cancel is dead.
- `cancelSession()` — the lone full cancel (`this.abortController?.abort()` **+ `DELETE /api/chat/sessions/{id}`**, the real backend stop) — is therefore never reached live.
- The **actual** live stop affordance is the composer's `@composer-cancel → this.abortController?.abort()`, where `this` is the **VIEW** (`UnifiedChatView`), whose `AbortController` is a *different* instance than the agent controller's, and which sends **no backend DELETE**. So clicking stop during an agent run may abort the wrong (idle) stream and leave `AgentLoopService` iterating — a possible token/compute leak (open for a live check).

So `initiate` and `interject` are live + proven (§32/§33); `halt` is **forward-looking, not wired**. The §32 "stop it through one channel" claim is corrected to: *two of the three legs are live; halt is designed but undispatched, and the present composer "stop" is an FE-only stream teardown, not a true run halt.* (The §30 prose comments themselves were already made accurate in `5914193e5`; this corrects the higher-level completeness claim.) The §30 follow-on is to wire a real "stop the agent" control through `dispatchRunControl({kind:'halt'})` → `cancelSession`, then live-verify the backend actually halts. Logged to `docs/observations.md` with exact locations.

**Closure status.** 565 is shipped + landed + pushed. The one honor-system item still owed is an independent, *measured* (axe/contrast) whole-screen UX audit of the §30/§33 surfaces by an auditor ≠ committer (563 retired the gate, so it is expected practice, not build-enforced).
